Salah — Prayer
intermediate
6 min
Ranking of Best Sunnah Prayers After Fajr
Intra-Hanafi dispute on ranking rawatib prayers

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ranking of rawatib prayers after Fajr sunnah and explain the evidence for the preferred view.

Core Idea
The four rak'ahs before Zuhr are the most emphasized rawatib because the Prophet threatened loss of intercession for abandoning them.

The rawatib prayers (emphasized sunnahs) are not all equal in virtue. Hanafi scholars have differed on which is most excellent after the Fajr sunnah. This passage from Hashiya al-Tahtawi presents the main opinions and the tarjih (preferred view) based on hadith evidence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue
The text discusses which rawatib prayer is the most virtuous after the Fajr sunnah. Note that this is a dispute within the Hanafi school itself.
2
Note the different opinions
Al-Halwani ranked Maghrib sunnah first, then Zuhr after, then Isha after, then Zuhr before, etc. Another view equated several rawatib. The preferred view is that the four rak'ahs before Zuhr are the most emphasized.
3
Examine the evidence
Al-Halwani relied on the fact that Maghrib sunnah was never abandoned by the Prophet. The preferred view relies on the hadith: 'Whoever leaves the four before Zuhr will not attain my intercession.'
4
Determine the tarjih
The text endorses al-Hasan's view that the pre-Zuhr sunnah is the most correct (al-ashah). It also notes that Imam Muhammad beginning with it in al-Mabsut is not a proof of superiority.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم اختلف في الأفضل بعد ركعتي سنة الفجر قال :الحلواني ركعتا المغرب، ثم التي بعد الظهر ثم التي بعد العشاء ثم التي قبل الظهر ثم التي قبل العصر ثم التي قبل العشاء، وقيل التي بعد العشاء والتي قبل الظهر وبعده وبعد المغرب كلها سواء وقيل التي قبل الظهر أكد قال الحسن وهو الأصح وقد ابتدأ في المبسوط بها . قوله : (ثم اختلف في (الأفضل أي من المؤكدات والمستحبات . قوله: (قال الحلواني ركعتا المغرب) فإنه لم يدعهما سفراً، ولا حضراً كذا في الشرح قوله : (ثم التي بعد الظهر لأنها سنة متفق عليها بخلاف التي قبلها لأنه قيل أنها للفصل بين الأذان والإقامة كذا في الشرح. قوله : (وهو الأصح) كذا صححه في الدراية، والعناية والنهاية وعلله في البحر بأنه ورد فيها، وعيد هو قوله صلى الله عليه وسلم : من ترك الأربع التي قبل الظهر لم تنله شفاعتي وكذا ذكر تصححه العلامة نوح قوله : (وقد ابتدأ) أي الإمام محمد في المبسوط بها، وهو لا يدل على أفضليتها لأنّ الظهر أول صلاة في الوجود.
Then they differed regarding the best (sunnah) after the two rak'ahs of Fajr sunnah. Al-Halwani said: The two rak'ahs of Maghrib, then those after Zuhr, then those after Isha, then those before Zuhr, then those before Asr, then those before Isha. And it is said: those after Isha, those before Zuhr, after it, and after Maghrib are all equal. And it is said: those before Zuhr are the most emphasized. Al-Hasan said: that is the most correct, and he began with it in al-Mabsut. His statement: (then they differed regarding the best) i.e., among the emphasized and recommended. His statement: (Al-Halwani said the two rak'ahs of Maghrib) because he never left them in travel nor at home, as in the commentary. His statement: (then those after Zuhr) because it is a sunnah agreed upon, unlike those before it because it is said they are for separating the adhan and iqama, as in the commentary. His statement: (that is the most correct) as was corrected in al-Diraya, al-Inaya, and al-Nihaya. Al-Bahr gave the reason that a threat came concerning them, and that is the hadith: Whoever leaves the four before Zuhr will not attain my intercession. And similarly, the correctness was mentioned by Allama Nuh. His statement: (and he began) i.e., Imam Muhammad began with it in al-Mabsut, and that does not indicate its superiority because Zuhr was the first prayer to exist.
Source pages p. 388

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute on ranking the best rawatib prayers after the Fajr sunnah. The base text states the disagreement. Al-Halwani's ranking places Maghrib sunnah first because it was never abandoned by the Prophet, then Zuhr after sunnah, then Isha after, then Zuhr before, then Asr before, then Isha before. Another view equates several. The preferred view is that the sunnah before Zuhr (four rak'ahs) is the most emphasized, based on the hadith threatening deprivation of intercession for abandoning it. The commentary clarifies that Imam Muhammad beginning with it in al-Mabsut does not prove superiority, as Zuhr was the first prescribed prayer. The ranking is based on evidence and practice.

Key Terms
الأفضل (al-afdal): The most virtuous or excellent among the sunnah prayers.
المؤكدات (al-mu'akkadat): The emphasized sunnah prayers (rawatib mu'akkadah).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the most correct Hanafi view, which sunnah prayer is the most virtuous after the Fajr sunnah?
A) The two rak'ahs after Maghrib
B) The four rak'ahs before Zuhr
C) The two rak'ahs after Zuhr
D) All are equal

Key Takeaway
The four rak'ahs before Zuhr are the most emphasized rawatib due to the hadith on intercession.

Salah — Prayer

Rulings on Specific Sunnah Prayers and the Four-Rak'ah Sunnah (Rubai'yyat)
Ruling statement with critical refinement on the performance of four-rak'ah sunnah prayers and intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on Jumu'ah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the number and timing of sunnah rak'ahs for Zuhr, Maghrib, Isha, and Jumu'ah, and explain the Hanafi rule that the four-rak'ah sunnah (rubai'yyat) must be prayed with a single salutation, including the intra-Hanafi difference on Jumu'ah.

Core Idea
The four-rak'ah sunnah prayers must be offered with a single salutation – separation invalidates them in the Hanafi school.

The rawatib prayers are well-known, but there are specific details about their performance that a Hanafi must know. This lesson clarifies the number of rak'ahs for the sunnah before and after the main prayers, the recommended recitations, and a critical ruling: the four-rak'ah sunnah (rubai'yyat) must be prayed with one salutation. We will also examine a difference of opinion within the Hanafi school regarding Jumu'ah. Understanding these nuances ensures your sunnah prayers are valid and complete according to the school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the sunnah prayers mentioned
List the specific sunnah prayers covered: the four before Zuhr, two after Maghrib, two after Isha, four before Jumu'ah, and four after Jumu'ah (including an opinion for six after Jumu'ah).
Also note the optional addition of two rak'ahs after the two sunnah of Zuhr.
2
Recognize the rule for the four-rak'ah sunnah (rubai'yyat)
Understand that the four before Zuhr, before Jumu'ah, and after Jumu'ah must be performed with a single salutation (taslima) at the end, not separating after two rak'ahs. This is based on the Prophet's practice and confirmed by al-Zayla'i.
Al-Zayla'i states that praying them with two salutations invalidates them.
3
Understand the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on Jumu'ah
Note that Abu Yusuf and, according to some narrations, Muhammad al-Shaybani hold that one should pray four before Jumu'ah and six after (four then two). Abu Hanifa's position is four before and four after, which is the mufta bihi.
The dispute is only on the number after Jumu'ah.
4
Consider the recitations and virtues
The passage recommends specific surahs for the sunnah after Maghrib (e.g., Surah Sajdah and Mulk) and mentions a hadith promising forgiveness for two rak'ahs after Maghrib recited with specific surahs.
Also note the hadith about twelve rak'ahs leading to a house in Paradise.
5
Analyze the principle about actions contradicting the tahrima and vowing nafl
The passage ends with a general rule: actions that contradict the tahrima (the opening takbir) do not invalidate the prayer but reduce its reward. It also mentions that vowing supererogatory prayers increases reward.
This is a secondary point, but useful for understanding the boundaries of validity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (ويندب أن يضم إليهم ركعتين) وهو مخير إن شاء جعلها بسلام واحد، وإن شاء جعلها بسلامين، والأولى فتضير أربعاً (و) منها ركعتان (بعد المغرب) ويستحب أن يطيل القراءة في سنة المغرب لأنه كان يقرأ في الأولى منهما ألم تنزيل وفي الثانية تبارك الذي بيده الملك كذا في الجوهرة، وعن أنس قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم: (من صلى بعد المغرب ركعتين قبل أن ينطق مع أحد يقرأ في الأولى بالحمد وقل يا أيها الكافرون وفي الركعة الثانية بالحمد وقل أحد خرج من ذنوبه كما تخرج الحية من سلخها (و) منها ركعتان (بعد العشاء وأربع قبل الظهر) لقوله : من ترك الأربع قبل الظهر لم تنله شفاعتي كذا في الاختيار، وقال في البرهان : كان يصلي قبل الظهر أربعاً إذا زالت الشمس فسأله أبو أيوب الأنصاري عن ذلك فقال : إن أبواب السماء تفتح في هذه الساعة فأحب أن يصعد لي في تلك الساعة خير قلت : أفي كلهن قراءة قال نعم قلت أيفصل بينهن بسلام قال: لا، وقوله : «ما من عبد مسلم يصلي في كل يوم ثنتي عشرة ركعة تطوعاً من غير الفريضة إلا بنى الله له بيتاً في الجنة» رواه مسلم زاد الترمذي والنسائي أربعاً قبل الظهر، وركعتين بعدها وركعتين بعد المغرب وركعتين بعد العشاء وركعتين قبل صلاة الغداة (و) منها أربع (قبل الجمعة) لأن النبي كان يركع قبل الجمعة أربعاً لا يفصل في شيء منهن (و) منها أربع (بعدها) لأنّ النبي كان يصلي بعد الجمعة أربع ركعات يسلم في آخرهن فلذا قيدنا به في الرباعيات فقلنا (بتسليمة) لتعلقه بقوله وأربع وقال الزيلعي : حتى لو صلاها بتسليمتين لا يعتد بها. قوله: (فلذا قيدنا) أي لقوله : لا يفصل في شيء منهن، وقوله يسلم في آخرهن. قوله : (لتعلقه الأولى حذفه لفهمه من قوله في الرباعيات، وقال أبو يوسف يصلي أربعاً قبل الجمعة وستاً بعدها، وفي الكرخي محمد مع أبي يوسف، وفي المنظومة مع الإمام، ثم عند أبي يوسف يصلي أربعاً، ثم اثنتين كذا في الحدادي، ولو أخر السنة لا تكون سنة على الصحيح، والكلام بين السنة والفرض وكل عمل ينافي التحريمة لا يسقطها، ولكن ينقص ثوابها على الأصح ، وفي الحلبي لو أراد أن يصلي النوافل ينذرها، ثم يصليها كما هي، ثم نقل عن شرف الأئمة أن أداء النقل بعد النذر أفضل من أدائه دون النذر .
His statement: (and it is recommended to add two rak'ahs to them) and he has the choice: if he wishes, he can make them with one salutation, or with two salutations. The preferable is to make them four. (And) from them are two rak'ahs (after Maghrib). It is recommended to prolong the recitation in the sunnah of Maghrib because he used to recite in the first of them 'Alif Lam Mim Tanzil' and in the second 'Tabarak alladhi bi yadihi al-mulk' as in al-Jawhara. And from Anas: The Prophet said: 'Whoever prays after Maghrib two rak'ahs before speaking to anyone, reciting in the first al-Hamd and Qul ya ayyuha al-kafirun, and in the second rak'ah al-Hamd and Qul Huwa Allahu Ahad, he will come out of his sins as the snake comes out of its skin.' (And) from them are two rak'ahs (after Isha and four before Zuhr) because of his saying: 'Whoever leaves the four before Zuhr will not attain my intercession' as in al-Ikhtiyar. And in al-Burhan: He used to pray four before Zuhr when the sun passed the meridian. Abu Ayyub al-Ansari asked him about that, and he said: 'The doors of heaven are opened at this hour, so I love that good deeds should ascend for me in that hour.' He said: 'Should there be recitation in all of them?' He said: 'Yes.' He said: 'Should I separate them with salutation?' He said: 'No.' And his saying: 'There is no Muslim slave who prays twelve rak'ahs of supererogatory prayer every day besides the obligatory except that Allah builds for him a house in Paradise.' Muslim reported it, and al-Tirmidhi and al-Nasa'i added: four before Zuhr, two after it, two after Maghrib, two after Isha, and two before the dawn prayer. (And) from them are four (before Jumu'ah) because the Prophet used to bow before Jumu'ah four rak'ahs without separating any of them. (And) from them are four (after it) because the Prophet used to pray after Jumu'ah four rak'ahs, making the salutation at the end of them. Therefore we restricted them in the quadripartite prayers and said: (with one salutation) due to its connection with his statement 'and four'. Al-Zayla'i said: even if he prays them with two salutations, they are not counted. His statement: (Therefore we restricted) i.e., because of his statement: he did not separate any of them, and his statement: he made the salutation at the end of them. His statement: (due to its connection) the first was omitted because it is understood from his statement in the quadripartite. Abu Yusuf said: one prays four before Jumu'ah and six after it. In al-Karkhi, Muhammad agrees with Abu Yusuf. In al-Manzuma, with the Imam. Then according to Abu Yusuf, he prays four then two as in al-Hadadi. If one delays the sunnah, it is not a sunnah on the correct view. The speech between the sunnah and the obligatory: any action that contradicts the tahrima does not invalidate it, but reduces its reward according to the correct view. In al-Halabi: if one wants to pray supererogatory prayers, he should vow them, then pray them as they are. Then it is reported from Sharf al-A'imma that performing nafl after a vow is better than performing it without a vow.
Source pages p. 388

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement detailing specific sunnah prayers for various times. It covers: - After Zuhr: It is recommended to add two rakahs to the two sunnah, making four. One may pray them with one or two salutations. - After Maghrib: Two rak'ahs, with recommended recitation of Surah al-Sajdah and al-Mulk, or alternative surahs as per hadith promise forgiveness. - After Isha: Two rak'ahs. - Four before Zuhr: Emphasized with a hadith about intercession. The Prophet prayed them without separation. - Before Jumu'ah: Four rak'ahs without separation. - After Jumu'ah: Four rak'ahs with one salutation. Al-Zayla'i says two salutations invalidate them. There is also a narration about vowing nafl prayers to increase reward. The passage includes opinions from Abu Yusuf and others on the number for Jumu'ah.

Key Terms
الرباعيات (al-ruba'iyyat): The sunnah prayers consisting of four rak'ahs, such as the four before Zuhr and four before/after Jumu'ah.
بتسليمة (bi taslima): With a single salutation at the end of four rak'ahs, i.e., not separating with tashahhud after two.
التحريمة (al-tahrima): The opening takbir (Allahu Akbar) that initiates the prayer, making certain actions forbidden (haram) during prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, how should the four sunnah rak'ahs before Jumu'ah be performed?
A) With two separate salutations (after the second and fourth rak'ah)
B) With one salutation at the end of the fourth rak'ah
C) With a salutation after the first two rak'ahs and then continue with two more without salutation
D) Any way is acceptable

Key Takeaway
The four-rak'ah sunnah prayers (rubai'yyat) must be prayed with a single salutation in the Hanafi school, and the mufta bihi for Jumu'ah is four before and four after, despite an ikhtilaf from Abu Yusuf and Muhammad.

Salah — Prayer
beginner
6 min
First Sitting in Emphasized Sunnah Prayers
Ruling on the first sitting of emphasized sunnahs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the recitation prescribed in the first sitting of a four-rak'ah mu'akkadah sunnah prayer and explain why the Hanafi school restricts it to tashahhud only.

Core Idea
In the first sitting of an emphasized sunnah, only the tashahhud is recited, as it resembles obligatory prayers in its fixed structure.

The emphasized sunnah prayers (sunan mu'akkadah) share certain rules with obligatory prayers due to their strong recommendation. One such rule is the restriction of the first sitting to the tashahhud, omitting the blessings on the Prophet until the final sitting. This lesson examines the ruling and its rationale, as derived from the commentary of al-Tahtawi on Maraqi al-Falah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its context
Recognize that the ruling applies to the first sitting (al-julus al-awwal) in a four-rak'ah emphasized sunnah prayer (e.g., before Zuhr, after Zuhr, before Jumu'ah).
The prayer is supererogatory but emphasized, so it is not obligatory but carries weight.
2
State the ruling
The ruling is that in the first sitting, one recites only the tashahhud and stops at the shahada ('Ashhadu anna Muhammadan 'abduhu wa rasuluhu'). No blessings (salawat) are added. Also, when standing for the third rak'ah, one does not recite the opening supplication (du'a al-istiftah).
3
Identify the dalil (proof)
The proof cited in the text is that these sunnahs, due to their emphasis, resemble obligatory prayers (ashbahat al-fara'id). The resemblance provides a basis for applying some rules of fard prayers, such as restricting the first sitting to tashahhud.
No specific Quran or hadith is quoted; the argument is based on qiyas (analogy) using the illa of emphasis.
4
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Since fard prayers have a fixed first sitting with only tashahhud, the emphasized sunnahs, being similar in emphasis, are analogized to them. Therefore, the same restriction applies.
This is a form of qiyas: the emphasis (ta'akkud) is the effective cause (illa).
5
Note the ikhtilaf and the mufta bihi
The Shafi'i school recommends sending blessings in every sitting. The Hanafi school restricts it to the final sitting. The mufta bihi is the Hanafi view, as supported by Fath al-Qadir and Sharh al-Munya.
There is also an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on whether adding salawat requires sujud al-sahw.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(ويقتصر) المتنفل (في الجلوس الأول من السنة (الرباعية المؤكدة) وهي التي قبل الظهر والجمعة وبعدها (على) قراءة (التشهد فيقف على قوله : وأشهد أن محمداً عبده ورسوله وإذا تشهد في الآخر يصلي على النبي (و) إذا قام للشفع الثاني من الرباعية المؤكدة (لا يأتي في) ابتداء الثالثة بدعاء الاستفتاح كما في فتح القدير وهو الأصح كما في شرح المنية لأنها لتأكدها أشبهت الفرائض فلا تبطل شفعته ولا خيار المخيرة ولا يلزمه كمال المهر بالانتقال إلى الجنان، وقد يقال: إن المدخر في عليين أكثر مما ادخر في غيرها من باقي الجنان. قوله : (وهو خير له من قيام نصف ليلة قد يقال : إنه نزل منزلة من أدرك ليلة القدر، وهي خير من ألف شهر، ولا شك أن قيام نصف ليلة أقل من ذلك، ويمكن أن يجاب بأنه يكتب له قيام نصف ليلة زيادة على ثواب مدرك ليلة القدر أو أنّ المشبه لا يعطي حكم المشبه به من كل وجه. قوله : (غفر له بها ذنوب خمسين سنة) حمله أكثر العلماء على الصغائر، وأطلق بعضهم فعممه للكبائر. قوله : (ولم يقيد فيه بكونها قبل التكلّم فأما أن يحمل المطلق على المقيد لاتحاد الحادثة، أو يقال : إنّ التقييد للكمال لا لتحصيل أصل الموعود به. قوله: (وفي التجنيس الخ) الظاهر أن هذا تفريع على قولهما، وما بعده تفريح على قول الإمام من اختلافهم فيما هو الأفضل من صلاة الليل وذكر في شرح المشكاة أن الأولى فصل المندوبة عن المؤكدة بالتسليم. قوله: (وفي الدرر بتسليمة) وهو أدوم وأشق ولذا اختاره الكمال در قوله: (وقيل بها لظاهر الأحاديث، واختاره المحقق في الفتح، واستظهره الحلبي. قوله: (فيقف على قوله، وأشهد أن محمداً عبده ورسوله واختلف في وجوب سجدتي السهو على من زاد على التشهد فيها كما في الدرر، والغرر كذا في الشرح قوله : ( فلا تبطل شفعته) فهو على شفعته إذا طلب الأخذ بالشفعة على فور خروجه من الصلاة ذكره السيد قوله : (ولا يلزمه كمال المهر) ما لم توجد الخلوة الصحيحة الخالية عن الموانع بعد سلامه من تلك الصلاة قاله السيد. قوله :
And the person praying supererogatory prayers is restricted in the first sitting of the sunnah (the emphasized four-rak'ah sunnahs, which are those before Zuhr and Jumu'ah and after Zuhr) to reciting the tashahhud, stopping at his statement: 'And I bear witness that Muhammad is His servant and Messenger.' And when he recites tashahhud in the last sitting, he sends blessings on the Prophet. And when he stands for the second pair of the emphasized four-rak'ah sunnah, he does not recite the opening supplication at the beginning of the third rak'ah, as in Fath al-Qadir, and it is the soundest view as in Sharh al-Munya, because due to their emphasis they resemble obligatory prayers. So it does not invalidate his pre-emption right, nor does it give the woman with a choice the option, nor does it necessitate the full dower by moving to the Gardens. And it may be said: The reward stored in Illiyin is greater than that stored in the rest of Paradise. His statement: 'It is better for him than half a night of standing'—it may be said that he has been placed in the position of one who attained Laylat al-Qadr, which is better than a thousand months, and there is no doubt that half a night of standing is less than that. It can be answered that he is recorded as having stood half a night in addition to the reward of one who attained Laylat al-Qadr, or that the simile does not give the compared thing the ruling of the compared thing in every respect. His statement: 'Forgiven for him sins of fifty years'—most scholars interpreted it as minor sins, and some generalized it to major sins. His statement: 'And it is not restricted to its being before speaking'—so either the absolute is carried upon the restricted due to the unity of the incident, or it is said that the restriction is for perfection, not for obtaining the basic promise. His statement: 'And in al-Tajnis, etc.'—apparently this is a branch of their statement, and what follows is a branch of the Imam's statement from their difference of opinion regarding what is best regarding night prayer. It is mentioned in Sharh al-Mishkat that the better is to separate the mandub from the mu'akkad by making taslim. His statement: 'And in al-Durar, with one taslim'—it is more continuous and more difficult, therefore al-Kamal chose it. His statement: 'And it is said due to the apparent meaning of the hadith, and al-Muhaqqiq chose it in al-Fath, and al-Halabi considered it preferable.' His statement: 'He stops at his statement: And I bear witness that Muhammad is His servant and Messenger'—and there is disagreement on the obligation of the prostration of forgetfulness for one who adds to the tashahhud in it, as in al-Durar and al-Ghurar, so in the commentary. His statement: 'It does not invalidate his pre-emption right'—so he retains his right of pre-emption if he demands to take it immediately upon leaving the prayer, mentioned by al-Sayyid. His statement: 'And he is not obliged to pay the full dower'—unless a valid privacy free of impediments has occurred after his completion of that prayer, said by al-Sayyid. His statement:
Source pages p. 391

Commentary
This passage deals with the rulings of the first sitting in the emphasized (mu'akkadah) sunnah prayers of four rak'ahs (such as before Zuhr, after Zuhr, and before Jumu'ah). The ruling is that in the first sitting, one only recites the tashahhud up to 'Ashhadu anna Muhammadan 'abduhu wa rasuluhu', and does not send blessings upon the Prophet (which is reserved for the final sitting). Additionally, when standing for the third rak'ah, one does not recite the opening supplication (du'a al-istiftah). The reason given is that these sunnahs, due to their emphasis, resemble obligatory prayers. The hashish comments discuss various related issues: the meaning of the reward promises in previous hadith, whether the forgiveness is for minor or major sins, the number of taslims for the six after Maghrib, and the effect of this prayer on pre-emption rights and dower obligations—such actions do not invalidate pre-emption or impose full dower because the prayer is not a contractual act.

Key Terms
الجلوس الأول (al-julus al-awwal): The first sitting in a four-rak'ah prayer after the second rak'ah, before standing for the third.
التحيات (al-tahiyyat): The tashahhud recitation in the sitting position; here specified to stop at the shahada.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Recite only tashahhud up to the shahada
C) Recite only salawat without tashahhud
D) Sit briefly in silence

Key Takeaway
The first sitting of an emphasized sunnah prayer is restricted to tashahhud only; salawat and istiftah are avoided, following the Hanafi reliance on the analogy to obligatory prayers.

Six Rak'ahs After Maghrib: Virtue and Number of Taslims
Discussion of virtue and number of taslims for six rak'ahs after Maghrib

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the virtue of the six rak'ahs after Maghrib as reported in Hanafi sources, and identify the different opinions within the Hanafi school regarding the number of taslims.

Core Idea
Six rak'ahs after Maghrib are mandubah (recommended), not mu'akkadah, and may be performed with one, two, or three taslims according to varying Hanafi reports.

In this passage, the Hashiya discusses the merit of praying six rak'ahs after Maghrib, citing two hadiths that promise immense forgiveness. The author also notes an intra-Hanafi difference on how many taslims to make when performing these six rak'ahs. Understanding this distinction helps clarify the recommended (mandubah) category in Hanafi fiqh and its practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is praying six rak'ahs after Maghrib. The text states they are mandubah (recommended), not mu'akkadah (emphasized).
2
Locate the dalil
Two hadiths are cited: from Ibn Umar (with restriction to before speaking) and from Ammar ibn Yasir (without restriction). Both promise forgiveness.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The explicit mention of reward indicates desirability (istihbab). The variation in wording shows flexibility in timing.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
There is disagreement on the number of taslims: al-Tajnis says three, al-Qunawi says two, and al-Durar says one taslim.
5
Determine the practical consequence
The worshipper may choose any of these methods; the virtue is not affected by the number of taslims.

Commentary
This passage from the hashia discusses the virtue and ruling of the six rak'ahs after Maghrib. The author cites two hadiths: one from Ibn Umar promising forgiveness of sixty years of sins, and one from Ammar ibn Yasir promising forgiveness even for abundant sins. The hadith from Ibn Umar restricts the reward to praying before speaking, while the other does not. The author notes the difference in opinion regarding the number of taslims: al-Tajnis says three taslims, al-Qunawi says two, and al-Durar says one. The author then clarifies that these six rak'ahs are mandubah (recommended) and distinct from the two-rak'ah emphasized sunnah after Maghrib, as the text groups them with other mandubat. The passage also mentions a hadith about four rak'ahs before and after Zuhr being praiseworthy, but the main focus is on Maghrib.

Key Terms
مؤكدة (mu'akkadah): Emphasized sunnah prayers that the Prophet regularly performed and recommended strongly.
مندوبة (mandubah): Recommended but not emphasized acts of worship.
تسليمة (taslimah): One salutation (saying 'Assalamu alaykum' twice) that ends a prayer or a unit of prayer.

First Sitting in Emphasized Sunnah Prayers
Ruling on first sitting in emphasized sunnah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the correct recitation in the first sitting of the emphasized sunnah and explain why the opening supplication is omitted in the third rak'ah.

Core Idea
In emphasized sunnah, the first sitting stops at the shahadah, and istiftah is omitted in the third rak'ah because of its resemblance to fard.

The sunnah mu'akkada four-rak'ah prayers (before/after Zuhr and Jumu'ah) have a specific rule for the first sitting: you only recite the tashahhud up to the shahadah. Additionally, when standing for the third rak'ah, you do not recite the opening supplication (istiftah). This lesson explains the ruling and its rationale based on Hanafi fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the prayer and the ruling
Recognize that the prayer is a four-rak'ah emphasized sunnah (sunnah mu'akkada) performed before or after Zuhr and Jumu'ah. The ruling is that in the first sitting, one recites only the tashahhud and stops at the shahadah ('wa ashhadu anna Muhammadan 'abduhu wa rasuluh').
The last sitting includes the full tashahhud and blessings on the Prophet.
2
Note the omission of istiftah
When standing for the second pair (i.e., the third rak'ah), one does not recite the opening supplication (istiftah). This is the correct view according to Fath al-Qadir and Sharh al-Munyah.
In regular nafl prayers, istiftah is recited at the beginning of each cycle, but here it is omitted.
3
Understand the rationale
The reason given in the text is that the emphasized sunnah is so strong in recommendation that it resembles the obligatory prayers (fard). In fard, istiftah is only recited once at the beginning and not repeated later. Therefore, this sunnah follows the same pattern.
This is a talil (legal reasoning) based on qiyas.
4
Recognize the consequences
Because of the prayer's resemblance to fard, certain other rulings apply: the right of pre-emption (shuf'a) is not invalidated, the option of the woman in marriage (khiyar) remains, and the full mahr is not obligated upon moving to the gardens (a metaphorical expression for reward).
These consequences are mentioned in the text but are not the primary focus.

Commentary
This extensive passage from the hashia covers the ruling on the first sitting in emphasized sunnah prayers. The author states that in the first sitting of a four-rak'ah emphasized sunnah (before and after Zuhr and Jumu'ah), one only recites the tashahhud up to 'And I bear witness that Muhammad is His servant and Messenger.' Key Terms
تشهد (tashahhud): The testimony recited in the sitting of prayer: 'At-tahiyyat lillah...' up to 'wa ashhadu anna Muhammadan abduhu wa rasuluh.'
استفتاح (istiftah): The opening supplication (like 'Subhanakallahumma...') recited at the beginning of the first rak'ah.
سنة مؤكدة (sunnah mu'akkadah): An emphasized sunnah prayer that the Prophet regularly performed and recommended strongly, similar to fard in significance.

advanced
8 min
Praying More Than Two Rak'ahs of Nafl Without Sitting
Ruling on praying nafl in sets of more than two rak'ahs without intermediate sitting

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on praying more than two rak'ahs of nafl without intermediate sitting and explain how istihsan overrides qiyas in this case.

Core Idea
In supererogatory prayer, a set of four rak'ahs is valid as one unit by istihsan, even without sitting after the first two.

This passage from Hashiyat al-Tahtawi addresses a common practical question: what happens when someone prays a nafl prayer of four or more rak'ahs without pausing to sit after every two? By strict analogy (qiyas), this would invalidate the prayer, but the Hanafi school applies juristic preference (istihsan) to rule it valid. The key is understanding that supererogatory prayers have greater flexibility, and the Prophet's own practice supports this.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling by qiyas
The act is praying more than two rak'ahs of nafl (e.g., four) without sitting except at the end. By qiyas, this is invalid because sitting after every two rak'ahs is required by analogy with obligatory prayers.
Zufar and one narration from Muhammad al-Shaybani held this view.
2
Recognize the Hanafi preferred ruling by istihsan
The Hanafi school, following Abu Hanifa and another narration from Muhammad, rules that the prayer is valid (sahih) by istihsan. The entire set is considered one continuous prayer.
Istihsan is based on the flexibility of nafl and the Prophet's practice.
3
Examine the dalil from the Sunnah
The text cites a hadith from Muslim that the Prophet (ﷺ) prayed nine rak'ahs at night with only one sitting in the eighth. This shows that sitting only at the end is permissible.
The hadith is ahad but sufficient for practice.
4
Understand the intra-Hanafi dispute
Zufar and a riwaya from Muhammad hold invalidity by qiyas; the relied-upon view (mufta bihi) is validity by istihsan. The dispute hinges on whether nafl is more flexible.
The author of al-Fath and others uphold istihsan.
5
Apply the rule to practical scenarios
If someone forgets to sit after the first two rak'ahs, they must perform sajdah al-sahw and return to the sitting if they remember before prostrating. If they sit only in the third and make taslim, there is disagreement.
This shows the nuanced application of the ruling.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإذا صلى نافلة أكثر من ركعتين كأربع فأتمها ولم يجلس إلا في آخرها فالقياس فسادها وبه قال زفر وهو رواية عن محمد وفي الاستحسان لا تفسد وهو قوله : صح نفله استحساناً لأنها صارت صلاة واحدة لأن التطوع كما شرع ركعتين شرع أربعاً أيضاً وفيها الفرض الجلوس آخرها لأنها صارت من ذوات الأربع ويجبر ترك القعود على الركعتين ساهياً بالسجود، ويجب العود إليه بتذكره بعد القيام ما لم يسجد كذا في الفتح، وروى مسلم أنه صلى تسع ركعات لم يجلس إلا في الثامنة، ثم نهض فصلى التاسعة، وإذا لم يقعد إلا على الثالثة وسلم اختلف في صحتها، أو في الخلاصة
And when he prays a nafl prayer of more than two rak'ahs, like four, and completes them and does not sit except in the last of them, then by qiyas it is invalid, and Zufar held this, and it is a narration from Muhammad. And by istihsan, it is not invalid, and that is his statement: his nafl is valid by istihsan, because it becomes one prayer. Because supererogatory prayer, just as it is legislated as two rak'ahs, is also legislated as four. And in it, the obligatory sitting is in its last because it becomes one of four-rak'ah prayers. And the omission of the sitting after two rak'ahs forgetfully is compensated by prostration of forgetfulness, and it is obligatory to return to it upon remembering after standing as long as he has not prostrated. Thus in al-Fath. And Muslim narrated that he (ﷺ) prayed nine rak'ahs and did not sit except in the eighth, then stood and prayed the ninth. And if he does not sit except in the third and then makes taslim, there is disagreement on its validity, or in al-Khulasah.
Source pages p. 392

Commentary
This passage from the hashia addresses the ruling when someone prays a nafl prayer of more than two rak'ahs (e.g., four) and only sits at the end. By strict analogy (qiyas), this would invalidate the prayer because each pair of rak'ahs should be separated by a sitting. Zufar and one narration from Muhammad hold this view. However, the Hanafi school prefers istihsan (juristic preference), ruling that the prayer is valid because all rak'ahs are considered as one continuous prayer. The author explains that supererogatory prayers can be performed as four rak'ahs in one set, with the obligatory sitting only at the end. If one forgets to sit after two rak'ahs, he must perform prostration of forgetfulness (sajdah al-sahw) and return to the sitting if he remembers before prostrating. The hadith from Muslim (narrated by Aisha) that the Prophet (ﷺ) prayed nine rak'ahs at night with only one sitting in the eighth supports the permissibility. If one sits only in the third and then makes taslim, there is disagreement on validity, with some saying it is valid and others not.

Key Terms
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference that overrides strict analogy (qiyas) due to a stronger evidence or custom.
قياس (qiyas): Analogical reasoning that derives a ruling for a new case from an established case due to shared effective cause ('illa).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling when someone prays four rak'ahs of nafl without sitting except at the end?
A) Invalid by qiyas and istihsan.
B) Valid by istihsan, though some say invalid by qiyas.
C) Invalid and must be repeated.
D) Valid only if done intentionally.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, performing more than two rak'ahs of nafl without intermediate sitting is valid by istihsan, supported by the Prophet's practice, and any omission of the wajib sitting is compensated by sajdah al-sahw.

Dislike of Excess Rak'ahs in Day and Night Nafl Prayers
Ruling on exceeding four or eight rak'ahs in nafl prayers.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on exceeding four rak'ahs by day and eight by night in nafl prayers and identify the differing views and their evidence.

Core Idea
Increasing nafl rak'ahs beyond four by day and eight by night: majority say disliked, but some authenticate permissibility.

This passage addresses a practical question for those who wish to pray extra nafl prayers with a single taslim. The Hanafi school has an internal difference: most mashayikh consider it makruh to exceed four rak'ahs in the day and eight at night, while al-Sarakhsi and the author of al-Mi'raj hold there is no dislike, citing the Prophet's practice of praying thirteen rak'ahs at night. Let's examine the proofs and reasoning behind these positions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is performing more than four rak'ahs during the day or eight at night with one taslim. The ruling according to most mashayikh is makruh (disliked).
The ruling applies to supererogatory prayers, not obligatory ones.
2
Locate the dalil for the majority view
The majority base their view on the fact that the Prophet (ﷺ) did not exceed these numbers. This is an implicit proof from practice.
Absence of action can indicate prohibition under certain usul principles.
3
Identify the counterview and its dalil
Al-Sarakhsi and al-Mi'raj argue that it is not disliked, relying on a hadith from Aisha that the Prophet prayed thirteen rak'ahs at night. Additionally, joining worship is considered virtuous.
The hadith is from Sahih al-Bukhari, a strong source.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The text presents both views but does not give a clear tarjih. It mentions that in al-Mi'raj the more correct view is no dislike, but the majority view is also recorded as the 'choice of most mashayikh'.
This indicates that neither view is definitively rejected.
5
Determine the practical consequence
In practice, a Hanafi should be aware that most scholars consider it disliked, but there is a valid opinion allowing it. The mufta bihi is not specified, so caution would favour avoiding excess, but one may follow the permissive view with knowledge of the difference.
Intra-madhhab differences like this are common in Hanafi fiqh.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وكره الزيادة على أربع بتسليمة في نهار والزيادة على ثمان ليلاً بتسليمة واحدة لأنه لم يزد عليه وهذا اختيار أكثر المشايخ، وفي المعراج والأصح أنه لا يكره لما فيه من وصل العبادة وكذا صحح السرخسي عدم كراهة الزيادة عليها لما صحيح البخاري عن عائشة الله عنها كان يصلي بالليل ثلاث عشرة
And it is disliked to increase beyond four with one taslim during the day, and to increase beyond eight at night with one taslim, because he (ﷺ) did not increase beyond that. And this is the choice of most mashayikh. And in al-Mi'raj, the more correct view is that it is not disliked, due to the joining of worship. Similarly, al-Sarakhsi declared the lack of dislike for increasing beyond them, because in Sahih al-Bukhari from Aisha (may Allah be pleased with her) that he (ﷺ) used to pray at night thirteen rak'ahs.
Source pages p. 392

Commentary
This passage discusses the ruling on how many rak'ahs can be joined with a single taslim in nafl prayers. The majority of Hanafi scholars (mashayikh) hold that it is makruh (disliked) to join more than four rak'ahs during the day and more than eight at night with one taslim. This is based on the fact that the Prophet (ﷺ) did not exceed these numbers. However, there is another view, adopted by the author of al-Mi'raj and al-Sarakhsi, that it is not disliked because joining worship is a virtuous act. They cite the hadith from Aisha that the Prophet (ﷺ) prayed thirteen rak'ahs at night, which suggests praying more than eight is allowed. The text does not explicitly state which view is mufta bihi, but the phrasing 'the more correct view' in al-Mi'raj suggests a preference for the non-dislike position. However, the author of the hashia records both opinions.

Key Terms
كراهة (karahah): Dislike; an act that is discouraged but not prohibited. May be either tanzih (slightly disliked) or tahrimi (prohibitively disliked).

Validity of Extended Nafl Without Intermediate Sitting (Istihsan over Qiyas)
Presents the ruling that extended nafl without sitting is valid by istihsan

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on praying more than two rak'ahs of nafl without intermediate sitting, explain why istihsan overrides qiyas, and identify the intra-Hanafi dispute.

Core Idea
Extended nafl without sitting is valid by istihsan, overriding qiyas, because the prayer becomes one unit.

This passage from Hashiyat al-Tahtawi clarifies a subtle intra-Hanafi dispute regarding supererogatory prayers. While qiyas (analogy) would invalidate the prayer if one does not sit after two rak'ahs, istihsan (juristic preference) upholds its validity based on evidence and ease. The lesson will unpack this conflict and the underlying principles.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act: praying more than two rak'ahs of nafl (e.g., four) without sitting except at the end. By qiyas, it is invalid (Zufar's view). By istihsan, it is valid (Abu Hanifa's view).
The final mufta bihi is the istihsan position.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof cited is a hadith from Sahih Muslim: the Prophet prayed nine rak'ahs without sitting except in the eighth.
This is an ahad hadith, so thubut is zanni.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The hadith demonstrates the permissibility of extended rak'ahs without intermediate sitting, supporting the istihsan ruling.
It shows that the prayer can be considered one unit.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Intra-Hanafi: Abu Hanifa vs. Zufar and a narration from Muhammad al-Shaybani. Also, a difference in tarawih due to its specific legislation.
The passage clarifies that tarawih has a different ruling.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is istihsan (valid). Al-Tahtawi indicates the istihsan view is correct.
The dispute is legitimate within the school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإذا صلى نافلة أكثر من ركعتين) كأربع فأتمها (ولم يجلس إلا في آخرها فالقياس فسادها وبه قال زفر وهو رواية عن محمد وفي الاستحسان لا تفسد وهو قوله : (صح) نفله (استحساناً لأنها صارت صلاة واحدة) لأن التطوع كما شرع ركعتين شرع أربعاً أيضاً وفيها الفرض الجلوس آخرها لأنها صارت من ذوات الأربع ويجبر ترك القعود على الركعتين ساهياً بالسجود، ويجب العود إليه بتذكره بعد القيام ما لم يسجد كذا في الفتح، وروى مسلم أنه صلى تسع ركعات لم يجلس إلا في الثامنة، ثم نهض فصلى التاسعة، وإذا لم يقعد إلا على الثالثة وسلم اختلف في صحتها، أو في الخلاصة

قوله: (وفي الاستحسان الخ) تطويل من غير فائدة، فالأولى الإقتصار على ما في المصنف. قوله : (لأنها صارت من ذوات الأربع (الخ هذا الكلام صريح في أنها تحسب بتمامها له خلافاً لمن قال : إنها شفعاً واحداً، ولا ينافيه ما ذكره ابن أمير حاج في بحث التراويح : لو صلى الكل بسلام واحد، ولم يقعد إلا في آخرها اختلف فيه المشايخ، والصحيح أنه يجزيه عن تسليمة واحدة كما لو صلى أربعاً بتسليمة واحدة، ولم يقعد على رأس الركعتين على ما هو الصحيح اه لأنه في التراويح خاصة لكونها شرعت على هيئة مخصوصة، فلا تؤدى بغيرها فالمعنى أنها تنوب عن ركعتين من التراويح وإن كانت تحسب له عشرين نافلة فتدبر . قوله: (وصحح الفساد في الخلاصة) لأن القعدة المشروعة قد تركها والتي فعلها لم تكن في محلها، ثم يجب عليه قضاء ركعتين لأنه شرع في الشفع الأول، ثم أفسده بترك القعود ولا يلزمه بالثالثة شيء مطلقاً عمداً كان، أو سهواً لأنّ البناء على الفاسد لا يلزمه شيئاً، أو تمامه في الشرح.
And if he prays supererogatory (nafl) more than two rak'ahs, like four and completes them, and he does not sit except in the last one, then by analogy (qiyas) it is invalid, and Zufar said this, and it is a narration from Muhammad; and by juristic preference (istihsan) it is not invalid, and it is his (Abu Hanifa's) saying: his nafl is valid by istihsan, because it has become one prayer. Because supererogatory (tatawwu') as it is legislated as two rak'ahs, it is also legislated as four, and in it, sitting at the end is obligatory (fard) because it has become one of the four-rak'ah prayers. And the omission of sitting at the end of two rak'ahs is compensated by prostration of forgetfulness (sajdah al-sahw) if done forgetfully, and it is obligatory to return to it upon remembering after standing as long as he has not prostrated, as in al-Fath. And Muslim narrated that he (the Prophet) prayed nine rak'ahs and did not sit except in the eighth, then he stood up and prayed the ninth. And if he did not sit except at the third and made taslim, there is disagreement on its validity, or in al-Khulasa.

His statement: '(And in istihsan...)' is lengthy without benefit, so it is better to limit to what is in the text. His statement: '(Because it has become one of the four-rak'ah prayers...)' This speech is explicit that it counts in its entirety for him, contrary to those who say it is one pair (shaf'). And it does not contradict what Ibn Amir Hajj mentioned in the discussion of tarawih: 'If he prays all with one taslim and does not sit except at the end, the mashayikh disagreed, and the correct view is that it suffices for one taslim, just as if he prayed four with one taslim and did not sit at the end of two rak'ahs, according to the correct view,' because it is specifically in tarawih due to its being legislated in a specific manner, so it is not performed otherwise. So the meaning is that it substitutes for two rak'ahs of tarawih even if it counts for him as twenty nafl, so ponder. His statement: '(And he declared it invalid in al-Khulasa)' because the legislated sitting has been omitted, and the one he performed was not in its place, and then he must make up two rak'ahs because he began the first pair (shaf') and then invalidated it by omitting the sitting, and nothing is required from him by the third rak'ah, whether intentionally or forgetfully, because building on the invalid does not necessitate anything, or its completion in al-Sharh.
Source pages p. 392

Commentary
This passage addresses a Hanafi dispute regarding voluntary prayers (nafl) of more than two rak'ahs. The base text from Maraqi al-Falah states the ruling: if one prays more than two rak'ahs of nafl (e.g., four) and does not sit for tashahhud except at the end, then according to qiyas (analogy) the prayer is invalid—this was the view of Zufar and a narration from Muhammad al-Shaybani. However, according to istihsan (juristic preference), the prayer is valid, and this is the relied-upon position (qawl Abi Hanifa). The reason is that nafl, like the obligatory prayers, is legislated as two rak'ahs but also as four. Since the prayer becomes one unit of four rak'ahs, sitting (qa'dah) at the end becomes obligatory (fard) for the entire prayer. If one omits the intermediate sitting forgetfully, it is compensated by sajdah al-sahw, and one must return to it upon remembering if he has not yet prostrated (as in al-Fath). The hadith from Muslim is cited as evidence: the Prophet (ﷺ) prayed nine rak'ahs without sitting except in the eighth, then stood for the ninth. This shows that extended prayer without intermediate sitting is valid. The hashya then clarifies that the phrase 'wa fi al-istihsan' is sufficient, and that the prayer counts as one complete unit. It addresses potential confusion with tarawih prayer, where the ruling is different because tarawih is legislated with specific pairs. The discussion also notes that some (in al-Khulasa) declared the prayer invalid if one omits the intermediate sitting, requiring compensation by repeating two rak'ahs. The hashya resolves that the prayer is valid by istihsan, and the correct view is the one stated.

Key Terms
الاستحسان (al-istihsan): Juristic preference that allows overriding qiyas in certain cases for a more suitable ruling.
القياس (al-qiyas): Analogical reasoning deriving a ruling for a new case from an original case with shared cause.
الشفع (al-shaf'): A pair of rak'ahs; a unit of two rak'ahs in prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Invalid by both qiyas and istihsan
B) Valid by istihsan, but invalid by qiyas
C) Valid only if one sits at the end of every two rak'ahs
D) Invalid unless it is tarawih

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, extended nafl without intermediate sitting is valid by istihsan, supported by the Prophet's practice.

Dislike of Exceeding Four or Eight Rak'ahs per Taslim
Intra-Hanafi dispute on karahah of exceeding four/eight rak'ahs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the Hanafi ruling on exceeding four rak'ahs (day) or eight (night) with one taslim and explain the intra-madhhab dispute regarding karahah.

Core Idea
The majority of Hanafi scholars hold that exceeding four (day) or eight (night) rak'ahs in one taslim is prohibitively disliked, but some authorities disagree.

This passage from Hashiyat al-Tahtawi addresses a nuanced issue in nafl prayer: can one combine more than four rak'ahs during the day or eight at night under a single taslim? While the majority of later mashayikh rule this as makruh tahrimi, there is a significant minority opinion that sees no dislike. The discussion revolves around the absence of prophetic precedent and the interpretation of the hadith of Aisha about the Prophet's night prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the majority ruling
The act is performing voluntary prayers with a single taslim exceeding four rak'ahs during the day or eight at night. The majority of mashayikh consider this makruh tahrimi (prohibitively disliked).
The ruling applies to nafl prayers, not to fard or other specific prayers.
2
State the evidence for the majority view
The majority rely on the absence of any report that the Prophet (ﷺ) exceeded these numbers with one taslim. They argue that if it were permissible, the Prophet would have done so to teach permissibility.
3
Identify the minority view and its evidence
Scholars like those cited in al-Mi'raj and al-Sarakhsi hold that it is not disliked. Their evidence includes the hadith of Aisha that the Prophet prayed thirteen rak'ahs at night, and the principle that connecting worship is commendable.
The minority view considers the act permissible without dislike.
4
Analyze the rebuttal to the minority evidence
Al-Tahtawi argues that the hadith of Aisha does not prove that all thirteen rak'ahs were performed with one taslim, so it does not refute the majority position. The hadith is insufficient to remove the dislike.
This critical refinement shows that the hadith is not directly relevant to the case.
5
Determine the mufta bihi position
The relied-upon position for fatwa is the majority view of dislike, though there is flexibility given the disagreement. Practically, one should avoid exceeding the limits to avoid potential sin.
The authority weight is fatawa mutakhkhirin.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وكره الزيادة على أربع بتسليمة في نقل (النهار و) الزيادة (على ثمان ليلاً) بتسليمة واحدة لأنه لم يزد عليه وهذا اختيار أكثر المشايخ، وفي المعراج والأصح أنه لا يكره لما فيه من وصل العبادة وكذا صحح السرخسي عدم كراهة الزيادة عليها لما صحيح البخاري عن عائشة الله عنها كان يصلي بالليل ثلاث عشرة

قوله: (وكره الزيادة على أربع بتسليمة في نقل (النهار) باتفاق الروايات لأنه لم يرو أنه صلى الله عليه وسلم زاد على ذلك، ولولا الكراهة لزاد تعليماً للجواز كذا قالوا وهذا يفيد أنها تحريمية اهـ سيد عن النهر. قوله: (وعلى ثمان ليلاً) تعرب ثمان إعراب قاض، وقد تظهر عليها الحركات. قوله: (لما في صحيح البخاري الخ) هذا لا ينتج المدعي لأنه لا يفيد أنه جمع بين العشر بتسليمة واحدة.
And it is disliked to increase beyond four with one taslim in a tradition (relating to the day) and the increase (beyond eight at night) with one taslim, because he did not increase beyond that, and this is the choice of most mashayikh. And in al-Mi'raj, the soundest view is that it is not disliked because of the connection of worship. Similarly, al-Sarakhsi declared there is no dislike of increasing beyond it due to the Sahih al-Bukhari from Aisha (may Allah be pleased with her): 'He used to pray at night thirteen rak'ahs.'

His statement: '(And it is disliked to increase beyond four with one taslim in a tradition (relating to the day)) by agreement of the narrations, because it has not been reported that the Prophet (ﷺ) increased beyond that, and were it not for dislike, he would have increased to teach permissibility, as they said, and this indicates it is prohibitively disliked (tahriman).' From Sayyid from al-Nahr. His statement: '(And beyond eight at night)' 'eight' is declined like 'qadi', and the vowels appear on it. His statement: '(Due to what is in Sahih al-Bukhari...)' this does not produce what is claimed because it does not indicate that he combined the ten with one taslim.
Source pages p. 392

Commentary
This passage discusses the ruling on making voluntary prayers with a single taslim (salutation) exceeding four rak'ahs during the day or eight at night. The base text from Maraqi al-Falah states that this is disliked (makruh) according to the majority of later scholars (mashayikh), as the Prophet (ﷺ) did not increase beyond that. However, in al-Mi'raj, the correct view is that it is not disliked because the act should be performed as a continuous worship. Al-Sarakhsi corrected the view to be no dislike, citing the hadith of Aisha that the Prophet prayed thirteen rak'ahs at night. The hashya clarifies that the dislike according to most narrations is because no report shows the Prophet exceeding four in day or eight at night. The hadith of Aisha is argued not to prove that he prayed all thirteen with one taslim. The hashya also notes that the word 'eight' is declined. The passage concludes that there is disagreement, with the majority ruling of dislike (tahrimi).

Key Terms
الكراهة (al-karahah): Legal dislike; here it is prohibitively disliked (makruh tahrimi), close to haram.
التسليمة (al-taslimah): The salutation ending the prayer; a single taslim marks the end of a complete prayer unit.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) Disliked (makruh)
C) Permissible only if done at night

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school predominantly considers exceeding four (day) or eight (night) rak'ahs with one taslim as prohibitively disliked, though a minority disputes this.

Preferred Number of Rak'ahs in Night Nafl: An Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Abu Hanifa and the two imams on the best way to perform night and day nafl prayers

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa and the two sahibayn on the preferred number of rak'ahs for night voluntary prayer, explain the evidence for each, and identify which view is mufta bihi and why.

Core Idea
The night prayer can be four rak'ahs with one taslim, but the fatwa follows two-by-two following the hadith.

This lesson examines a classic intra-Hanafi dispute about the best way to perform voluntary prayers at night. Abu Hanifa preferred four rak'ahs in one sitting, while his two main students—Abu Yusuf and Muhammad—favored two rak'ahs with a separate taslim each. The dispute turns on how to interpret the prophetic hadith 'Night prayer is two by two.'

Guided Path
1
State both positions
Clearly articulate the views of Abu Hanifa (four rak'ahs with one taslim is best for both night and day) and the sahibayn (day: same as Abu Hanifa; night: two-by-two is best).
Note that the dispute is only about night; day is agreed upon.
2
Identify the main proof for each
Abu Hanifa relies on the Prophet's reported practice of praying four rak'ahs at night (and four for duha) without separating with taslim. The sahibayn rely on the explicit hadith: 'Night prayer is two by two.'
Both proofs are accepted as authentic; the issue is how to weigh them.
3
Analyze the Hanafi response to the hadith
Ibn al-Humam explains that the hadith may indicate permissibility of two-by-two, not superiority over four. He argues that four is more virtuous because it is more burdensome, citing hadith on reward according to exertion.
The response uses istihsan and preference for the more strenuous act.
4
Determine the practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf)
The fatwa is given according to the sahibayn for night prayer (two-by-two), but the more virtuous act remains four rak'ahs with one taslim. Thus, a person may choose either, but following the fatwa is recommended for ease.
The mufta bihi is based on the hadith, but virtue is not lost.
5
Note the authority weight
Although the fatwa follows the sahibayn, later Hanafi scholars like al-Tahtawi and Ibn al-Humam affirm that Abu Hanifa's view is superior in virtue. The authority weight is from fatawa mutakhkhirin.
This shows the nuanced hierarchy: fatwa vs. afdaliyyah.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والأفضل فيهما) أي الليل والنهار (رباع) عند أبي حنيفة رحمه الله تعالى لأن النبي كان يصلي بالليل أربع ركعات لا تسل عن حسنهن وطولهن ثم يصلي أربعاً لا تسل عن حسنهن وطولهن وكان صلى الله عليه وسلم يصلي الضحى أربعاً، ولا يفصل بينهن بسلام وثبت مواظبته الله على الأربع في الضحى (وعندهما) أي أبي يوسف و محمد (الأفضل) في النهار كما قال الإمام: وفي الليل مثنى مثنى) قال في الدراية: وفي العيون (وبه) أي بقولهما (يفتى) اتباعاً للحديث وهو قوله عليه الصلاة والسلام: صلاة الليل مثنى مثنى

قوله: اتباعاً للحديث الخ) أجاب المحقق ابن الهمام عن هذا الحديث بأن لفظه يحتمل أن يكون المعنى فيه مثنى في حق الفضيلة بالنسبة إلى الأربع أو في حق الإباحة بالنسبة إلى الفرد، وترجيح ! أحدهما لا يكون إلا بمرجح، وقد ورد فعله على كلام النحوين لكن عقلنا زيادة فضيلة الأربع بأنها أكثر مشقة على النفس بسبب طول تقييدها في مقام الخدمة، ورأيناه قال: «إنما أجرك على قدر نصبك وقال : أفضل الأعمال أجهدها ولهذا لو نذر أن يصلي أربعاً بتسليمة لا يخرج عنه بتسليمتين، وعلى القلب يخرج فحكمنا بأن المراد الثاني وهو الإباحة أن يباح مثنى لا ،واحدة أو ثلاثاً، ووافق الكمال على ذلك تلميذه العلامة قاسم، وغيره.
And the more excellent in them (i.e., night and day) is four rak'ahs according to Abu Hanifa (may Allah have mercy on him) because the Prophet used to pray at night four rak'ahs—do not ask about their beauty and length—then he would pray four [more]—do not ask about their beauty and length. And the Prophet (ﷺ) used to pray the forenoon (duha) prayer four rak'ahs, and he did not separate them with a taslim. And his constant practice (muwazabah) on four in duha has been established. And according to them (i.e., Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), the more excellent in the day is as Imam [Abu Hanifa] said, but in the night it is two by two (mathna mathna). It is said in al-Dirayah and in al-Uyun: and by their statement (i.e., of the two) fatwa is given, following the hadith, which is his statement (peace be upon him): 'The night prayer is two by two.'

His statement: 'Following the hadith...' al-Muhaqqiq Ibn al-Humam answered this hadith by saying: its wording may mean that it is two by two in terms of virtue compared to four, or in terms of permissibility compared to single [rak'ahs]. Preferring one of them cannot be except with a preponderance, and his action has been reported by the grammarians. But we understood the increased virtue of four because it is more burdensome on the soul due to the length of constraint in the station of service, and we saw that he said: 'Your reward is according to your exertion,' and he said: 'The best deeds are the most strenuous.' For this reason, if someone vows to pray four rak'ahs with one taslim, he does not fulfill it by two taslims, and conversely, he does fulfill it. So we ruled that the intended meaning is the second, which is permissibility: that two by two is permissible, not one or three. And al-Kamal agreed with that, and his student the scholar Qasim, and others.
Source pages p. 393

Commentary
This passage presents the intra-Hanafi dispute on the preferred number of rak'ahs for voluntary prayers (nafl). Abu Hanifa holds that the best is to pray four rak'ahs in both night and day, based on the practice of the Prophet (ﷺ) as reported by Aisha (four rak'ahs, then four more at night, and four for duha without separating with taslim). Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the two sahibayn) agree for the day but for the night they consider two-by-two to be better, following the hadith 'The night prayer is two by two.' The fatwa is given according to their view. The hashya by al-Tahtawi reports Ibn al-Humam's answer to the hadith: it can be interpreted as two-by-two being better in virtue or merely permissible. He resolves that it indicates permissibility, not superiority over four, because four is more burdensome and thus more rewarding, citing hadith about reward according to exertion. He gives an example: if one vows to pray four with one taslim, he cannot fulfill it with two taslims, proving that four with one taslim is a valid and distinct act. Thus, four is superior, but two-by-two is permissible.

Key Terms
مثنى مثنى (mathna mathna): Two by two; performing prayer in units of two rak'ahs with a separate taslim each.
الأفضل (al-afdal): The more excellent or preferred form of worship.
رباع (ruba'): Four; here meaning four rak'ahs with one taslim.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Two rak'ahs separately, two by two
C) Eight rak'ahs with one taslim
D) Thirteen rak'ahs in one go

Key Takeaway
For night voluntary prayers, the Hanafi fatwa is two-by-two, but four rak'ahs with one taslim is more virtuous according to Abu Hanifa.

Long Qiyam vs Many Sujud: Hanafi Preference
Determines the preferred act in voluntary prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the superiority of long standing over abundant prostration in voluntary prayer and explain the proofs cited.

Core Idea
Long qiyam is preferred because recitation is superior to tasbih and the Prophet said the best prayer is long standing.

What brings more reward in voluntary prayer: prolonged standing or many prostrations? This passage from Maraqi al-Falah with al-Tahtawi's hashya addresses precisely this question, presenting the Hanafi preference for long qiyam and the proofs that support it, while also acknowledging an internal disagreement within the school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its level
Determine what exactly is being ruled upon. Is it a matter of obligation, recommendation, or mere preference?
The text uses 'ahab' (more beloved), indicating preference within sunnah, not obligation.
2
Locate the primary proof (dalil)
Find the hadith cited and note its wording. Understand how it is used to support the preference for long standing.
The hadith 'Afḍal al-ṣalāt ṭūl al-qunūt' directly states the best prayer has long standing.
3
Understand the secondary reasoning
Identify the reasoning that long standing increases recitation, and recitation is superior to tasbih (which increases with prostration).
Recitation (qira'ah) is a pillar of the prayer; tasbih is a sunnah act within ruku' and sujud.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Recognize that Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani initially held a contrary view, preferring abundant ruku' and sujud, but later agreed with the majority.
This ikhtilaf is documented in al-Mujtaba and reconciled by al-Tahawi and others.
5
Evaluate the tarjih (preferred view)
Determine which position is mufta bihi and why. Consider the strength of the proofs and the later authorities.
Al-Tahtawi supports long qiyam, and this is the relied-upon position for fatwa.

And because recitation becomes abundant with long standing, and with abundant bowing and prostration, tasbih (glorification) becomes abundant, and recitation is better than it. Commentary
This passage discusses the relative virtue of long standing (qiyam) versus many prostrations (sujud) in voluntary prayer. The base text states that long standing is more beloved (ahab), citing the hadith 'The best of prayer is long standing,' and reasoning that recitation (qira'ah) increases with long standing, and recitation is superior to tasbih (which increases with sujud). The hashya provides additional proof: long standing is more strenuous and farther from hypocrisy, and it is a time of divine mercy and manifestation. The Quranic verse 'Their sides forsake their beds' (32:16) is cited in praise of night prayers, with the hashya noting the appropriate context. However, a contrary view is transmitted from Muhammad al-Shaybani that abundant ruku' and sujud is better. Al-Tahawi reports that Muhammad later agreed with the majority, and this was corrected in al-Bada'i. The hashya also mentions that Imam Ahmad hesitated and Malik equated them. The text ends abruptly, seemingly about to present further discussion.

القنوت (al-qunut): Here means standing, not the du'a of qunut; synonymous with qiyam.
التجافي (al-tajafi): Leaving or keeping away from beds, used in Quran for those who pray at night.
أفضل الصلاة طول القنوت (Afḍal al-ṣalāt ṭūl al-qunūt): Hadith meaning 'The best of prayer is long standing.'

The Hanafi school prefers long standing in voluntary prayer because of the hadith and the principle that recitation (a pillar) outweighs tasbih (a sunnah).

Preferred Number of Rak'ahs: Four at Once or Two by Two?
Intra-Hanafi dispute on the best rak'ah count for night nafl.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on the preferred number of rak'ahs for night prayer and identify the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
Abu Hanifa prefers four rak'ahs in one taslim; the Sahibayn say two-by-two at night — the fatwa follows the Sahibayn.

This lesson examines an intra-Hanafi dispute about the best way to perform supererogatory night prayer. Imam Abu Hanifa favored praying four rak'ahs with a single salam, based on the Prophet's practice. His two foremost students, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, held that night prayer should be prayed two rak'ahs at a time, citing an explicit hadith. Understanding this difference and which view is relied upon for fatwa is essential for a Hanafi's practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the dispute
Recognize that the act is supererogatory night prayer (tahajjud). The dispute is whether it is better to pray four rak'ahs with one taslim or two-by-two.
Both forms are valid; the dispute is about optimality (afdaliyyah).
2
State Abu Hanifa's position and proof
Abu Hanifa holds that four rak'ahs with one taslim is best. His proof is the Prophet's consistent practice of praying four rak'ahs at night without separating them.
This is based on the hadith reported by Aisha about the Prophet's night prayer.
3
State the Sahibayn's position and proof
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad hold that night prayer is best performed two-by-two. Their proof is the explicit hadith: 'Night prayer is two by two.'
This hadith is found in Sahih al-Bukhari and Muslim.
4
Analyze the tarjih
The fatwa follows the Sahibayn because an explicit statement (mantuq) is given precedence over inferred practice (mafhum) in Hanafi usul.
Al-Tahtawi cites al-Diraya and al-Uyun that the fatwa is with the Sahibayn.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence is that praying two-by-two is the recommended form, but praying four with one taslim is still valid. The reward (thawab) is greater in the preferred form.
A person following Abu Hanifa's view is not sinful, but the mufta bihi is to follow the Sahibayn.

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the preferred number of rak'ahs in nafl prayers, specifically in night and day prayer. The base text states that the best is four rak'ahs with one taslim, which is the position of Imam Abu Hanifa. He supports this with the practice of the Prophet (ﷺ) who prayed four rak'ahs at night without separating them, and four for Duha. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that at night, the best is two-by-two, citing the hadith 'Night prayer is two by two.' The passage notes that the fatwa is given according to the Sahibayn. The commentator then discusses the preference between length of standing and abundance of prostrations. Abu Hanifa's view that length of standing is better is supported by the hadith 'The best prayer is length of qunut' and because recitation is superior to tasbih. However, a transmission from Muhammad favors abundance of prostrations. Abu Yusuf reconciles by saying that if one has a set recitation, increasing the number of rak'ahs is better; otherwise, lengthy standing is better.

Key Terms
رباع (rubāʿ): Four rak'ahs prayed with a single taslim (one sitting for tashahhud and salam at the end).
مثنى (mathnā): Two rak'ahs prayed with a separate taslim, i.e., two-by-two.
صلاة الليل (ṣalāt al-layl): Any voluntary prayer performed during the night, including tahajjud and witr.

Length of Standing vs Abundance of Prostrations: A Hanafi Preference Debate
Intra-Hanafi dispute on preference between long standing and many prostrations in nafl prayer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi positions on whether long standing or many prostrations is superior in supererogatory prayer, and apply Abu Yusuf's distinction.

Core Idea
Length of standing is generally better than more prostrations, but if one has a set amount of recitation, more rak'ahs become preferable.

After discussing the number of rak'ahs, the commentator turns to a related preference: is it better to have a long standing (qiyam) or to increase the number of prostrations (sujud) in nafl prayer? Imam Abu Hanifa holds that long standing is better, citing a hadith. However, a report from Imam Muhammad favors more prostrations. Abu Yusuf reconciles the two by distinguishing based on whether one has a fixed amount of Quranic recitation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two competing virtues
Recognize that the debate is between long standing (qiyam tawil) and many prostrations (kathrat al-sujud) in supererogatory prayer.
Both increase reward, but which is better is disputed.
2
State Abu Hanifa's position and evidence
Abu Hanifa holds that long standing is better. His evidence is the hadith: 'The best prayer is length of standing' and the reasoning that recitation (which increases with long standing) is superior to tasbih (which increases with many prostrations).
This position is considered the main view in the school.
3
State Muhammad's contrary view
Imam Muhammad transmitted a view that abundance of bowing and prostration is better. This is based on a report in al-Mujtaba.
This view is considered a nawadir (rare) transmission.
4
Explain Abu Yusuf's reconciliation
Abu Yusuf distinguishes: if a person has a fixed amount of Quranic recitation (a specific portion to recite), then increasing the number of rak'ahs is better because each additional rak'ah adds extra sujud without reducing the total recitation. Otherwise, long standing is better.
This reconciliation harmonizes the two positions.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position is Abu Hanifa's view that long standing is generally better, but with Abu Yusuf's practical distinction when there is fixed recitation.
This nuanced approach is often applied in fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الصلاة
٣٩٣
ركعة، ثم يصلي إذا سمع النداء بالصبح ركعتين خفيفتين فتبقى العشر نفلاً أي، والثلاث وتراكما في البرهان (والأفضل فيهما) أي الليل والنهار (رباع) عند أبي حنيفة رحمه الله تعالى لأن النبي كان يصلي بالليل أربع ركعات لا تسل عن حسنهن وطولهن ثم يصلي أربعاً لا تسل عن حسنهن وطولهن وكان صلى الله عليه وسلم يصلي الضحى أربعاً، ولا يفصل بينهن بسلام وثبت مواظبته الله على الأربع في الضحى (وعندهما) أي أبي يوسف و محمد (الأفضل) في النهار كما قال الإمام: وفي الليل مثنى مثنى) قال في الدراية: وفي العيون (وبه) أي بقولهما (يفتى) اتباعاً للحديث وهو قوله عليه الصلاة والسلام: صلاة الليل مثنى مثنى وصلاة الليل خصوصاً في الثلث الأخير منه أفضل من صلاة النهار) لأنه أشق على النفس، وقال تعالى : تتجافى جنوبهم عن المضاجع (وطول القيام) في الصلاة ليلاً أو نهاراً (أحب من كثرة السجود) لقوله : (أفضل الصلاة طول القنوت) أي القيام ولأن القراءة تكثر بطول القيام وبكثرة الركوع والسجود يكثر التسبيح والقراءة أفضل منه ونقل في المجتبى عن محمد خلافه، وهو أن كثرة الركوع والسجود أفضل وفصل أبو يوسف رحمه الله تعالى فقال : إذا كان له ورد من الليل بقراءة من القرآن فالأفضل أن يكثر عدد الركعات، وإلا فطول القيام أفضل لأن القيام في الأول لا يختلف ويضم إليه زيادة الركوع والسجود.
Book of Prayer. ... then he prays when he hears the call for Fajr two light rak'ahs, so the ten remain as supererogatory, and the three as witr. And in al-Burhan: (The best in both) i.e., night and day (is four) according to Abu Hanifa, may Allah have mercy on him, because the Prophet used to pray at night four rak'ahs—do not ask about their beauty and length—then pray four more—do not ask about their beauty and length—and he used to pray Duha four, and he did not separate between them with a salam, and his constant practice of four in Duha is established. (And according to them two) i.e., Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the best in the day is as the Imam said, and at night it is two by two). He said in al-Diraya: And in al-Uyun: (And by it) i.e., by their statement (the fatwa is given) following the hadith, which is his saying, peace be upon him: 'Night prayer is two by two.' And night prayer, especially in the last third, is better than day prayer because it is harder on the soul, and Allah says: 'Their sides forsake their beds.' And (length of standing) in prayer at night or day (is more beloved than abundance of prostrations) because of his saying: 'The best prayer is length of qunut' i.e., standing, and because recitation increases with length of standing, and with abundance of bowing and prostrations, glorification increases, and recitation is better than it. And it was reported in al-Mujtaba from Muhammad a contrary opinion, that abundance of bowing and prostration is better. And Abu Yusuf, may Allah have mercy on him, distinguished, saying: If one has a portion of the night with recitation from the Quran, then increasing the number of rak'ahs is better; otherwise, length of standing is better, because standing in the first case is not different, and to it is added the increase of bowing and prostration.
Source pages p. 393

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the preferred number of rak'ahs in nafl prayers, specifically in night and day prayer. The base text states that the best is four rak'ahs with one taslim, which is the position of Imam Abu Hanifa. He supports this with the practice of the Prophet (ﷺ) who prayed four rak'ahs at night without separating them, and four for Duha. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that at night, the best is two-by-two, citing the hadith 'Night prayer is two by two.' The passage notes that the fatwa is given according to the Sahibayn. The commentator then discusses the preference between length of standing and abundance of prostrations. Abu Hanifa's view that length of standing is better is supported by the hadith 'The best prayer is length of qunut' and because recitation is superior to tasbih. However, a transmission from Muhammad favors abundance of prostrations. Abu Yusuf reconciles by saying that if one has a set recitation, increasing the number of rak'ahs is better; otherwise, lengthy standing is better.

Key Terms
طول القيام (ṭūl al-qiyām): Lengthy standing in prayer, especially in supererogatory prayers, to increase recitation.
كثرة السجود (kathrat al-sujūd): Abundance of prostrations, i.e., increasing the number of rak'ahs to have more sujud.
ورد (ward): A fixed portion of Quranic recitation that one regularly recites in night prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Yusuf's distinction, in which scenario is it better to increase the number of rak'ahs?
A) When one has a fixed amount of recitation
B) When one wants long standing
C) When one prays in congregation
D) When one is travelling

Key Takeaway
The merit of long standing vs many prostrations depends on whether one has a fixed recitation: if yes, more rak'ahs are better; if not, long standing is better.
