Tahiyyat al-Masjid: Ruling and Etiquette
Ruling on the sunnah of greeting the mosque with two rak'ahs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on tahiyyat al-masjid, identify the conditions for its validity, and apply the exceptions.

Core Idea
Tahiyyat al-masjid is sunnah, not wajib; the hadith's command is understood as a recommendation.

This lesson examines the sunnah of greeting the mosque with two rak'ahs upon entry. We will study the proof from hadith, the conditions for its performance, and the important exceptions, including disliked times and the Sacred Mosque. Understanding these nuances ensures one fulfills this sunnah correctly.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its proof
The passage states that tahiyyat al-masjid is sunnah. The primary proof is the hadith: 'If one of you enters the mosque, let him not sit until he prays two rak'ahs.' The Hanafi school interprets this imperative as a recommendation, not an obligation.
2
Understand the conditions
The prayer should be performed at a non-disliked time, preferably before sitting. If one sits, he may still pray without losing the sunnah. The prayer can be any prayer performed upon entry, even an obligatory one, without the intention of greeting.
Disliked times: after Fajr and after Asr, and at midday.
3
Note the exceptions
At disliked times, one should not pray tahiyyah but instead engage in dhikr. The Sacred Mosque is excepted: its greeting is tawaf for those who intend it. If one is unable to pray due to ritual impurity, he may recite the four tasbih phrases.
For multiple entries per day, two rak'ahs suffice for the whole day.
4
Recognize the substitution and sufficiency
Any prayer performed upon entry suffices for tahiyyah, even an obligatory prayer, because the purpose of reverence is achieved. The sunnah is not invalidated by sitting first.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
في تحية المسجد وصلاة الضحى وإحياء الليالي
وغيرها (سن تحية المسجد بركعتين) يصليهما في غير وقت مكروه (قبل الجلوس) لقوله : إذا دخل أحدكم المسجد فلا يجلس حتى يركع ركعتين (وأداء الفرض ينوب عنها قاله الزيلعي ( و ) كذا كل صلاة أداها أي فعلها (عند الدخول بلا نية التحية) لأنها التعظيمة وحرمته، وقد حصل ذلك بما صلاه ولا تفوت بالجلوس عندنا وإن كان الأفضل فعلها قبله وإذا تكرر دخوله يكفيه ركعتان في اليوم وندب أن يقول عند دخول المسجد :
في المجتبى قوله للسائل : عليك بكثرة السجود وللآخر: أعني على نفسك بكثرة السجود وقوله : أقرب ما يكون العبد من ربه وهو ساجده لأنّ السجود غاية التواضع والعبودية والله سبحانه وتعالى أعلم، وأستغفر الله العظيم.
فصل في تحية المسجد
قوله: (وغيرها) كصلاة الليل والإستخارة. قوله : (سن) تحية المسجد) أي تحية رب المسجد لأن التحية إنما تكون لصاحب المكان لا للمكان ويستثنى المسجد الحرام فإن تحيته المثلا الطواف وصرح علي: بأن من دخل المسجد الحرام لا يشتغل بتحية لأن تحية هذا المسجد الشريف هو الطواف لمن عليه طواف، أو أراده بخلاف من لم يرده، أو أراد أن يجلس
فلا يجلس حتى يصلي ركعتين تحية المسجد .اهـ. قوله : ( بركعتين) وإن شاء بأربع والثنتان أفضل قهستاني قوله: (في غير وقت مكروه في القهستاني إذا دخل المسجد بعد الفجر، أو العصر لا يأتي بالتحية، بل يسبح ويهلل، ويصلي على النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم فإنه حينئذ يؤيدي حق المسجد كما إذا دخل للمكتوبة فإنه غير مأمور بها كما في التمرتاشي، اهـ، وفي الدر عن الضياء عن القوت من لم يتمكن منها لحدث، أو غيره يقول: كلمات التسبيح الأربع أربعاً اهـ وهي سبحان الله والحمد لله، ولا إله إلا الله والله أكبر . قوله : (قبل الجلوس) هذا بيان للأولى كما يأتي، وهذا قول العامة، وهو الصحيح، وقيل: يجلس أولاً، ثم يصلي. قوله: (وإن كان الأفضل فعلها قبله هذا يدل على أنهم حملوا النهي في حديث فلا يجلس حتى يركع ركعتين
On greeting the mosque, Duha prayer, and reviving the nights and other things. (It is sunnah to greet the mosque with two rak'ahs) that he prays at a non-disliked time (before sitting) because of his saying: 'If one of you enters the mosque, let him not sit until he prays two rak'ahs.' (And the performance of the obligatory prayer suffices for it), said al-Zayla'i. (And likewise any prayer that he performs upon entering without the intention of greeting), because it is reverence and honor, and that has been achieved by what he prayed. And it is not lost by sitting according to us, although it is better to do it before sitting. And if his entry is repeated, two rak'ahs per day suffice for him. And it is recommended to say upon entering the mosque: ... In al-Mujtaba: his saying to one questioner: 'I urge you to increase prostrations,' and to another: 'Help me with your prostration,' and his saying: 'The closest a servant is to his Lord is while he is prostrating,' because prostration is the ultimate humility and servitude. And Allah knows best, and I seek forgiveness from Allah the Almighty. Chapter on greeting the mosque. His saying: (and other things) like night prayer and istikhara. His saying: (Sunnah of greeting the mosque) i.e., greeting the Lord of the mosque, because greeting is only for the master of the place, not for the place. The Sacred Mosque is excepted, for its greeting is tawaf. And Ali stated: 'Whoever enters the Sacred Mosque should not busy himself with tahiyyah because the greeting of this noble mosque is tawaf for one who has tawaf to do or intends it, contrary to one who does not intend it or wants to sit, then he should not sit until he prays two rak'ahs of tahiyyat al-masjid.' End. His saying: (with two rak'ahs) and if he wishes, with four, but two are better (Qahistani). His saying: (at a non-disliked time). In al-Qahistani: If one enters the mosque after Fajr or Asr, he should not perform tahiyyah, but rather should glorify, say tahlil, and send blessings on the Prophet, for then he fulfills the right of the mosque, as if he entered for an obligatory prayer, he is not commanded to do it, as in al-Tamartashi. End. And in al-Durr from al-Diya' from al-Qut: If one is unable to do it due to hadath or other reason, he says the four words of tasbih four times: 'Subhan Allah, al-Hamd li Allah, La ilaha illa Allah, Allahu Akbar.' His saying: (before sitting) is an explanation of what is better, as will come. This is the statement of the majority, and it is correct. And it was said: He may sit first then pray. His saying: (And although it is better to do it before him) indicates that they understood the prohibition in the hadith 'Do not sit until you pray two rak'ahs' as one of etiquette, not absolute obligation.
Source pages p. 394

Commentary
This passage discusses the ruling (tahiyyat al-masjid), which is a sunnah upon entering the mosque. The primary ruling is that it is sunnah to pray two rak'ahs before sitting, based on the hadith: 'If one of you enters the mosque, let him not sit until he prays two rak'ahs.' The commentator explains several points: (1) A person may fulfill this sunnah by any prayer performed upon entering, even an obligatory prayer, because the purpose is reverence. (2) If one sits before praying, the sunnah is not lost according to the Hanafi school, though it is better to pray before sitting. (3) If one enters the mosque multiple times a day, two rak'ahs are sufficient for the entire day. (4) The times of prohibition (after Fajr and Asr) apply: one should not pray tahiyyah then but instead do dhikr. (5) The Sacred Mosque has a different greeting: tawaf, not prayer, for those who intend tawaf. (6) If one is unable to pray due to ritual impurity or other reason, he may recite the four tasbih phrases. The passage ends with a note on the understanding of the hadith: the prohibition of sitting without praying is a recommendation, not an absolute prohibition.

Key Terms
تحية المسجد (taḥiyyat al-masjid): A two-rak'ah prayer performed upon entering a mosque to honor the mosque (actually its Lord).
سن (sunnah): A recommended act that the Prophet consistently performed or encouraged, but not obligatory. Omission is not sinful but leaves one lacking in reward.
وقت مكروه (waqt makrūh): A time when it is disliked to pray nafl prayers, such as after Fajr until sunrise, after Asr until sunset, and at midday.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person enters the mosque after Asr prayer, what is the preferred action regarding tahiyyat al-masjid according to the Hanafi school?
A) He should pray two rak'ahs of tahiyyah
B) He should recite tasbih, tahlil, and send blessings on the Prophet
C) He should leave the mosque immediately
D) He should sit and not pray anything

Key Takeaway
Tahiyyat al-masjid is a sunnah performed before sitting, but it is not obligatory and can be substituted by other prayers or dhikr at disliked times.

Preference in Night Prayer: Many Rak'ahs vs Long Standing
Abu Yusuf's ruling on preferring many rak'ahs over long qiyam

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the preference between increasing rak'ahs and lengthening standing in night prayer, and apply the distinction based on whether a fixed recitation exists.

Core Idea
In night prayer, more rak'ahs are preferred if recitation is fixed; otherwise, longer standing is better.

This lesson examines a specific ruling by Imam Abu Yusuf regarding the optimal manner of performing night prayer (qiyam al-layl). The ruling distinguishes between two scenarios: when a person has a fixed portion of Qur'an to recite, and when they do not. Understanding this distinction helps in tailoring one's night prayer to maximize reward according to Hanafi fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
Read the passage and identify the two conditions described: having a fixed nightly recitation (ward) versus not having one.
The presence of a fixed recitation is the key variable.
2
State the preferred action for each scenario
For the first scenario (fixed recitation), Abu Yusuf says increasing the number of rak'ahs is better. For the second scenario (no fixed recitation), lengthening the standing (qiyam) is better.
3
Understand the rationale
The reasoning is that when recitation is fixed, the standing duration per rak'ah is limited. Increasing rak'ahs adds extra cycles of ruku' and sujud, which are highly rewarded. When no recitation is fixed, one can prolong the standing to recite more Qur'an, which is also virtuous.
The text explicitly states: 'because the standing does not differ in the first [rak'ahs] and to it is added the increase of bowing and prostration.'
4
Apply to practice
Consider a person who has a daily hizb (portion) to recite. According to this ruling, they should perform more rak'ahs with shorter recitations rather than a few long rak'ahs.
This ruling is from Abu Yusuf (nawadir) and is accepted in the Hanafi school as a recommended practice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يوسف رحمه الله تعالى فقال : إذا كان له ورد من الليل بقراءة من القرآن فالأفضل أن يكثر عدد الركعات، وإلا فطول القيام أفضل لأن القيام في الأول لا يختلف ويضم إليه زيادة الركوع والسجود.
Yusuf (Abu Yusuf), may Allah have mercy on him, said: If a person has a regular portion of the night for reciting some of the Qur'an, then it is better to increase the number of rak'ahs; otherwise, lengthening the standing is better, because the standing does not differ in the first [rak'ahs] and to it is added the increase of bowing and prostration.
Source pages p. 394

Commentary
This passage from Imam Abu Yusuf discusses the preferred manner of performing night prayer (qiyam al-layl). The author distinguishes two scenarios: if the worshipper has a fixed amount of Qur'an to recite during the night, then performing more rak'ahs with shorter recitations is preferable, as this adds extra prostrations (sujud). If there is no fixed recitation, then longer standing with more recitation is better. This ruling highlights a nuanced approach to balancing the benefits of extra sujud versus prolonged qiyam, and it is specific to the Hanafi school's emphasis on the virtues of prostration.

Key Terms
ورد (ward): A fixed or regular portion of recitation from the Qur'an that one habitually reads.
قيام (qiyam): The standing portion of prayer, specifically the recitation of Qur'an during the night prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Lengthen the standing (qiyam)
B) Increase the number of rak'ahs
C) Perform both equally
D) Shorten the prayer

Key Takeaway
The preference in night prayer depends on whether the worshipper has a fixed recitation: if yes, more rak'ahs; if no, longer standing, because adding rak'ahs adds extra ruku' and sujud.

intermediate

Tahiyyat al-Masjid: Greeting the Mosque
Complete ruling on tahiyyat al-masjid including exceptions and conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling of tahiyyat al-masjid, identify its exceptions (Masjid al-Haram, disliked times), and apply the substitute (tasbih) when prayer is not possible.

Core Idea
Tahiyyat al-masjid is a sunnah muakkadah that greets Allah, not the mosque, with specific exceptions and substitutes.

This lesson unpacks the Hanafi ruling on greeting the mosque upon entry. You'll learn that it is a recommended prayer (sunnah muakkadah) but with important conditions: it should be performed before sitting, not during disliked times, and the Sacred Mosque has a different greeting. When prayer is impossible due to impurity or prohibited time, remembrance of Allah suffices.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Recognize that the act is tahiyyat al-masjid – praying two rak'ahs upon entering a mosque. According to the Hanafi school, it is sunnah muakkadah (emphasized sunnah).
The ruling is derived from the hadith: 'When one of you enters the mosque, let him not sit until he prays two rak'ahs.'
2
Locate the dalil and its interpretation
The primary evidence is the prophetic command. Hanafis interpret the imperative as indicating sunnah, not obligation, due to other evidence showing it is not fard (e.g., permissible to leave it, substitute in makruh times).
The prohibition of sitting before praying is interpreted as dislike (tanzih), not haram.
3
Trace the exceptions
Apply the exception for Masjid al-Haram: its greeting is tawaf, not prayer. Also, note the restriction for disliked times (after Fajr and Asr): prayer is not offered; instead, recite tasbih.
If one cannot pray due to ritual impurity or other reason, the four tasbih phrases (SubhanAllah, Alhamdulillah, La ilaha illallah, Allahu Akbar) are said four times each.
4
Determine the preferred timing and multiplicity
The sunnah is to pray before sitting, though if one sits first, the greeting is still valid (but disliked). Two rak'ahs per day suffice for multiple entries, but some recommend greeting for each entry.
Two rak'ahs are better than four, but four are permissible.
5
Apply the ruling in practice
When entering any mosque (except Masjid al-Haram), offer two rak'ahs immediately if time permits and you are able. If it is after Fajr/Asr or you cannot pray, recite the four tasbih phrases.
For Masjid al-Haram, perform tawaf if you intend it; otherwise, pray two rak'ahs if you intend to sit.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (سن) تحية المسجد) أي تحية رب المسجد لأن التحية إنما تكون لصاحب المكان لا للمكان ويستثنى المسجد الحرام فإن تحيته المثلا الطواف وصرح علي: بأن من دخل المسجد الحرام لا يشتغل بتحية لأن تحية هذا المسجد الشريف هو الطواف لمن عليه طواف، أو أراده بخلاف من لم يرده، أو أراد أن يجلس فلا يجلس حتى يصلي ركعتين تحية المسجد .اهـ. قوله : ( بركعتين) وإن شاء بأربع والثنتان أفضل قهستاني قوله: (في غير وقت مكروه في القهستاني إذا دخل المسجد بعد الفجر، أو العصر لا يأتي بالتحية، بل يسبح ويهلل، ويصلي على النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم فإنه حينئذ يؤيدي حق المسجد كما إذا دخل للمكتوبة فإنه غير مأمور بها كما في التمرتاشي، اهـ، وفي الدر عن الضياء عن القوت من لم يتمكن منها لحدث، أو غيره يقول: كلمات التسبيح الأربع أربعاً اهـ وهي سبحان الله والحمد لله، ولا إله إلا الله والله أكبر . قوله : (قبل الجلوس) هذا بيان للأولى كما يأتي، وهذا قول العامة، وهو الصحيح، وقيل: يجلس أولاً، ثم يصلي. قوله: (وإن كان الأفضل فعلها قبله هذا يدل على أنهم حملوا النهي في حديث فلا يجلس حتى يركع ركعتين على التنزيه قوله : (يكفيه ركعتان في اليوم علله بعضهم بالحرج كما في الحموي على الأشباه، وقيل لكل دخول تحية لأنه معتبر بتحية الإنسان، فإنه يجيبه كلما لقيه كما في السراج
His saying: 'Sunnah is the greeting of the mosque' means the greeting of the Lord of the mosque, because greeting is only for the owner of the place, not the place. And the Sacred Mosque is exempted, for its greeting is tawaf by analogy. And 'Ali explicitly stated: whoever enters the Sacred Mosque should not occupy himself with tahiyya, because the greeting of this noble mosque is tawaf for one who has a tawaf to perform or intends it; as for one who does not intend it or intends to sit, he should not sit until he prays two rak'ahs of tahiyyat al-masjid. End. His saying: 'with two rak'ahs' though if he wishes he may do four, but two are better (Qahistani). His saying: 'in a disliked time' in Qahistani: if one enters the mosque after Fajr or Asr, he does not perform tahiyya, but rather glorifies, declares Allah's oneness, and sends blessings upon the Prophet, because then he fulfills the right of the mosque, just as when he enters for an obligatory prayer, he is not commanded to do it. So in al-Tamartashi. End. And in al-Durr from al-Diya' from al-Qut: he who is unable to pray due to ritual impurity or other reason says the four tasbih phrases four times. End. They are: Subhanallah, Alhamdulillah, La ilaha illallah, Allahu Akbar. His saying: 'before sitting' is a statement of what is better as follows. This is the view of the majority and it is correct. It is also said: he may sit first then pray. His saying: 'although it is better to do it before' indicates that they interpreted the prohibition in the hadith 'do not sit until you pray two rak'ahs' as indicating dislike (tanzih). His saying: 'two rak'ahs per day suffice for him' some explained it due to hardship, as in al-Hamawi on al-Ashbah. And it is said: for each entry there is a greeting, because it is considered like greeting a person: if one meets him multiple times, he greets each time, as in al-Siraj.
Source pages p. 394

Commentary
This passage from Tahtawi's Hashiya explains the ruling of Tahiyyat al-Masjid in detail. It clarifies that the greeting is for Allah, the Owner of the mosque, not the mosque itself. Masjid al-Haram is an exception; its greeting is tawaf, not prayer. However, if one does not intend tawaf or has already performed it, then two rak'ahs of tahiyya are recommended before sitting. The sunnah is two rak'ahs, though four are allowed. The prayer should not be performed during disliked times (after Fajr and Asr); instead, one should recite tasbih. If one cannot pray due to impurity, tasbih phrases (four times each) are a substitute. The preferred time to pray is before sitting, but the obligation is not lost if one sits first—the prohibition in the hadith is interpreted as disliked (tanzih), not haram. If a person enters the mosque multiple times, two rak'ahs per day are sufficient, though some say each entry requires a separate greeting.

Key Terms
تحية المسجد (tahiyyat al-masjid): A voluntary prayer of two rak'ahs offered upon entering a mosque, intended as a greeting to Allah.
تنزيه (tanzih): Interpreting a prohibition as indicating dislike (makruh tanzihi) rather than prohibition (haram).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the substitute for tahiyyat al-masjid if one enters the mosque during a disliked time?
A) Recite istighfar
B) Recite the four tasbih phrases four times
C) Sit and wait
D) Perform tawaf

Key Takeaway
Tahiyyat al-masjid is a sunnah muakkadah, preferably offered before sitting, with exceptions for Makkah (tawaf), disliked times (tasbih), and inability to pray (tasbih).

Recommended Acts: Mosque Supplications and Post-Wudu Prayer
Ruling with proof on two recommended acts

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the recommended supplications for mosque entry/exit, explain the post-wudu dua prayer's reward, and identify the condition of offering it before the limbs dry.

Core Idea
Two rak'ahs after wudu before limbs dry make Paradise obligatory.

This passage from the classical Hashiya outlines two beautiful recommended practices: specific supplications upon entering and leaving the mosque, and a quick two-rak'ah prayer after wudu. These actions are sunnah ghayr mu'akkadah, bringing immense reward. The key detail is the time constraint—'before the limbs dry'—which highlights the immediacy of this devotion.

Guided Path
1
Identify the acts and their rulings
The text states two acts: (1) saying a specific dua when entering and leaving the mosque, (2) praying two rak'ahs after wudu. Both are recommended (mandub).
Ruling level: sunnah ghayr mu'akkadah for both.
2
Locate the dalil for each act
For the supplications, the proof is the command of the Prophet (ﷺ). For the two rak'ahs, the hadith from Muslim: 'There is no Muslim who performs wudu and does it well, then stands and prays two rak'ahs with his heart present except that Paradise becomes obligatory for him.'
The hadith is ahad, hence zanni al-thubut, but sufficient for mandub.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The hadith explicitly promises Paradise for this specific action, indicating great merit. The phrase 'before it dries' (qabla jafafih) is derived from the context of immediacy, though not explicitly in this hadith; it is mentioned by the author as a condition for the recommended time.
The condition of 'before jafaf' is a time recommendation, not a validity condition.
4
Note the ikhtilaf (if any)
There is no significant dispute among the schools on the recommendation. All agree it is a meritorious act. The Hanafi position is clear that it is sunnah ghayr mu'akkadah.
Some might think it is wajib due to the promise of Paradise, but the Hanafi principle is that ahad hadith imply wujub only if there is no contradicting evidence; here the context shows it is a reward for a recommended act.
5
Identify the conditions and pillars
For the post-wudu prayer, the only condition specified is that it be offered before the limbs dry (jafuf). This is not a pillar of the prayer itself but a recommended time frame. The prayer itself is a regular nafl of two rak'ahs.
If delayed after drying, the prayer is still valid as nafl but loses the specific reward.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ندب أن يقول عند دخول المسجد : اللهم افتح لي أبواب رحمتك، وعند خروجه: اللهم إني أسألك فضلك، من [؟] لأمر النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم به وندب ركعتان بعد الوضوء قبل جفافه لقوله : ما من مسلم يتوضا فيحسن وضوأه، ثم يقوم فيصلي ركعتين يقبل عليهما بقلبه إلا وجبت له الجنة رواه مسلم
It is recommended that upon entering the mosque he says: O Allah, open for me the doors of Your mercy, and upon leaving: O Allah, I ask You of Your bounty, from [؟] due to the command of the Prophet ﷺ. And two rak'ahs after wudu before it dries are recommended due to his saying: 'There is no Muslim who performs wudu and does it well, then stands and prays two rak'ahs with his heart present except that Paradise becomes obligatory for him.' Narrated by Muslim.
Source pages p. 394

Commentary
This passage specifies two recommended acts. First, upon entering the mosque, one should recite a supplication asking for Allah's mercy; upon leaving, ask for His bounty, based on the Prophet's practice. Second, it is recommended (mandub) to pray two rak'ahs immediately after completing wudu, before the limbs dry. The hadith from Muslim promises Paradise for those who do this with concentration. This prayer is separate from tahiyyat al-masjid and can be performed at any time, though if one enters the mosque after wudu, a single prayer can fulfill both intentions.

Key Terms
جفوف (jufuf): Drying of the limbs after wudu; the prayer should be offered before the washed parts dry.
ندب (nadb): Recommended (mandub) – an act whose performance is rewarded and omission is not punishable.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The post-wudu prayer before jafaf brings the promise of Paradise, but it remains a recommended act, not obligatory.

The Ruling and Proofs of Salat al-Duha
Ruling on salat al-duha with proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on salat al-duha, identify its number of rak'ahs and time, and explain the basis of the recommendation using the hadith evidence.

Core Idea
Salat al-duha is recommended (mandub) with four rak'ahs, based on the Prophet's consistent practice and confirmed by multiple hadiths.

Salat al-duha, the forenoon prayer, is a voluntary prayer that many Muslims perform. This passage clarifies the Hanafi position on its ruling, number of rak'ahs, and preferred time. It also addresses a scholarly difference on whether one should be constant upon it. By studying this passage, you will learn the evidence and the stronger view within the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The text states that duha prayer is 'recommended (mandub) on the stronger view' (ala al-rajih). This indicates a definitive Hanafi position that it is mustahabb, not wajib.
The phrase 'ala al-rajih' shows that the author is presenting the preferred view after considering differences.
2
Locate the dalil
The evidence comes from the practice of the Prophet (peace be upon him) as narrated by Aisha: he used to pray four rak'ahs of duha and increase as he wished. Additionally, a hadith from Tabarani permits up to twelve rak'ahs, and a hadith from Muslim names it 'prayer of the awwabin' at the time when young camels feel heat.
All hadiths are ahad (single-transmitter), thus providing zanni al-thubut, but sufficient to establish recommendation.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The Prophet's actual practice (f‌iʿl) indicates desirability. The hadith about increasing 'as he wishes' shows that more than four is permissible. The timing hadith specifies the preferred moment.
Hanafi usul holds that the Prophet's actions (except those specific to him) indicate recommendation (mandub) unless there is evidence of obligation.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Scholars differed on whether it is better to be constant upon duha daily. The text says the apparent view (al-zahir) is that constancy is better, citing the hadith 'The most beloved of actions to Allah is the one in which the doer is constant, even if it is little.' There is also an intra-Hanafi difference on whether duha is recommended at all.
Author takes the view that constancy enhances the virtue, but even without constancy the prayer is valid and rewardable.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The author states the ruling as 'on the stronger view' (ala al-rajih) and concludes with the minimum of two rak'ahs from al-Durr, confirming that the recommended practice is at least two, optimally four.
The tarjih relies on the strength of the evidence (multiple hadiths) and the weight of scholarly opinion.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ندب صلاة الضحى على الراجح وهي أربع ركعات لما روينا قريباً عن عائشة رضي الله عنها أنه عليه السلام كان يصلي الضحى أربع ركعات ويزيد ما شاء فلذا قلنا ندب أربع فصاعداً في وقت الضحى وابتداؤه من ارتفاع الشمس إلى قبيل زوالها فيزيد على الأربع إلى ثنتي عشرة ركعة لما روى الطبراني في الكبير عن أبي الدرداء قال : قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم : [الحديث] واختلف العلماء هل الأفضل المواظبة عليها أولا والظاهر الأول لحديث أحب العمل إلى الله تعالى ما داوم عليه صاحبه وإن قل، وروي أنه أمر أن يقرأ في صلاة الضحى بالشمس وضحاها ،والضحي، وتمامه في شرح البدر العيني على البخاري. قوله: (وابتداؤه من إرتفاع الشمس) ووقتها المختار إذا مضى ربع النهار لحديث زيد بن أرقم أن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم قال : صلاة الأوابين حين ترمض الفصال) رواه مسلم وترمض بفتح التاء، والميم أي تبرك من شدة الحر في أخفافها قوله إلى ثنتي عشرة ركعة وفي الدو عن المنية أقلها ركعتان
The forenoon prayer (salat al-duha) is recommended on the stronger view. It is four rak'ahs, based on what we narrated recently from Aisha - may Allah be pleased with her - that the Prophet ﷺ used to pray four rak'ahs of duha and increase as he wished, so we said that four and above are recommended. Its time begins from sunrise to just before noon. He may increase from four to twelve rak'ahs due to what al-Tabarani narrated in al-Kabir from Abu al-Darda' who said: The Messenger of Allah ﷺ said: [hadith]. The scholars differed on whether it is better to be constant upon it or not. The apparent view is the first, due to the hadith: 'The most beloved of actions to Allah is the one in which the doer is constant, even if it is little.' And it is narrated that he ordered to recite in duha prayer Surah al-Shams and al-Duha. And its completion is in Sharh al-Badr al-'Ayni 'ala al-Bukhari. His saying: 'its beginning is from the rising of the sun' and its preferred time is when a quarter of the day has passed, due to the hadith of Zayd ibn Arqam that the Messenger of Allah ﷺ said: 'The prayer of the awwabin (repentant) is when the young camels feel the heat of the sun' - narrated by Muslim. 'Tarmad' means they lie down from intense heat on their hooves. His saying: 'up to twelve rak'ahs' and in al-Durr from al-Munya: its minimum is two rak'ahs.
Source pages p. 395

Commentary
This passage discusses salat al-duha, the forenoon prayer. The author affirms that it is recommended (mandub) on the more correct view. The default number is four rak'ahs, based on the practice of the Prophet as reported by Aisha, but one may increase up to twelve. The time begins after sunrise and lasts until just before noon, with the preferred time being after a quarter of the day (when the sun is high and hot). There is a scholarly difference on whether it is better to be constant in performing it daily; the stronger view is that continuity is better (to maintain the habit). The minimum according to some sources is two rak'ahs. The recitation in duha prayer is recommended to include Surah al-Shams (91) and Surah al-Duha (93).

Key Terms
صلاة الضحى (salat al-duha): A voluntary prayer performed after sunrise until before noon, recommended with four rak'ahs.
الأوابين (al-awwabin): A name for salat al-duha when performed in the late morning; the time when young camels feel heat.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Salat al-duha is recommended (mandub) in the Hanafi school, with four rak'ahs as the norm, based on the Prophet's practice and additional hadiths allowing up to twelve.

Duas for Mosque Entry/Exit and Two Rak'ahs After Wudu
Commentary on recommended practices with hadith proofs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the recommended (nadb) acts of dua when entering/leaving the mosque and the two rak'ahs after wudu, and explain the prophetic proofs for them.

Core Idea
Duas upon entering/leaving mosque and two rak'ahs after wudu are recommended acts with strong prophetic merit but not obligatory.

This lesson explores two beautiful sunnan: the specific duas for entering and leaving the mosque, and the two-rak'ah prayer performed immediately after wudu. The commentator draws on authentic hadiths to demonstrate their virtue while clarifying that they fall under the category of recommendation (nadb), not obligation. Understanding these proofs reinforces our love for the Prophet's practice and encourages us to seize these rewards without legal overburden.

Guided Path
1
Identify the acts and their rulings
Read the passage and list the three practices: dua on entering mosque, dua on leaving mosque, and two rak'ahs after wudu. The text explicitly says they are 'nadb' (recommended).
Nadb is a Hanafi category below sunnah muakkadah.
2
Locate the dalil for each act
For the duas, the commentary cites Quran 62:10 for 'seeking bounty'. For the two rak'ahs, hadith from Muslim (and later Bukhari via Bilal) provide the proof.
The hadith from Muslim directly mentions the two rak'ahs.
3
Analyse the wajh al-dalalah
The dalil for the two rak'ahs uses a promise of Paradise but not a direct imperative. According to Hanafi usul, such a promise indicates great reward but not obligation (wujub). Hence, the ruling is nadb.
The hadith is ahad, so even if it were imperative, it could not impose fard; here it's a promise, not a command.
4
Understand the commentary expansions
The commentary explains that the same virtue is attained even if one prays an obligatory prayer after wudu, and that 'with his heart present' means awareness of Allah's greatness. It also notes a minority opinion that 'two rak'ahs suffice for the day' due to hardship.
These expansions show the depth of Hanafi fiqh in deriving rulings.

Book of Prayer. O Allah, open for me the doors of Your mercy, and upon leaving: O Allah, I ask You of Your bounty. And two rak'ahs after wudu before it dries are recommended because of the command of the Prophet, peace be upon him: 'There is no Muslim who performs wudu well, then stands and prays two rak'ahs with his heart present in them except that Paradise becomes obligatory for him' - narrated by Muslim. Regarding the word of abrogation: his saying: 'Two rak'ahs suffice for the day' - some explained it due to hardship, as in al-Hamawi on al-Ashbah. And it is said: for every entry there is a greeting because it is analogous to greeting a person, for he responds every time he meets him, as in al-Siraj. His saying: 'And it is recommended' i.e., after mentioning prayer upon the Prophet, as the hadiths indicate. His saying: 'O Allah open for me the doors of Your mercy' i.e., Your benevolence and favor with sincerity, acceptance, and so on. His saying: 'O Allah I ask You of Your bounty' is taken from His saying: 'Then when the prayer is concluded, disperse through the land and seek of the bounty of Allah' [al-Jumu'ah:62]. His saying: 'Because of his saying, peace be upon him, etc.' And from Abu Huraira, may Allah be pleased with him, that the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, said to Bilal: 'O Bilal, tell me the most hopeful deed you have done in Islam, for I have heard the sound of your sandals before me in Paradise.' He said: 'I have not done any deed more hopeful than that I never performed purification at any time of night or day but that I prayed with that purification whatever was written for me to pray.' Narrated by al-Bukhari. And 'ad-daff' with fath the sound of the sandal while walking, as in al-Halabi. And in Sharh al-Mishkat: from the important letter dal, and tashdid of fa, the book of purification: if one prays an obligatory prayer after wudu, he obtains this virtue just as the greeting of the mosque is obtained by that, end. His saying: 'He turns to them with his heart' such that he brings to mind the greatness of Allah. His saying: 'Except that Paradise becomes obligatory for him' i.e., it is confirmed.
Source pages p. 395

Commentary
This passage from Hashiya Al-Tahtawi is a commentary on the matn of Maraqi al-Falah. It covers two recommended acts: (1) the duas upon entering and leaving the mosque, and (2) the two rak'ahs after wudu. The author first cites a hadith from Muslim that whoever performs wudu well and prays two rak'ahs with full presence of heart, Paradise becomes obligatory for him. The commentary then explains the phrase 'two rak'ahs suffice for the day' as either due to hardship or as a greeting for entering. It then discusses the dua 'O Allah open for me the doors of Your mercy' and explains that it refers to divine favor. The long hadith of Bilal from Bukhari is also cited, where Bilal mentions that his hope rests on praying after every wudu. The commentary clarifies that the reward applies even if one prays an obligatory prayer after wudu. Finally, it explains that 'with his heart present' means bringing to mind the greatness of Allah, and 'Paradise becomes obligatory' means it is confirmed for him. The overall ruling is that these acts are recommended (nadb) in the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
ندب (nadb): A recommended act, not obligatory. The text uses 'nadb' to indicate the ruling.
ركعتان بعد الوضوء (rak'atan ba'da al-wudu): Two units of prayer performed after completing wudu, before the water dries.
تحية المسجد (tahiyyat al-masjid): Greeting of the mosque, two rak'ahs upon entering. The text analogizes the two rak'ahs after wudu to this.

Salat al-Duha: Ruling, Number, Time, and Virtues
Details the recommended forenoon prayer, its preferred number, time, and virtues.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling of salat al-duha, explain the preferred number of rak'ahs with evidence, identify its preferred time, and list its virtues.

Core Idea
Salat al-duha is a recommended prayer; four rak'ahs are preferred, but two to twelve are permissible.

The Hanafi school, following the majority of hadith scholars, holds that salat al-duha is a recommended (mandub) prayer. While some scholars questioned its recommendation, the preferred view is that it is a sunnah ghayr muakkadah. This lesson unpacks the ruling, the evidence for four rak'ahs, the optimal time, and the virtues narrated from the Prophet (peace be upon him).

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Salat al-duha is a voluntary prayer prayed in the forenoon. According to the preferred Hanafi view, it is recommended (mandub) – not obligatory.
The text says 'wa qila ghayru mandubah' indicating a minority view that it is not recommended.
2
Examine the proof for the number
Al-Hakim reports that reliable hadith scholars chose four rak'ahs due to tawatur of authentic reports. The Prophet's consistent practice was to pray four, but he could increase.
The dalil is the hadith 'He used to pray four rak'ahs of duha and increase as he wished.'
3
Analyze the time specification
The time begins from sunrise; the preferred time is when a quarter of the day has passed, based on the hadith of Zaid ibn Arqam about the prayer of al-awwabin.
The hadith 'when the young camels feel the heat' indicates the middle of the forenoon.
4
Review the flexibility and virtues
The minimum is two rak'ahs, the preferred is four, and one may go up to twelve. Each number carries increasing rewards as narrated in a hadith.
The virtues include not being written among the heedless, being among the worshippers, etc.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : وندب صلاة الضحى) الضحوة إرتفاع النهار، والضحى بالضم، والقصر فوق ذلك وبالفتح والمد إذا علت الشمس إلى ربع السماء. قوله: (على الراجح) وقيل غير مندوبة قوله : (وهي أربع ) قال الحاكم: صحبت جماعة . أئمة الحديث الحفاظ من الأثبات، فوجدتهم يختارون الأربع لتواتر الأخبار الصحيحة فيها وإليها أذهب فقد روي في قوله تعالى : وإبراهيم الذي وفي قال : أتدرون ما وفي ؟ وفى عمل يومه بأربع ركعات الضحى واختلف العلماء هل الأفضل المواظبة عليها أولا والظاهر الأول لحديث أحب العمل إلى الله تعالى ما داوم عليه صاحبه وإن قل، وروي أنه أمر أن يقرأ في صلاة الضحى بالشمس وضحاها ،والضحي، وتمامه في شرح البدر العيني على البخاري. قوله: (وابتداؤه من إرتفاع الشمس) ووقتها المختار إذا مضى ربع النهار لحديث زيد بن أرقم أن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم قال : صلاة الأوابين حين ترمض الفصال) رواه مسلم وترمض بفتح التاء، والميم أي تبرك من شدة الحر في أخفافها قوله إلى ثنتي عشرة ركعة وفي الدو عن المنية أقلها ركعتان، من صلي الضحى ركعتين لم يكتب من الغافلين ومن صلى أربعاً كتب من العابدين ومن كفي . ذلك اليوم ومن صلى ثمانياً كتبه الله تعالى من القانتين ومن صلى اثنتي عشرة ركعة بنى الله له بيتاً في الجنة
His saying: 'And the forenoon prayer is recommended (according to the preferred view).' Adh-dhuha means the elevation of the day; ad-duha (with damm and qasr) is above that; and with fath and madd when the sun has risen to a quarter of the sky. His saying: 'According to the preferred view' - and it is said it is not recommended. His saying: 'And it is four (rak'ahs).' Al-Hakim said: I accompanied a group of imams of hadith, reliable preservers, and I found them choosing four due to the tawatur of authentic reports on it, and I adopt that. It is narrated concerning His saying: 'And Ibrahim who fulfilled' - he said: Do you know what 'fulfilled' meant? He fulfilled the work of his day with four rak'ahs of duha. The scholars differed on whether it is better to be constant upon it or not, and the apparent is the first due to the hadith: 'The most beloved action to Allah is that which its doer does constantly, even if it is small.' And it is narrated that he commanded to recite in the duha prayer 'By the sun and its brightness' and 'Ad-Duha'. Its completion is in Sharh al-Badr al-Ayni on al-Bukhari. His saying: 'And its beginning is from the rising of the sun.' Its chosen time is when a quarter of the day has passed, due to the hadith of Zaid ibn Arqam that the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, said: 'The prayer of the penitent (al-awwabin) is when the young camels feel the heat of the sun' - narrated by Muslim. 'Tarmadu' with fath of ta and mim means they kneel due to intense heat on their hooves. His saying: 'Up to twelve rak'ahs' - and in al-Daw' and al-Minya, its minimum is two rak'ahs. Whoever prays two rak'ahs of duha is not written among the heedless; whoever prays four is written among the worshippers; and whoever prays eight, Allah writes him among the devout; and whoever prays twelve rak'ahs, Allah builds for him a house in Paradise.
Source pages p. 395

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the matn statement that salat al-duha is recommended (nadb) according to the preferred view. The author (al-Tahtawi) explains the linguistic meaning of 'duha' and then discusses the ruling. He mentions that some said it is not recommended, but the preferred view is that it is recommended. The preferred number of rak'ahs is four, based on the strong practice of the Prophet (peace be upon him) as reported by Aisha and others. Al-Hakim attests to the tawatur of reports supporting four rak'ahs. The commentary also mentions a report linking Ibrahim (peace be upon him) to four rak'ahs of duha. There is discussion on whether constant practice is better, and the hadith about loving consistent actions supports constancy. The time for duha begins from sunrise to just before noon, with the preferred time being after a quarter of the day has passed, as indicated by the hadith of Zaid ibn Arqam about the prayer of al-awwabin (the penitent). The commentary then notes that the number of rak'ahs can be increased up to twelve, with the minimum being two. The virtues of different numbers are listed from a hadith (narrated by al-Tabarani): two rak'ahs spare one from heedlessness, four make one among worshippers, eight among the devout, and twelve earn a house in Paradise. The overall ruling: salat al-duha is a recommended act with flexible numbers, four being the preferred.

Key Terms
الضحى (al-duha): The forenoon, from sunrise to just before noon. The text distinguishes different linguistic forms.
مندوبة (mandubah): Recommended (synonym of nadb). The text says 'wa qila ghayru mandubah' meaning some said it is not recommended.
الأوابين (al-awwabin): Those who frequently repent; the prayer at the time when young camels feel heat is called the prayer of the penitent.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) 2
B) 4
C) 8
D) 12

Key Takeaway
Salat al-duha is a recommended sunnah prayer; four rak'ahs are preferred, prayed after a quarter of the day, with great virtues for those who pray it regularly.

Salah — Prayer

The Night Prayer: Recommendation, Rak'ahs, and Virtue
Ruling with proof and dispute resolution

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on salat al-layl, identify its preferred time, and explain the minimum recommended rak'ahs.

Core Idea
Night prayer is recommended, not obligatory—its minimum is eight rak'ahs, best in the last sixth.

The night prayer (tahajjud) holds immense virtue, yet its legal status is often misunderstood. This lesson clarifies that according to the Hanafi school, it is a recommended (mandub) act, not an obligation. We also explore the preferred time and the minimum number of rak'ahs that one should pray, drawing from the text of Hashiya al-Tahtawi.

Guided Path
1
Establish the ruling
Identify that the text states 'Wa nudiba salat al-layl'—night prayer is recommended. Understand the term 'nadb' and its place in Hanafi fiqh (less than sunnah muakkadah).
The matn uses 'nadb' explicitly, which the hashiah affirms.
2
Determine the best time
Note 'khususaan akhirahu'—especially its last part. The hashiah specifies this as the fifth sixth of the night, when divine descent occurs.
This is based on hadith about Allah's descent to the lowest heaven.
3
Analyze the recommended rak'ahs
The text says 'aql ma yanbaghi an yatanaqqala bi-layli thamanu rak'at'—the minimum one should pray is eight. Note the alternative view from al-Hawi al-Qudsi (minimum two, maximum eight).
The hashiah reconciles by stating eight is recommended, but less is permissible.
4
Review the virtue
The text quotes Quran 32:17 about hidden joy. Understand that the virtue is immense, but the lesson focuses on the ruling, not the details of reward.
This encourages the practice without affecting the legal classification.

وندب صلاة الليل خصوصاً آخره كما ذكرناه وأقل ما ينبغي أن ينتقل بالليل ثمان ركعات كذا في الجوهرة، وفضلها لا يحصر قال تعالى: ﴿فلا تعلم نفس ما أخفي لهم من قرة أعين﴾ [السجدة/17] قوله: (وأما أكثرها فبقوله فقط قال : وهذا لو صلى الأكثر بسلام واحد أما لو فصل فكلما زاد فهو أفضل كما أفاده ابن حجر في شرح البخاري ،اهـ ولعل هذا على مذهب الشافعي، وإلا فالزيادة على أربع في نفل النهار مكروهة عندنا قوله : (لما روى الطبراني الخ) وروى يقول الله : ابن آدم اضمن لي ركعتين من أول النهار أكفك آخره، وروى يقول الله تعالى : يا ابن آدم اكفني أول النهار بأربع ركعات أكفك بهن آخر يومك ، وروي مقام الصدقات التي على كل مفصل من بني آدم وهي ثلثمائة وستون مفصلاً. قوله: (كفى ذلك اليوم) أي مع حصول الفضيلتين السابقتين وكذا يقال فيما بعد قوله : ( وندب صلاة الليل الخ) ذهب طائفة من العلماء وعليه الأصوليون من مشايخنا إلى أن قيام الليل فرض عليه تمسكوا بقوله تعالى: قم الليل إلا قليلاً) [المزمل / ۷۳] وعلى هذا فتكون صلاة الليل مندوبة لأن الأدلة القولية فيه إنما تفيد الندب، وقال طائفة : كان تطوعاً منه ، فيكون في حقنا سنة لقوله تعالى : ومن الليل فتهجد به نافلة لك وأجاب الأولون قالوا: لا منافاة لأن المراد بالنافلة الزائدة أي زائدة على ما فرض على غيرك، وربما يعطي التقييد بالمجرور ذلك، وفي تفسير ابن عباس : قم الليل يعني كله إلا قليلاً فاشتد ذلك على النبي ، وعلى أصحابه، وقاموا الليل كله، ولم يعرفوا ما حد القليل، فأنزل الله تعالى نصفه أو أنقص منه قليلاً، أو زد النصف إلى الثلث أو زد عليه إلى الثلثين خيره بين هذه المنازل فإشتد ذلك أيضاً على النبي ، وعلى أصحابه فقاموا الليل كله حتى انتفخت أقدامهم مخافة أن لا يحفظوا القدر الواجب، فعلوا ذلك سنة فأنزل الله تعالى ناسختها فقال : علم أن لن تحصوه يعني قيام الليل من الثلث والنصف ،والثلثين، وكان هذا قبل أن تفرض الصلوات الخمس، فلما فرضت الصلوات الخمس نسخت هذه كما نسخت الزكاة كل صدقة، وصوم رمضان كل صوم اهـ وفي تفسير الجزري نسخ وجوب التقدير بقوله تعالى : علم أن لن تحصوه فتاب عليكم فاقرؤا ما تيسر أي صلوا ما تيسر من الصلاة ولو قدر حلب شاة، ثم نسخ وجوب قيام الليل بالصلوات الخمس بعد سنة أخرى فكان بين الوجوب، والتخفيف سنة وبين الوجوب، والنسخ سنتان كذا في العيني على البخاري قوله: (خصوصاً آخره) وهو السدس الخامس من أسداس الليل، وهو الوقت الذي ورد فيه النزول الإلهي . قوله : (وأقل ما ينبغي أن يتنقل بالليل ثمان ركعات الذي في الحاوي القدسي أن أقله ركعتان وأكثره ثمان لما روي عليه يعني أنقص من
And the night prayer is recommended, especially its latter part as we mentioned. The minimum that one should pray at night is eight rak'ahs, as in al-Jawhara. Its virtue cannot be counted; Allah says: 'No soul knows what joy is hidden for them' [as-Sajda:17]. His saying: 'As for its maximum, it is by his saying only.' He said: This is if one prays the maximum with one taslim; but if he separates them, then every increase is better, as Ibn Hajar stated in Sharh al-Bukhari, end. Perhaps this is according to the Shafi'i school; otherwise, increasing beyond four in daytime voluntary prayer is disliked (makruh) according to us. His saying: 'As narrated by al-Tabarani, etc.' And it is narrated that Allah says: 'O son of Adam, guarantee Me two rak'ahs at the beginning of the day, and I will suffice you at its end.' And it is narrated that Allah says: 'O son of Adam, suffice Me at the beginning of the day with four rak'ahs, and I will suffice you with them at the end of your day.' And it is narrated in place of the charities on every joint of the children of Adam, and they are three hundred and sixty joints. His saying: 'That suffices for the day' i.e., along with the attainment of the two previous virtues, and likewise is said later. His saying: 'And the night prayer is recommended, etc.' A group of scholars, including our usul scholars, held that qiyam al-layl was obligatory upon him (the Prophet), adhering to His saying: 'Stand the night except a little' [al-Muzzammil:73]. On this basis, the night prayer is recommended because the verbal evidences only indicate recommendation. Another group said: It was voluntary for him, so it is a sunnah for us, due to His saying: 'And from the night, perform tahajjud as an additional (nafilah) for you' [al-Isra:79]. The first group responded: There is no contradiction, because nafilah means additional (za'idah), i.e., additional to what was prescribed for others. And perhaps the restriction with the preposition (lak) indicates that. In the tafsir of Ibn Abbas: 'Stand the night' means all of it except a little, and this was hard upon the Prophet and his companions, and they stood the whole night, not knowing the limit of 'little'. Then Allah sent down: 'Half of it, or reduce it a little, or add to it' giving him choice among these stations. That was also hard upon the Prophet and his companions, so they stood the whole night until their feet swelled, fearing they would not maintain the obligatory amount. They did that for a year. Then Allah sent down its abrogator, saying: 'He knows that you cannot be precise' meaning standing the night from the third, half, and two-thirds. This was before the five prayers were prescribed. When the five prayers were prescribed, this abrogated that, just as zakat abrogated every charity, and Ramadan fasting every fast, end. In the tafsir of al-Jazari, the obligation of estimation was abrogated by His saying: 'He knows that you cannot be precise, so He has turned to you (in mercy); so recite what is easy of it' i.e., pray what is easy of prayer, even if it is the amount of milking a goat. Then the obligation of qiyam al-layl was abrogated by the five prayers after another year. So there was one year between obligation and alleviation, and two years between obligation and abrogation, as in al-Ayni on al-Bukhari. His saying: 'Especially its latter part' which is the fifth sixth of the night, and it is the time when the divine descent occurs. His saying: 'And the minimum that one should pray at night is eight rak'ahs' - in al-Hawi al-Qudsi, its minimum is two rak'ahs and its maximum is eight, as narrated from him, meaning less than.
Source pages p. 396

Commentary
This passage from Hashiya Al-Tahtawi covers the night prayer (salat al-layl) from several angles. It begins by stating that the night prayer is recommended (nadb), especially its latter part (the last sixth of the night, when divine descent is reported). The minimum recommended number of rak'ahs is eight according to al-Jawhara, but the text notes that in al-Hawi al-Qudsi the minimum is two and maximum eight. The virtue of night prayer is immense, as indicated by Quranic verse [as-Sajda:17]. The commentator then addresses a typical objection: if one prays more than eight, is it better? The response distinguishes methods: if done with one taslim (continuous), it may be disliked for daytime voluntary but not for night; but if one separates them (with taslim after every two rak'ahs), increase is better. This point is said to be based on the Shafi'i school, as in the Hanafi school increasing beyond four in daytime nafil is disliked. The text then narrates hadiths about the virtues of praying two or four rak'ahs at the beginning of the day (these are for duha, but included here for contrast? Actually they are separate). Then the main dispute: a group of scholars, including Hanafi usul scholars (al-usuliyyun min mashayikhina), held that qiyam al-layl was obligatory (fard) upon the Prophet based on the command 'Stand the night except a little' [al-Muzzammil:73]. According to this view, the night prayer for the Ummah is still recommended (nadb) because the verbal evidences for obligation only apply to the Prophet. Another group held it was voluntary for the Prophet and thus a sunnah for us, citing 'And from the night, perform tahajjud as an additional (nafilah) for you' [al-Isra:79]. The first group responds that nafilah here means 'additional' to what was prescribed for others, not that it was voluntary. The commentary then explains the historical process of abrogation: first, the obligation of standing the night was estimated (with options), then it was eased to a general 'recite what is easy', and finally abrogated by the five daily prayers after two years. The text thus concludes that the operative ruling (mufta bihi) is that the night prayer is recommended (nadb), not obligatory. The hashiah here refines the understanding by clarifying the dispute and settling on the non-obligatory status.

Key Terms
قيام الليل (qiyam al-layl): Standing (praying) at night, synonymous with salat al-layl. The text discusses whether it was obligatory on the Prophet.
نافلة (nafilah): Additional, supererogatory. In the verse, it is interpreted by some as 'additional' to what is prescribed for others, not merely voluntary.
مندوبة (mandubah): Recommended. The text concludes that the night prayer is mandubah (nadb).
تطوع (tatawwu'): Voluntary act of worship. In the dispute, some scholars described the night prayer as tatawwu' for the Prophet.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what is the minimum number of rak'ahs recommended for the night prayer?
A) 2
B) 4
C) 8
D) 12

Key Takeaway
The night prayer is recommended (mandub) in the Hanafi school, with the best time being the last part of the night and the minimum recommended rak'ahs being eight.

Was Qiyam al-Layl Obligatory on the Prophet? The Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute with proofs and abrogation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the two Hanafi opinions on whether qiyam al-layl was obligatory on the Prophet and analyze the proofs and abrogation narrative presented by al-Tahtawi.

Core Idea
Qiyam al-layl on the Prophet: abrogated obligation or voluntary sunnah? Both views agree on recommendation for us.

A fascinating intra-Hanafi dispute concerns the status of the night prayer for the Prophet himself. Was it an obligation lifted only from him? Or was it always voluntary? This lesson dissects the two positions, their Quranic proofs, and the historical sequence of abrogation presented in Hashiya al-Tahtawi. Understanding this debate sharpens one's appreciation for how Hanafi scholars handle scriptural commands.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two positions
The text mentions two groups: 'ta'ifatun min al-'ulama' (a group of scholars) who said qiyam al-layl was fard upon the Prophet, and 'ta'ifatun' who said it was tatawwu' (voluntary). Understand that both are within the Hanafi school.
The first group includes 'al-usuliyyun min mashayikhina' (our Hanafi usul scholars).
2
Analyze the first proof
The first group uses the imperative 'qum al-layla illa qalilan' (al-Muzzammil:2). In Hanafi usul, commands indicate obligation (al-amr yufidu al-wujub). This was initially binding on the Prophet.
The obligation was later abrogated, but the proof shows it was once fard.
3
Analyze the second proof
The second group uses 'wa min al-layli fatahajjad bihi nafilatan lak' (al-Isra:79). The word 'nafilah' typically means voluntary or extra. They argue it was voluntary for him, so it is a sunnah for us.
The first group responds that 'nafilah' means 'additional' to what others are obliged with.
4
Examine the abrogation narrative
The text provides a detailed tafsir from Ibn Abbas and al-Jazari: initial obligation, then easing, then final abrogation by the five daily prayers after two years. This supports the view of an original obligation that was lifted.
Abrogation (naskh) is a key usul principle here.
5
Resolve the dispute
Both groups agree on the final ruling for the Ummah: the night prayer is recommended (nadb). The hashiah sides with the recommendation and uses the abrogation narrative to explain why obligation was repealed.
The thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence) is minimal for the Ummah.

فقط قال : وهذا لو صلى الأكثر بسلام واحد أما لو فصل فكلما زاد فهو أفضل كما أفاده ابن حجر في شرح البخاري ،اهـ ولعل هذا على مذهب الشافعي، وإلا فالزيادة على أربع في نفل النهار مكروهة عندنا قوله : (لما روى الطبراني الخ) وروى يقول الله : ابن آدم اضمن لي ركعتين من أول النهار أكفك آخره، وروى يقول الله تعالى : يا ابن آدم اكفني أول النهار بأربع ركعات أكفك بهن آخر يومك ، وروي مقام الصدقات التي على كل مفصل من الليل فرض عليه تمسكوا بقوله تعالى: قم الليل إلا قليلاً) [المزمل / ۷۳] وعلى هذا فتكون صلاة الليل مندوبة لأن الأدلة القولية فيه إنما تفيد الندب، وقال طائفة : كان تطوعاً منه ، فيكون في حقنا سنة لقوله تعالى : ومن الليل فتهجد به نافلة لك وأجاب الأولون قالوا: لا منافاة لأن المراد بالنافلة الزائدة أي زائدة على ما فرض على غيرك، وربما يعطي التقييد بالمجرور ذلك، وفي تفسير ابن عباس : قم الليل يعني كله إلا ذلك أيضاً على النبي ، وعلى أصحابه فقاموا الليل كله حتى انتفخت أقدامهم مخافة أن لا يحفظوا القدر الواجب، فعلوا ذلك سنة فأنزل الله تعالى ناسختها فقال : علم أن لن تحصوه يعني قيام الليل من الثلث والنصف ،والثلثين، وكان هذا قبل أن تفرض الصلوات الخمس، فلما فرضت الصلوات الخمس نسخت هذه كما نسخت الزكاة كل صدقة، وصوم رمضان كل صوم اهـ وفي تفسير الجزري نسخ وجوب التقدير بقوله تعالى : علم أن لن تحصوه فتاب عليكم فاقرؤا ما تيسر أي صلوا ما تيسر من الصلاة ولو قدر حلب شاة، ثم نسخ وجوب قيام الليل بالصلوات الخمس بعد سنة أخرى فكان بين الوجوب، والتخفيف سنة وبين الوجوب، والنسخ سنتان كذا في العيني على البخاري قوله: (خصوصاً آخره) وهو السدس الخامس من أسداس الليل، وهو الوقت الذي ورد فيه النزول الإلهي . قوله : (وأقل ما ينبغي أن يتنقل بالليل ثمان ركعات الذي في الحاوي القدسي أن أقله ركعتان وأكثره ثمان لما روي عليه يعني أنقص من
And the night prayer is recommended, especially its latter part as we mentioned. The minimum that one should pray at night is eight rak'ahs, as in al-Jawhara. Its virtue cannot be counted; Allah says: 'No soul knows what joy is hidden for them' [as-Sajda:17]. His saying: 'As for its maximum, it is by his saying only.' He said: This is if one prays the maximum with one taslim; but if he separates them, then every increase is better, as Ibn Hajar stated in Sharh al-Bukhari, end. Perhaps this is according to the Shafi'i school; otherwise, increasing beyond four in daytime voluntary prayer is disliked (makruh) according to us. His saying: 'As narrated by al-Tabarani, etc.' And it is narrated that Allah says: 'O son of Adam, guarantee Me two rak'ahs at the beginning of the day, and I will suffice you at its end.' And it is narrated that Allah says: 'O son of Adam, suffice Me at the beginning of the day with four rak'ahs, and I will suffice you with them at the end of your day.' And it is narrated in place of the charities on every joint of the children of Adam, and they are three hundred and sixty joints. His saying: 'That suffices for the day' i.e., along with the attainment of the two previous virtues, and likewise is said later. His saying: 'And the night prayer is recommended, etc.' A group of scholars, including our usul scholars, held that qiyam al-layl was obligatory upon him (the Prophet), adhering to His saying: 'Stand the night except a little' [al-Muzzammil:73]. On this basis, the night prayer is recommended because the verbal evidences only indicate recommendation. Another group said: It was voluntary for him, so it is a sunnah for us, due to His saying: 'And from the night, perform tahajjud as an additional (nafilah) for you' [al-Isra:79]. The first group responded: There is no contradiction, because nafilah means additional (za'idah), i.e., additional to what was prescribed for others. And perhaps the restriction with the preposition (lak) indicates that. In the tafsir of Ibn Abbas: 'Stand the night' means all of it except a little, and this was hard upon the Prophet and his companions, and they stood the whole night, not knowing the limit of 'little'. Then Allah sent down: 'Half of it, or reduce it a little, or add to it' giving him choice among these stations. That was also hard upon the Prophet and his companions, so they stood the whole night until their feet swelled, fearing they would not maintain the obligatory amount. They did that for a year. Then Allah sent down its abrogator, saying: 'He knows that you cannot be precise' meaning standing the night from the third, half, and two-thirds. This was before the five prayers were prescribed. When the five prayers were prescribed, this abrogated that, just as zakat abrogated every charity, and Ramadan fasting every fast, end. In the tafsir of al-Jazari, the obligation of estimation was abrogated by His saying: 'He knows that you cannot be precise, so He has turned to you (in mercy); so recite what is easy of it' i.e., pray what is easy of prayer, even if it is the amount of milking a goat. Then the obligation of qiyam al-layl was abrogated by the five prayers after another year. So there was one year between obligation and alleviation, and two years between obligation and abrogation, as in al-Ayni on al-Bukhari. His saying: 'Especially its latter part' which is the fifth sixth of the night, and it is the time when the divine descent occurs. His saying: 'And the minimum that one should pray at night is eight rak'ahs' - in al-Hawi al-Qudsi, its minimum is two rak'ahs and its maximum is eight, as narrated from him, meaning less than.
Source pages p. 396

Commentary
This passage from Hashiya Al-Tahtawi covers the night prayer (salat al-layl) from several angles. It begins by stating that the night prayer is recommended (nadb), especially its latter part (the last sixth of the night, when divine descent is reported). The minimum recommended number of rak'ahs is eight according to al-Jawhara, but the text notes that in al-Hawi al-Qudsi the minimum is two and maximum eight. The virtue of night prayer is immense, as indicated by Quranic verse [as-Sajda:17]. The commentator then addresses a typical objection: if one prays more than eight, is it better? The response distinguishes methods: if done with one taslim (continuous), it may be disliked for daytime voluntary but not for night; but if one separates them (with taslim after every two rak'ahs), increase is better. This point is said to be based on the Shafi'i school, as in the Hanafi school increasing beyond four in daytime nafil is disliked. The text then narrates hadiths about the virtues of praying two or four rak'ahs at the beginning of the day (these are for duha, but included here for contrast? Actually they are separate). Then the main dispute: a group of scholars, including Hanafi usul scholars (al-usuliyyun min mashayikhina), held that qiyam al-layl was obligatory (fard) upon the Prophet based on the command 'Stand the night except a little' [al-Muzzammil:73]. According to this view, the night prayer for the Ummah is still recommended (nadb) because the verbal evidences for obligation only apply to the Prophet. Another group held it was voluntary for the Prophet and thus a sunnah for us, citing 'And from the night, perform tahajjud as an additional (nafilah) for you' [al-Isra:79]. The first group responds that nafilah here means 'additional' to what was prescribed for others, not that it was voluntary. The commentary then explains the historical process of abrogation: first, the obligation of standing the night was estimated (with options), then it was eased to a general 'recite what is easy', and finally abrogated by the five daily prayers after two years. The text thus concludes that the operative ruling (mufta bihi) is that the night prayer is recommended (nadb), not obligatory. The hashiah here refines the understanding by clarifying the dispute and settling on the non-obligatory status.

Key Terms
قيام الليل (qiyam al-layl): Standing (praying) at night, synonymous with salat al-layl. The text discusses whether it was obligatory on the Prophet.
نافلة (nafilah): Additional, supererogatory. In the verse, it is interpreted by some as 'additional' to what is prescribed for others, not merely voluntary.
ناسخ ومنسوخ (nasikh wa mansukh): Abrogating and abrogated. The text uses the concept of naskh to show that the obligation was later removed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what is the final status of the night prayer for the Ummah?
A) It is obligatory (fard)
B) It is recommended (nadb)
C) It is neither recommended nor obligatory
D) It depends on the individual's intention

Key Takeaway
The intra-Hanafi dispute over the Prophet's obligation of qiyam al-layl does not alter the Ummah's ruling: it remains a recommended (nadb) act.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
10 min
Salat al-Duha: Virtues, Number of Rak'ahs, and Hanafi Ruling
Ruling with proof and cross-madhhab note

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the most virtuous number of rak'ahs for Salat al-Duha, apply the condition of praying in pairs, and distinguish the Hanafi view from the Shafi'i view on joining rak'ahs.

Core Idea
Eight rak'ahs is the most virtuous; do not pray more than four with one salam.

This lesson unpacks the virtues and rulings of Salat al-Duha, a confirmed sunnah prayer. You will learn the rewards for different numbers of rak'ahs, the Hanafi position that eight is best, and the important condition that exceeding four rak'ahs with a single salam is makruh. We will also examine the hadith evidence and a cross-madhhab difference with the Shafi'i school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is Salat al-Duha (forenoon prayer). Determine its hukm level (sunnah muakkadah) and the most virtuous number of rak'ahs according to the Hanafi school.
The text says eight is the most virtuous because it is established by the Prophet's action.
2
Locate the dalil
Find the hadith evidence cited. The passage presents a hadith qudsi: 'Son of Adam, guarantee Me two rak'ahs at the beginning of the day, and I will guarantee you its end.' Also mentions the virtue of four and the substitution for charity.
The imperative 'اضمن' indicates recommendation (nadb).
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Explain how the hadith proves the recommendation. The command implies reward, not obligation; thus the prayer is sunnah, not wajib.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
The text notes a difference with the Shafi'i school regarding praying more than four with one salam. Shafi'is allow it; Hanafis consider it makruh.
The commentator says 'perhaps this is according to the Shafi'i school'.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The Hanafi relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that eight is most virtuous, and one should pray in sets of two rak'ahs, not more than four with one salam.
Al-Tahtawi cites al-Dhakha'ir al-Ashrafiyya for the virtue of eight.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
من صلى الضحى ركعتين لم يكتب من الغافلين ومن صلى أربعاً كتب من العابدين ومن كفي ذلك اليوم ومن صلى ثمانياً كتبه الله تعالى من القانتين ومن صلى اثنتي عشرة ركعة بنى الله له بيتاً في الجنة. وأكثرها اثنتا عشرة وأوسطها ثمان وهو أفضلها كما في الذخائر الأشرفية لثبوته بفعله، وقوله: (وأما أكثرها فبقوله فقط) قال: وهذا لو صلى الأكثر بسلام واحد أما لو فصل فكلما زاد فهو أفضل كما أفاده ابن حجر في شرح البخاري، اهـ ولعل هذا على مذهب الشافعي، وإلا فالزيادة على أربع في نفل النهار مكروهة عندنا. قوله: (لما روى الطبراني الخ) وروى يقول الله: ابن آدم اضمن لي ركعتين من أول النهار أكفك آخره، وروى يقول الله تعالى: يا ابن آدم اكفني أول النهار بأربع ركعات أكفك بهن آخر يومك، وروي مقام الصدقات التي على كل مفصل من بني آدم وهي ثلثمائة وستون مفصلاً. قوله: (كفى ذلك اليوم) أي مع حصول الفضيلتين السابقتين وكذا يقال فيما بعد
Whoever prays Duha two rak'ahs is not written among the heedless; whoever prays four is written among the worshippers; whoever prays eight, Allah the Exalted writes him among the obedient; whoever prays twelve rak'ahs, Allah builds for him a house in Paradise. The maximum is twelve, and the middle is eight, and it is the most virtuous as in al-Dhakha'ir al-Ashrafiyya due to its being established by his action. And his saying: (As for the maximum, it is by his saying only). He said: This is if he prays the maximum with one salam. But if he separates, then every increase is better, as Ibn Hajar benefited in his commentary on al-Bukhari. End. Perhaps this is according to the Shafi'i school; otherwise, increasing beyond four in supererogatory daytime prayers is disliked (makruh) according to us. The commentator said: (Because al-Tabarani narrated) and it is narrated that Allah says: 'Son of Adam, guarantee Me two rak'ahs at the beginning of the day, and I will guarantee you its end.' And it is narrated that Allah says: 'O son of Adam, suffice Me at the beginning of the day with four rak'ahs, and I will suffice you with them at the end of your day.' And it is narrated that it takes the place of the charities due on every joint of the son of Adam, which are three hundred and sixty joints. The commentator said: ('Suffices that day') meaning along with obtaining the two preceding virtues, and similarly is said in what follows.
Source pages p. 396

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the rulings and virtues of Salat al-Duha (the forenoon voluntary prayer). It starts by listing the virtues associated with different numbers of rak'ahs: two, four, eight, and twelve, each with a specific reward. The commentator then clarifies that the maximum number of rak'ahs for Duha is twelve, the middle is eight, and eight is the most virtuous because the Prophet ﷺ practiced it. However, the author of al-Dhakha'ir al-Ashrafiyya says that the maximum is based on the Prophet's saying only, not action. The commentator adds that praying the maximum (twelve) with one salam is allowed, but if one separates into multiple sets, each increase is better, as noted by Ibn Hajar. But the commentator cautions that this may be according to the Shafi'i school; in the Hanafi school, increasing beyond four rak'ahs in daytime voluntary prayers without separating (i.e., praying more than four with a single salam) is makruh (disliked). The passage then presents hadith evidence from al-Tabarani and others, including a hadith qudsi where Allah asks the believer to guarantee Him two rak'ahs at the start of the day, and He will guarantee the rest of the day. Another hadith mentions four rak'ahs. It also mentions that Duha prayer can substitute for the charity due on each of the 360 joints of the body. The commentator explains that the phrase 'suffices that day' means the person obtains both the virtues of being written among the heedless/worshippers (from the previous rewards) and the sufficiency mentioned.

Key Terms
صلاة الضحى (Salat al-Duha): A supererogatory prayer performed after sunrise until before zenith; its time begins after the sun has risen to the height of a spear (approx. 15-20 minutes after sunrise) and ends before zawal (when the sun reaches its zenith).
مكروهة (makruhah): Disliked (makruh tanzihi) – here meaning that praying more than four rak'ahs of Duha with a single salam is makruh because it resembles the Shafi'i practice and violates the Hanafi principle of performing supererogatory prayers in pairs (two rak'ahs each).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the most virtuous number of rak'ahs for Salat al-Duha?
A) Two rak'ahs
B) Four rak'ahs
C) Eight rak'ahs
D) Twelve rak'ahs

Key Takeaway
Salat al-Duha is a confirmed sunnah; the most virtuous is eight rak'ahs, prayed in sets of two, and exceeding four with one salam is makruh tanzihi.
