Salah — Prayer
intermediate
10 min
Ruling and Virtues of Salat al-Layl (Night Prayer)
Critical commentary on the ruling and abrogation of night prayer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on night prayer (sunnah muakkadah) and explain the historical process of abrogation that led to its current status.

Core Idea
Night prayer was once obligatory but was abrogated by the five daily prayers; it is now a confirmed sunnah.

Night prayer (Salat al-Layl) holds a special place in Islamic worship. The Hanafi school holds that it was initially an obligation upon the Prophet ﷺ and his community, but was later abrogated in stages, culminating in its current status as a highly recommended sunnah. This lesson traces that legal journey through the Quranic verses and tafsir, clarifying the ruling and the recommended practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the dispute
Note the two groups: one holds qiyam al-layl was fard upon the Prophet (based on al-Muzzammil:2), the other says it was supererogatory (based on al-Isra:79). The Hanafi usul scholars adopt the first view.
The dispute is historical; the practical ruling is the same.
2
Trace the stages of abrogation
Follow the narrative: initial command to stand most of the night → alleviation with choices → abrogation of precise amount by 'He knows you cannot measure it' → final abrogation by the five daily prayers.
This is a classic case of naskh (abrogation) in stages.
3
Derive the current ruling
Since the obligation was lifted, night prayer becomes mandubah (recommended) or sunnah muakkadah. The evidence now is the hadith encouraging it, not an imperative.
The Hanafi position is that it is a confirmed sunnah.
4
Note the recommended rak'ahs
The text states 'the least it is recommended to move oneself is eight' but al-Hawi al-Qudsi gives minimum two, maximum eight. The hadith does not fix a number; eight is considered the most virtuous.
Performance in pairs; witr is separate.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (وندب صلاة الليل الخ) ذهب طائفة من العلماء وعليه الأصوليون من مشايخنا إلى أن قيام الليل فرض عليه تمسكوا بقوله تعالى: {قم الليل إلا قليلاً} [المزمل/2] وعلى هذا فتكون صلاة الليل مندوبة لأن الأدلة القولية فيه إنما تفيد الندب، وقال طائفة: كان تطوعاً منه، فيكون في حقنا سنة لقوله تعالى: {ومن الليل فتهجد به نافلة لك} وأجاب الأولون قالوا: لا منافاة لأن المراد بالنافلة الزائدة أي زائدة على ما فرض على غيرك، وربما يعطي التقييد بالمجرور ذلك، وفي تفسير ابن عباس: قم الليل يعني كله إلا قليلاً فاشتد ذلك على النبي ﷺ وعلى أصحابه، وقاموا الليل كله، ولم يعرفوا ما حد القليل، فأنزل الله تعالى نصفه أو أنقص منه قليلاً، أو زد النصف إلى الثلث أو زد عليه إلى الثلثين خيره بين هذه المنازل فإشتد ذلك أيضاً على النبي ﷺ وعلى أصحابه فقاموا الليل كله حتى انتفخت أقدامهم مخافة أن لا يحفظوا القدر الواجب، فعلوا ذلك سنة فأنزل الله تعالى ناسختها فقال: {علم أن لن تحصوه} يعني قيام الليل من الثلث والنصف والثلثين، وكان هذا قبل أن تفرض الصلوات الخمس، فلما فرضت الصلوات الخمس نسخت هذه كما نسخت الزكاة كل صدقة، وصوم رمضان كل صوم اهـ وفي تفسير الجزري نسخ وجوب التقدير بقوله تعالى: {علم أن لن تحصوه} فتاب عليكم فاقرؤا ما تيسر أي صلوا ما تيسر من الصلاة ولو قدر حلب شاة، ثم نسخ وجوب قيام الليل بالصلوات الخمس بعد سنة أخرى فكان بين الوجوب والتخفيف سنة وبين الوجوب والنسخ سنتان كذا في العيني على البخاري. قوله: (خصوصاً آخره) وهو السدس الخامس من أسداس الليل، وهو الوقت الذي ورد فيه النزول الإلهي. قوله: (وأقل ما ينبغي أن يتنقل بالليل ثمان ركعات) الذي في الحاوي القدسي أن أقله ركعتان وأكثره ثمان لما روي عليه يعني أنقص من نفس ما أخفي لهم من قرة أعين وفي صحيح مسلم قال رسول الله ﷺ: عليكم بصلاة الليل فإنه دأب الصالحين قبلكم وقربة إلى ربكم ومكفرة للسيئات ومنهاة عن الإثم. قوله: (فإنه دأب الصالحين) أي عادة الصالحين أي معتادهم. قوله: (وقربة) أي مقربة لكم من ربكم. قوله: (ومكفرة للسيئات) أي الصغائر. قوله: (ومنهاة عن الإثم) أي ناهية عنه
His saying: (And recommended is night prayer, especially its end...) A group of scholars, and upon it are the usuliyyun among our mashayikh, held that standing at night (qiyam al-layl) was fard (obligatory) upon him, adhering to His saying: {Stand the night except a little} [al-Muzzammil:2]. Upon this, the night prayer becomes recommended (mandubah) because the verbal evidences only indicate recommendation. And another group said: It was a supererogatory act from him, so in our case it is sunnah due to His saying: {And from the night, pray with it as an extra prayer for you} [al-Isra:79]. The first group replied: There is no contradiction because what is meant by 'nafilah' is 'extra' meaning extra over what was fard upon others, and perhaps the restriction by the preposition indicates that. In the tafsir of Ibn Abbas: 'Stand the night' meaning all of it except a little, so that was hard upon the Prophet ﷺ and his companions, and they stood the whole night, and they did not know the limit of 'a little'. So Allah revealed: 'Half of it or reduce from it a little, or add to it half to a third or add to it to two-thirds' – He gave him choice among these positions. That too was hard upon the Prophet ﷺ and his companions, so they stood the whole night until their feet swelled, fearing they could not observe the obligatory amount. They did that for a year, then Allah revealed its abrogator saying: {He knows that you cannot measure it} meaning qiyam al-layl from the third, half, and two-thirds. This was before the five prayers were made fard. When the five prayers were made fard, this abrogated this, just as zakat abrogated every sadaqah, and Ramadan fasting abrogated every fast. In the tafsir of al-Jazari: The obligation of estimation was abrogated by His saying: {He knows that you cannot measure it, so He turned to you (in mercy), so recite what is easy} meaning pray what is easy of prayer even if it be the amount of milking a sheep. Then the obligation of qiyam al-layl was abrogated by the five prayers after another year, so between the obligation and the alleviation was one year, and between the obligation and the abrogation was two years – as in al-Ayni on al-Bukhari. His saying: (Especially its end) which is the fifth sixth of the sixths of the night, and it is the time in which the divine descent occurs. His saying: (And the least it is recommended to move oneself at night is eight rak'ahs) In al-Hawi al-Qudsi: The least is two rak'ahs and the most is eight, because it is narrated... meaning less than what is hidden for them of comfort of eyes. And in Sahih Muslim, the Messenger of Allah ﷺ said: 'Upon you is night prayer, for it is the habit of the righteous before you, a means of closeness to your Lord, an expiation of sins, and a prevention of sin.' His saying: ('Habit of the righteous') means the custom of the righteous, i.e., their usual practice. His saying: ('a means of closeness') means it brings you closer to your Lord. His saying: ('an expiation of sins') meaning minor sins. His saying: ('a prevention of sin') meaning it prevents from sin.
Source pages p. 396

Commentary
This passage is a critical commentary on the rulings of Salat al-Layl (night prayer). It begins by addressing a scholarly dispute: whether qiyam al-layl was fard (obligatory) upon the Prophet ﷺ or a supererogatory act. The first group, including Hanafi usul scholars, argued it was fard based on the verse 'Stand the night except a little' (al-Muzzammil:2), but they note that the verbal evidence indicates recommendation (nadb) for us. The second group held it was supererogatory for the Prophet, making it sunnah for us due to the verse 'And from the night, pray with it as an extra (nafilah) for you' (al-Isra:79). The first group responds that 'nafilah' means 'extra' beyond what is fard upon others, so no contradiction. The commentary then relates the history of abrogation: Initially, the Prophet and his companions were commanded to stand most of the night. This was hard on them, so Allah gave choices (half, a little less, etc.). Still difficult, they stood so long their feet swelled. After a year, the verse 'He knows that you cannot measure it' (al-Muzzammil:20) abrogated the precise obligation, allowing 'what is easy of prayer.' Later, the five daily prayers abrogated even that obligation, so night prayer became sunnah. The passage then explains that 'especially its end' refers to the fifth sixth of the night, when divine descent occurs. Regarding the number of rak'ahs, the commentary notes a difference: some say minimum two, maximum eight; the preferred view (from al-Hawi al-Qudsi) is that the least is two and the most is eight, but the text here says the recommended minimum for moving oneself is eight. A hadith from Sahih Muslim encourages night prayer as the habit of the righteous, closeness to Allah, expiation of minor sins, and preventer of sin.

Key Terms
قيام الليل (qiyam al-layl): Standing at night for prayer, referring specifically to voluntary night prayer (tahajjud) performed after 'Isha until before Fajr.
ناسخ ومنسوخ (nasikh wa mansukh): Abrogation: the process by which a later Quranic verse or hadith supersedes an earlier one. Here, the obligation of qiyam al-layl was abrogated by the verse 'اعلم أن لن تحصوه' and then by the five daily prayers.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What was the event that led to the final abrogation of the obligation of night prayer according to the Hanafi understanding?
A) The revelation of verse al-Muzzammil:2
B) The revelation of verse al-Isra:79
C) The institutionalization of the five daily prayers
D) The Prophet's migration to Madinah

Key Takeaway
Night prayer (Salat al-Layl) is a confirmed sunnah (sunnah muakkadah) in the Hanafi school, with a minimum of two and a most virtuous eight rak'ahs, and its performance brings immense reward.

beginner

Salat al-Istikhara: Prayer for Seeking Guidance
Describing the recommendation, method, and supplication of Salat al-Istikhara

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling of Salat al-Istikhara, describe its method, and apply the Hanafi principle that a command (amr) indicates recommendation (nadb) in non-obligatory acts.

Core Idea
Istikhara is a sunnah prayer to seek Allah's choice; its method is prayer + du'a, but du'a alone suffices if needed.

In this lesson, we examine the Hanafi ruling on Salat al-Istikhara, a prayer taught by the Prophet ﷺ for seeking divine guidance in permissible matters. The passage from Hashiya al-Tahtawi explains the recommendation, the prescribed method, and the supplication. We will analyze the proof from hadith and how Hanafi usul categorizes the command as nadb (recommendation).

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the act being discussed? What hukm level does the Hanafi school assign to it?
The act is Salat al-Istikhara; the ruling is sunnah muakkadah.
2
Locate the dalil
Which hadith is cited as proof? What is its source and transmission grade?
Hadith of Jabir in Sahih al-Bukhari; it is hadith ahad but widely accepted.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How does the hadith prove the ruling? Identify the amr (command) and how it indicates nadb.
The command 'let him pray' is interpreted as recommendation (nadb) in Hanafi usul for non-obligatory acts.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Is there any variation in practice? What alternative is mentioned?
If unable to pray, one may perform Istikhara by du'a alone, based on a weak narration from Abu Bakr.
5
Evaluate the practice
What is the mufta bihi (operative ruling) for fatwa today?
The primary method is prayer + du'a; du'a alone suffices in difficulty.

و) ندب (صلاة الاستخارة) وقد أفصحت السنة عن بيانها قال جابر رضي الله عنه: كان رسول الله ﷺ يعلمنا الاستخارة في الأمور كلها كما يعلمنا السورة من القرآن يقول: إذا هم أحدكم بالأمر فليركع ركعتين من غير الفريضة ثم ليقل: اللهم إني أستخيرك بعلمك وأستقدرك بقدرتك وأسألك من فضلك العظيم فإنك تقدر ولا أقدر وتعلم ولا أعلم وأنت علام الغيوب اللهم إن كنت تعلم أن هذا الأمر خير لي في ديني ومعاشي وعاقبة أمري أو قال: عاجل أمري وآجله فاقدره لي ويسره لي ثم بارك لي فيه وإن كنت تعلم أن هذا الأمر. قوله: (و) ندب (صلاة الاستخارة) أي طلب ما فيه الخير، وهي تكون لأمر في المستقبل ليظهر الله تعالى خير الأمرين. وأما صلاة الحاجة فتارة تكون لأمر نزل أو سينزل وهذا الأمر معنى يراد تحصيله أو دفعه وهذا أولى مما في السيد عن النهر. قوله: (كان رسول الله ﷺ يعلمنا الاستخارة الخ) وقال: من سعادة ابن آدم استخارة الله عز وجل زاد الحاكم ومن شقاوة ابن آدم تركه استخارة الله عز وجل وقد روى بإسناد حسن أن داود عليه السلام قال: أي عبادك أبغض إليك؟ قال: عبد استخارني في أمر فخرت له فلم يرض. قوله: (يقول) بدل من قوله يعلمنا. قوله: (فليركع ركعتين) يقرأ في الأولى بالكافرون وفي الثانية بالإخلاص. وقال بعضهم: يقرأ في الأولى بقوله تعالى: {وربك يخلق ما يشاء ويختار} إلى قوله: {يعلنون} وفي الثانية بقوله تعالى: {وما كان لمؤمن ولا مؤمنة} إلى قوله: {مبينا} وبعضهم يجمع بين ما ذكروا. إذا تعذر عليه الصلاة استخار بالدعاء فقد روى الترمذي بإسناد ضعيف عن أبي بكر الصديق رضي الله عنه أن النبي ﷺ كان إذا أراد الأمر قال: اللهم خر لي واختر لي اهـ. قوله: (اللهم إني أستخيرك) أي أطلب منك تحصيل خير الأمرين، والباء في قوله بعلمك للقسم أو للتعليل أي لأنك عالم بذلك، وكذا يقال فيما إذا بعد. قوله: (فإنك تقدر الخ) تعليل على اللف والنشر المشوش. قوله: (وأسألك من فضلك العظيم) يحتمل أن من اسم بمعنى بعض مفعول به لأسأل والفضل بمعنى المتفضل، ويحتمل أن المفعول به محذوف تقديره بيان الخير. قوله: (وأنت علام الغيوب) أي تعلم المغيبات علماً تاماً كما تفيده صيغة المبالغة. والغيوب جمع غيب بمعنى مغيب. وإذا كان يعلم المغيبات فعلم المشاهد لنا كذلك بل أولى على ما تقضي به العادة. قوله: (اللهم إن كنت تعلم الخ) الشك بالنسبة إلى الداعي لا إلى علام الغيوب. قوله: (أن هذا الأمر) يذكر حاجته بدل لفظ الأمر
(And recommended is the Prayer of Istikhara) and the Sunnah has clearly explained it. Jabir (may Allah be pleased with him) said: The Messenger of Allah ﷺ used to teach us Istikhara in all matters as he taught us a surah from the Quran. He said: When one of you intends a matter, let him pray two rak'ahs other than the obligatory prayer, then say: 'O Allah, I seek Your choice by Your knowledge, and I seek Your power by Your power, and I ask You of Your great bounty, for You can and I cannot, and You know and I know not, and You are the Knower of the unseen. O Allah, if You know that this matter is good for me in my religion, my livelihood, and the outcome of my affair (or he said: the immediate and the later of my affair), then decree it for me and make it easy for me, then bless me in it. And if You know that this matter...' The commentator said: (And recommended is the Prayer of Istikhara) i.e., seeking what contains good, and it is for a future matter so that Allah manifests the better of the two affairs. As for the Prayer of Need (Salat al-Haja), it is sometimes for a matter that has occurred or will occur, and this matter is a meaning that one wishes to attain or repel, and this is more appropriate than what is in al-Sayyid from al-Nahr. The commentator said: (The Messenger of Allah ﷺ used to teach us Istikhara...) And he said: 'From the happiness of the son of Adam is his seeking guidance from Allah, the Mighty and Majestic.' Al-Hakim added: 'And from the misery of the son of Adam is his abandoning seeking guidance from Allah, the Mighty and Majestic.' And it is narrated with a good chain that Dawud (peace be upon him) said: 'Which of Your servants is most hateful to You?' He said: 'A servant who sought guidance from Me in a matter and I chose for him, and he was not pleased.' The commentator said: (He says) it is a substitution for 'he used to teach us'. (Let him pray two rak'ahs) He recites in the first (after Fatiha) Surah al-Kafirun, and in the second Surah al-Ikhlas. Some said: He recites in the first the verse {And your Lord creates what He wills and chooses} [28:68] until {they associate}, and in the second the verse {It is not for a believing man or woman} [33:36] until {clear}. Some combine both. If praying is difficult for him, he may make Istikhara by du'a alone, as al-Tirmidhi narrated with a weak chain from Abu Bakr al-Siddiq (may Allah be pleased with him) that the Prophet ﷺ, when he wanted a matter, would say: 'O Allah, choose for me and grant me the better.' The commentator said: (O Allah, I seek Your choice by Your knowledge) i.e., I ask You to obtain the better of the two affairs. The 'ba' in 'by Your knowledge' is for oath or for causation, i.e., because You are knowledgeable of that. Similarly is said in what follows. (For You can and I cannot) is an explanation in the style of disarranged dispersal. (And I ask You of Your great bounty) 'Min' could be a noun meaning 'some' as the object of 'I ask' and 'al-fadl' means the Bestower, or the object is omitted and the appreciation is 'the explanation of good'. (And You are the Knower of the unseen) i.e., You know the hidden things completely, as the intensive form indicates. 'Al-ghuyub' is the plural of 'ghayb' meaning 'hidden'. And if He knows the hidden things, then His knowledge of the witnessed is likewise, indeed more so, as is customary. (O Allah, if You know that...) The doubt pertains to the supplicant, not to the Knower of the unseen. (That this matter) he mentions his need replacing the word 'matter'.
Source pages p. 397

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the recommendation of Salat al-Istikhara (the Prayer for Seeking Guidance). The author explains that Istikhara means asking Allah to choose the better of two options in a future matter. The primary practice is to pray two rak'ahs of non-obligatory prayer, then recite a specific supplication taught by the Prophet ﷺ. The supplication includes praising Allah, acknowledging His knowledge and power, and asking for guidance in a specific matter. The commentator provides various details: the recommended surahs to recite (al-Kafirun and al-Ikhlas, or alternatively verses from 28:68 and 33:36), and that one may also just make the du'a without prayer if unable. There is also a narration that not being pleased with Allah's choice after Istikhara is a sign of misery. The commentary explains parts of the du'a linguistically: 'a-stakhiruka' means to seek the better of two things, 'bi'ilmika' could be an oath or causal, 'al-ghuyub' indicates perfect knowledge of the unseen. The doubt in the du'a ('if You know') is from the perspective of the supplicant, not from Allah's knowledge.

Key Terms
استخارة (istikhara): Seeking from Allah to choose the better option between two permissible matters, achieved through prayer and supplication.
صلاة الحاجة (salat al-haja): The Prayer of Need, distinct from Istikhara in that it is for a specific need that has occurred or will occur, whereas Istikhara is for choosing between options.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the minimum requirement for performing Istikhara if one cannot pray?
A) It is not valid without prayer
B) One may make the du'a alone
C) One must give charity instead
D) One must wait until able to pray

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that Salat al-Istikhara is a sunnah muakkadah performed by two rak'ahs and a du'a, with an allowance for du'a only if needed, and one should trust Allah's choice without seeking signs.

The Recommendation of Salat al-Layl
Proof and commentary on the recommendation of night prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on salat al-layl, cite the hadith proof, and explain the significance of its attributes: da'b, qurba, mukaffira, and munahiya.

Core Idea
Salat al-layl is a confirmed sunnah — the righteous practice, nearness to Allah, expiation for minor sins, and deterrent from sin.

In this lesson, we examine a hadith from Sahih Muslim that the Hanafi school uses to establish the recommendation of night prayer. The commentary unpacks four key attributes that highlight its spiritual benefits and legal status. Understanding the precise wording and its interpretation is essential to avoid the common mistake of considering it obligatory.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What act is being discussed? What is its hukm level in the Hanafi school?
The act is salat al-layl (night prayer), and the ruling is sunnah muakkada (confirmed sunnah), not fard or wajib.
2
Locate the dalil
What proof does the author cite? Identify the hadith from Sahih Muslim and the Quranic verse reference (32:17).
The hadith uses the command 'عليكم بصلاة الليل' to indicate strong recommendation.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How does the phrase 'عليكم' indicate recommendation according to Hanafi usul?
The expression 'عليكم' (adhere to) implies emphasis but not obligation; it is a form of nadb (recommendation).
4
Examine the four attributes
Break down the hadith's four descriptions: da'b (practice of the righteous), qurba (nearness), mukaffira (expiation for minor sins), munahiya (deterrent from sin).
Each attribute reinforces the virtue and recommended nature of the act.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
نفس ما أخفي لهم من قرة أعين وفي صحيح مسلم قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم : عليكم بصلاة الليل فإنه دأب الصالحين قبلكم وقربة إلى ربكم ومكفرة للسيئات ومنهاة عن الإثم قوله : (فإنه دأب الصالحين) أي عادة الصالحين أي معتادهم. قوله : ( وقرية) أي مقربة لكم من ربكم. قوله : (ومكفرة للسيئات) أي الصغائر . قوله: (ومنهاة عن الإثم أي ناهية عنه
No soul knows what joy is hidden for them. And in Sahih Muslim, the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'Adhere to the night prayer, for it is the practice of the righteous before you, a means of nearness to your Lord, an expiation for sins, and a deterrent from sin.' His saying: ('For it is the practice of the righteous') meaning their custom. His saying: ('and nearness') meaning a means of closeness to your Lord. His saying: ('and expiation for sins') meaning minor sins. His saying: ('and a deterrent from sin') meaning it forbids sin.
Source pages p. 397

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof. The author cites the Quranic verse (32:17) and a hadith from Sahih Muslim to establish the recommendation of salat al-layl (night prayer). The hadith emphasizes that salat al-layl is the consistent practice (dab) of the righteous, a means of nearness (qurba) to Allah, an expiation (mukaffira) for minor sins, and a deterrent (munahiya) from sin. The commentary clarifies that 'dab' means habitual practice, 'qurba' means closeness, 'mukaffira' expiates minor sins (sagha'ir), and 'munahiya' forbids sin. This establishes salat al-layl as a highly recommended sunnah muakkada in the Hanafi school, based on explicit prophetic command and practice.

Key Terms
دأب (da'b): Habitual practice or consistent custom.
قربة (qurba): Means of drawing near to Allah.
مكفرة (mukaffira): Expiation, removal of sins.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on salat al-layl according to this passage?
A) It is fard (obligatory).
B) It is sunnah muakkada (confirmed sunnah).
C) It is makruh (disliked).
D) It is mubah (permissible).

Key Takeaway
Salat al-layl is a confirmed sunnah (sunnah muakkada) that brings nearness to Allah, expiates minor sins, and deters from sin, based on the hadith in Sahih Muslim.

The Ruling and Method of Salat al-Istikharah
Proof, method, and commentary on istikharah prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on salat al-istikharah, explain its proof from the hadith, and describe the correct method including recitation and the dua.

Core Idea
Istikharah is a recommended prayer for ambiguous permissible matters; after it, proceed with an open heart.

The prayer of istikharah (seeking good) is a sunnah taught by the Prophet for any matter where the best course is unclear. This passage from Hashiyat al-Tahtawi explains its ruling, contrasts it with salat al-hajah, provides the famous hadith of Jabir, and details the recitation and the comprehensive dua. Understanding these details ensures that you perform istikharah correctly, with the proper intention and expectation that Allah will guide you to what is best.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The text states that istikharah prayer is 'recommended' (mandub). Determine the precise hukm level: sunnah muakkadah or mustahabb.
Hanafis consider it a confirmed sunnah, as indicated by the Prophet's consistent teaching.
2
Locate the primary dalil
The author cites the hadith of Jabir where the Prophet taught istikharah like a surah from the Quran. Identify this as the proof.
The hadith is muttafaq alayh (agreed upon) except for minor variations.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Analyze how the hadith indicates recommendation (nadb) rather than obligation. The Prophet's teaching 'as he taught a surah' and the wording 'when one of you intends a matter' show it is for all ambiguous permissible matters.
The Hanafi usul principle: al-amr al-mujarrad 'an al-qarinah yufid al-nadb.
4
Examine the method and dua
The text gives specific recitation recommendations (Surah al-Kafirun and al-Ikhlas) and the full dua. Understand the meaning of the dua and the phrase 'if You know...' which expresses human doubt, not Divine ignorance.
If prayer is not possible, making dua alone suffices.
5
Apply the practical guidance
After praying, one should proceed with what the heart inclines to. The text also mentions repeating istikharah seven times. Recognize that istikharah is for the timing of obligatory acts like hajj, not whether to do them.
The heart's inclination should be free from whims; one should seek counsel and then decide.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : ( وندب صلاة الاستخارة) أي طلب ما فيه الخير، وهي تكون لأمر في المستقبل ليظهر الله تعالى خير الأمرين، وأما صلاة الحاجة فتارة تكون لأمر نزل، أو سينزل وهذا الأمر معنى يراد تحصيله، أو دفعه وهذا أولى مما في السيد عن النهر. قوله : (كان رسول الله لا يعلمنا الاستخارة الخ) وقال : من سعادة ابن آدم استخارة الله عز وجل زاد الحاكم ومن شقاوة ابن آدم تركه استخارة الله عز وجل وقد روى بإسناد حسن أن داود عليه السلام قال : أي عبادك أبغض إليك ؟ قال : عبد استخارني في أمر فخرت له فلم يرض. قوله : (يقول) بدل من قوله : يعلمنا قوله : ( فليركع ركعتين) يقرأ في الأولى بالكافرون، وفي الثانية بالإخلاص، وقال بعضهم : يقرأ في الأولى بقوله تعالى: ﴿وربك يخلق ما يشاء ويختار إلى يعلنون وفي الثانية بقوله تعالى: (وما كان لمؤمن ولا مؤمنة) إلى قوله : ومبينا ، وبعضهم يجمع بين ما ذكروا إذا تعذر عليه الصلاة استخار بالدعاء فقد روى الترمذي بإسناد ضعيف عن أبي بكر الصديق رضي الله عنه أن النبي كان إذا أراد الأمر قال: اللهم خر لي، واختر لي اهـ. قوله : (اللهم إني أستخيرك أي أطلب منك تحصيل خير الأمرين، والباء في قوله بعملك للقسم، أو للتعليل أي لأنك عالم بذلك، وكذا يقال : فيما إذا بعد. قوله : (فإنك تقدر الخ) تعليل على اللف والنشر المشوش، قوله: (وأسألك من العظيم) يحتمل أن من اسم بمعنى بعض مفعول به لأسأل والفضل بمعنى المتفضل، ويحتمل أن المفعول به محذوف تقديره بيان الخير قوله : (وأنت علام الغيوب) أي تعلم المغياب علماً تاماً كما تفيده صيغة المبالغة، والغيوب جمع غيب بمعنى مغيب، وإذا كان يعلم المغيبات فعلم المشاهد لنا كذلك، بل أولى على ما تقضي به العادة. قوله : (اللهم إن كنت تعلم الخ) الشك بالنسبة إلى الداعي لا إلى علام الغيوب. قوله : أن هذا الأمر يذكر حاجته بدل لفظ الأمر. فضلك شر لي في ديني ومعاشي وعاقبة أمري أو قال: عاجل أمري وآجله فاصرفه عني واصرفني عنه واقدر لي الخير حيث كان ثم رضني به قال : ويسمي حاجته رواه الجماعة إلا أن مسلماً وينبغي يجمع بين الروايتين فيقول وعاقبة أمري وعاجله وآجله والاستخارة في الحج والجهاد وجميع أبواب الخير تحمل على تعيين الوقت لا نفس الفعل وإذا استخار مضى لما ينشرح له صدره وينبغي أن يكررها سبع مرات لما روي عن أنس قال: قال رسول : يا أنس إذا هممت بأمر فاستخر ربك فيه سبع مرات ثم انظر إلى الذي يسبق إلى قلبك فإن الخير فيه
His saying: (and the prayer of istikharah is recommended) meaning seeking what is good. It is for a future matter so that Allah may make the better of two things apparent. As for the prayer of need (salat al-hajah), it is sometimes for a matter that has descended or will descend, and this matter is a meaning intended to be attained or repelled. His saying: (The Messenger of Allah would teach us istikharah...) and he said: 'Among the happiness of the son of Adam is his istikharah to Allah; among his misery is his abandonment of it.' Al-Hakim added. It is narrated with a good chain that Dawud (peace be upon him) said: 'Which of Your servants is most hateful to You?' He said: 'A servant who consulted Me in a matter and I chose for him, and he was not pleased.' His saying: ('he said') is a substitute for 'he would teach us'. His saying: ('then let him pray two rak'ahs') he recites in the first with al-Kafirun, and in the second with al-Ikhlas. Some say: he recites in the first: 'And your Lord creates what He wills and chooses...' and in the second: 'It is not for a believing man or woman...' to '...clear'. Some combine both. If prayer is difficult for him, he makes istikharah by dua. At-Tirmidhi narrated with a weak chain from Abu Bakr that the Prophet when he wanted to do something would say: 'O Allah, choose for me and grant me the better.' His saying: ('O Allah, I seek Your choice by Your knowledge') means I ask You to secure the better of two things. The ba in 'by Your knowledge' is for oath or for cause, i.e., because You know that. His saying: ('For You are able and I am not') is a cause, in the style of laf wa nashr. His saying: ('and I ask You from Your great bounty') possibly 'min' is partitive, 'bounty' meaning the Giver. 'Your great bounty' could be the object, or the object is implied as 'clarification of the good'. His saying: ('And You are the Knower of the unseen') means You know the hidden with complete knowledge, as the intensive form indicates. 'Unseen' is plural of ghayb meaning hidden. If He knows the hidden, then He knows the visible even more. His saying: ('O Allah, if You know...') the doubt is from the supplicant, not from the Knower of the unseen. His saying: ('that this matter') he mentions his need in place of the word 'this matter'. [Then the dua continues:] 'choose good for me in my religion, my livelihood, and the end of my affair' or said: 'immediate and future', 'then turn it away from me and turn me away from it, and decree for me good wherever it is, then make me content with it.' He said: And he names his need. The group narrated except Muslim. It is recommended to combine both narrations and say: 'and the end of my affair and its immediate and future'. Istikharah in hajj, jihad, and all doors of goodness pertains to the timing, not the act itself. When he makes istikharah, he should proceed with what his heart is open to. He should repeat it seven times due to what is narrated from Anas: The Prophet said: 'O Anas, when you intend a matter, consult your Lord seven times, then look to what comes to your heart, for indeed the good is in it.'
Source pages p. 397

Commentary
This passage is a detailed ruling with proof on salat al-istikharah. The commentator explains that istikharah is recommended (mandub) for future matters where one does not know the best course. It differs from salat al-hajah (prayer for need), which is for something already present. The proof includes the famous hadith of Jabir in which the Prophet taught the companions to pray two rak'ahs and recite the specific dua. The commentary expands on the recitation (various options), the meaning of the dua, and distinctions between istikharah for actions versus timing (e.g., whether to perform hajj this year). It cites additional narrations that istikharah is a sign of happiness, and that one should proceed with an open heart after praying. Repeating seven times is mentioned from a separate hadith. This establishes the Hanafi position that istikharah is a mustahabb prayer for all ambiguous matters, and after it, one acts on what one feels inclined to, provided it is free from whims.

Key Terms
الاستخارة (al-istikhārah): Seeking divine guidance to choose the better of two options in a permitted matter.
صلاة الحاجة (ṣalāt al-ḥājah): A prayer offered to request a specific need from Allah, distinct from istikharah.
ندب (nadb): Recommendation; an act that is not obligatory but carries reward.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
For what kind of matters is salat al-istikharah prescribed?
A) Matters of worship that are already known to be good.
B) Matters where one does not know the best course among permissible options.
C) Matters that are clearly sinful.
D) Only for matters related to marriage.

Key Takeaway
Salat al-istikharah is a recommended prayer for any ambiguous permissible matter, supported by the hadith of Jabir, and after it one should act on the inclination of the heart, repeating it if needed.

Salat al-Hajah: Ruling and Method
Proof and method of salat al-hajah prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling of salat al-hajah, identify the hadith proof, and explain the recommended procedure and number of rak'ahs.

Core Idea
Salat al-hajah is a recommended prayer for any lawful need, proven by a specific hadith detailing wudu, two rak'ahs, and a comprehensive dua.

In this lesson, we examine the ruling and method of salat al-hajah, a prayer for specific needs. The Hanafi school bases its recommendation on a hadith from Abdullah ibn Abi Awfa, which outlines the procedure. We will analyze the proof, the number of rak'ahs, and the meaning of the supplication.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage begins by stating that salat al-hajah is recommended (mandub). Recognize that this is a sunnah prayer, not obligatory.
The term 'mandub' is synonymous with mustahabb in Hanafi fiqh.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is a hadith from Abdullah ibn Abi Awfa. Identify the hadith and its source.
The hadith is classified as ahad (single-chain).
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
The hadith uses imperatives (فليتوضأ, ثم يصلي) which in Hanafi usul indicate recommendation when context suggests general encouragement, not obligation.
Hanafi usul holds that al-amr (command) can be for nadb (recommendation) if there is a qarina (indication).
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on rak'ahs
The text mentions that some Hanafis allow two, four, or up to twelve rak'ahs. Understand the basis for each view.
The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is two rak'ahs, but more are permissible.
5
Conclude with the mufta bihi
Summarize that the Hanafi school recommends two rak'ahs with the specific procedure and supplication.
The dua includes asking for causes of mercy and determinations of forgiveness.

And the prayer of need (salat al-hajah) is recommended, and it is two rak'ahs. From Abdullah ibn Abi Awfa: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'Whoever has a need from Allah or from any of the children of Adam, let him perform ablution and do it well, then pray two rak'ahs, then praise Allah and send blessings on the Prophet, then say: 'There is no god but Allah, the Forbearing, the Generous. His saying: ('It is two rak'ahs or four') and in al-Hawi it is twelve rak'ahs with one salaam, said as-Sayyid. His saying: ('to Allah') meaning without any intermediary from humans. His saying: ('or to any of the children of Adam') means what comes through their hands, otherwise all needs are from Allah. His saying: 'I ask You for the causes of Your mercy' meaning the things that necessitate mercy from You and beneficence. And his saying: 'and the determinations'

Commentary
This passage provides the ruling on salat al-hajah (prayer for need). The commentator begins by stating it is recommended (mandub). The proof is the hadith of Abdullah ibn Abi Awfa, which prescribes a specific procedure: perform wudu properly, pray two rak'ahs, praise Allah, send salawat on the Prophet, then recite a comprehensive dua. The dua asks for the causes of mercy, forgiveness, gain from righteousness, and safety from sin. The commentary notes differences of opinion on the number of rak'ahs: two, four, or twelve (as in al-Hawi). The phrase 'to Allah or to any of the children of Adam' is explained to mean that ultimately all needs are from Allah, but one may need an intermediary. This prayer is thus a means of supplication for any lawful need. The Hanafi school regards it as a confirmed sunnah, based on the explicit hadith.

Key Terms
صلاة الحاجة (ṣalāt al-ḥājah): A prayer performed to request a specific need from Allah, often with a detailed dua.
موجبات رحمتك (mujibāt raḥmatik): Things that necessitate or bring about Allah's mercy.
عزائم مغفرتك (azā'im maghfiratik): The determined decrees of forgiveness; asking for the full, firm realization of forgiveness.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Salat al-Istikhara: Ruling and Proof
Ruling with proof on istikhara and its supplication.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on istikhara, identify its proof, and apply its conditions for validity.

Core Idea
Istikhara is recommended for uncertain matters; act on genuine heart inclination free from whim.

Students often wonder whether istikhara must be followed by a dream or sign. This lesson clarifies that the Hanafi school regards it as a recommended prayer (mustahabb) for uncertain matters, with the key indicator being a genuine expansion of the chest after repeating the supplication. We analyze the proof and practical application.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its basis
Read the passage to determine the legal classification (ḥukm) of istikhara and the evidence cited.
The text explicitly uses 'nadb' (recommendation).
2
Analyze the proof (dalīl)
Examine the hadith from Anas: the imperative 'fastakhir' (seek guidance) is interpreted as recommendation not obligation, due to contextual indicators and consensus.
The dalīl is a Sunnah āḥād transmitted by 'Jamā'ah' except Muslim.
3
Determine the scope of istikhara
List which matters istikhara is for (uncertain) and which it is not for (known good/bad). Note the exception for timing of acts like Hajj.
The commentary expands that istikhara can be used to choose the time of a known good act.
4
Apply the condition of 'expansion of chest'
Understand 'inshirāh ṣadr' as a genuine inclination free from whims. The passage indicates that after istikhara one proceeds with what the heart settles on.
This is the practical indicator, not a dream or external sign.
5
Recite the supplication correctly
Identify the key phrases of the du'ā, the pronunciation of 'faqdirhu', and the recommended combination of narrations.
The text emphasizes correct Arabic: damm on dāl and kasr on rā'.

Order for me in my religion, my livelihood, and the outcome of my matter, or he said: the immediate and future of my matter. So turn it away from me and turn me away from it, and decree for me goodness wherever it is, then make me pleased with it. He said: And he specifies his need. Narrated by all except Muslim. And it is recommended to combine the two narrations and say: and the outcome of my matter, its immediate and future. And istikhara in Hajj, Jihad, and all doors of goodness is interpreted as determining the time, not the act itself. And when one performs istikhara, he proceeds with what his chest expands to. And it is recommended to repeat it seven times due to what was narrated from Anas: The Messenger of Allah said: O Anas, if you intend a matter, then seek guidance from your Lord in it seven times, then look to what precedes to your heart, for goodness is in it. He said: (And decree it for me) with damm of the dal and kasr, from the two patterns of nasr and daraba, meaning ordain it; it is not permissible to open it here because the opening is from qadara (with fatha) from the pattern of fataha, meaning ease and strength, and it is not appropriate here. He said: (Then bless me in it) meaning make for me from it extra goodness beyond its original goodness, and 'thumma' means 'waw', and ordering is based on what is observed. He said: (And if You know) meaning You know. He said: (So turn it away from me, etc.) Since turning away one specific one from the other does not necessarily imply turning the other away from it, he supplicates for turning each away from the other. He said: (Then make me pleased) and in a narration 'ardini' (make me satisfied). He said: (He said) and he specifies his need, meaning instead of the wording of the command as we presented, and it is recommended to begin the mentioned supplication with praise and salutation upon the Messenger of Allah. He said: (And istikhara in Hajj, Jihad, etc.) Know that the place of recommendation of istikhara is in matters where the servant does not know the correct course. As for what is known to be good or evil, such as acts of worship, good deeds, sins, and reprehensible acts, there is no need for istikhara in them. However, istikhara may be performed for determining the specific time, such as Hajj in this year due to the possibility of an enemy or tribulation. Therefore, it is good to perform istikhara in forbidding evil when dealing with a rebellious person who is feared to cause great general or specific harm by forbidding him. Although it is narrated in the hadith: 'The best jihad is a word of truth before a tyrant ruler', but if general harm to Muslims is feared, then he should not forbid; if he fears for himself, he may forbid, but the obligation falls away. Thus in al-'Ayni on al-Bukhari. He said: (He proceeds with what his chest expands to) meaning his heart, and it indicates that after istikhara, one of the two matters will happen without fail, and the meaning is that his chest expands with an expansion free from whims of the soul.
Source pages p. 398

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof regarding the prayer of istikhara (seeking guidance). The author, commenting on the matn, explains the recommended supplication and its details. The core ruling is that istikhara is recommended (mandub) when a person is uncertain about a matter. The evidence is the hadith from Anas in which the Prophet instructs repeating istikhara seven times and then acting upon what the heart inclines to, provided the inclination is free from whims. The commentary clarifies that istikhara is not for matters known to be good or evil, but for uncertain matters. It also specifies that for acts like Hajj and Jihad, istikhara pertains to timing rather than the act itself. The commentator discusses the wording of the supplication, emphasizing correct pronunciation and the inclusion of blessing. He also addresses exceptions, such as forbidding evil when harm is feared, citing a hadith about jihad and the ruling that obligation falls away when general harm is feared. Finally, the commentary clarifies that 'expansion of the chest' refers to a genuine inclination, not one driven by desire.

Key Terms
استخارة (istikhārah): A recommended prayer of two rak'ahs accompanied by a specific supplication, performed to seek guidance from Allah when one is uncertain about a matter.
انشراح صدر (inshirāḥ ṣadr): An expansion of the chest indicating a genuine inclination towards a course of action, free from whims and desires, after performing istikhara.
ندب (nadb): Recommendation; a legal category between sunnah and mubah in Hanafi fiqh.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Deciding whether to perform the obligatory Fajr prayer
B) Choosing between two equally permissible job offers
C) Whether to commit a sin in secret
D) Determining which day to perform Hajj in a year with no obstacles

Key Takeaway
Istikhara is a recommended prayer for uncertain matters; the sign to act is a genuine heart inclination free from desire, not a dream.

The Prayer of Need (Salat al-Haja): Ruling, Evidence, and Practice
Ruling and supplication for the prayer of need

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on salat al-haja, identify its prescribed steps from the hadith, and explain the permissibility of tawassul.

Core Idea
The prayer of need is a recommended act with a precise prophetic sequence.

Although many Muslims know salat al-haja as a general practice, the detailed hadith from Abdullah ibn Abi Awfa provides a precise sequence of actions and supplication. This lesson unpacks the Hanafi ruling, the evidence, and the nuances regarding the number of rak'ahs and the permissibility of tawassul.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what 'salat al-haja' is and what legal ruling it carries in the Hanafi school (mustahabb).
The text explicitly says 'nadb' (recommendation).
2
Locate the dalil (proof)
Find the hadith cited from Abdullah ibn Abi Awfa and note its content.
The hadith is the primary evidence; its authenticity is affirmed by al-Tabarani.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah (implication of the proof)
Understand why the imperative in the hadith indicates recommendation, not obligation.
The context of fulfilling needs shifts the imperative to nadb.
4
Analyze the ikhtilaf (disagreement) on rak'ahs
Note the differences in the number of rak'ahs mentioned (two, four, twelve) and the mufta bihi view.
The commentary mentions variants but does not explicitly resolve; common practice is two.

And recommended is the prayer of need, and it is two rak'ahs. From Abdullah ibn Abi Awfa: The Messenger of Allah said: Whoever has a need from Allah or from any of the children of Adam, let him perform ablution well, then pray two rak'ahs, then praise Allah and send blessings upon the Prophet, then say: 'There is no god but Allah, the Forbearing, the Generous. Glory be to Allah, Lord of the Great Throne. Praise be to Allah, Lord of the worlds. I ask You for the causes of Your mercy and the determinants of Your forgiveness, and the gain of every goodness and safety from every sin. Do not leave any sin for me except that You forgive it, nor any worry except that You relieve it, nor any need that is pleasing to You except that You fulfill it. O Most Merciful of the merciful.' And from his supplication: 'O Allah, I ask You and I turn to You by Your Prophet Muhammad, the Prophet of mercy. O Muhammad, I turn to You by your Lord concerning my need so that He may fulfill it for me. O Allah, intercede him for me.' He said: (And it is two rak'ahs or four, and in al-Hawi it is twelve rak'ahs with one taslim, as the sayyid said.) He said: (To Allah) meaning without the intermediary of the children of Adam, and his saying: 'or to any of the children of Adam' means what occurs through their hands, otherwise all needs are from Allah. He said: 'I ask You for the causes of Your mercy' meaning the things that necessitate mercy and kindness from You. And his saying: 'and the determinants of Your forgiveness' meaning the things that necessitate the forgiveness of sins completely, as if they compel that. He said: (And the gain of every goodness) meaning every good, i.e., I ask You to make my gain and my gift every good. He said: (O Most Merciful of the merciful) then he asks whatever he wishes of worldly and otherworldly matters, for it will be decreed for him. Thus in Ibn Amir Haj. He said: (And from his supplication) meaning the supplication for fulfilling need after the prayer, or from his supplication that he taught to a blind man who came to him, saying: O Messenger of Allah, pray to Allah to heal me. He said: If you wish, you may delay that, and it will be greater for your reward; and if you wish, I will pray. He said: Pray to Allah. So he commanded him to perform ablution well, pray two rak'ahs, and supplicate with this supplication. End. And it has many chains. Al-Tabarani said after mentioning its chains: The hadith is authentic. He said: 'I turn to you by your Lord' etc. This is problematic based on what they said: it is disliked for a man to say: 'O Allah, I ask You by Your prophets.' The answer is that hearing is specific to this, and the truth is there is no specificity, as is established in the istisqa of Umar with al-Abbas. And what was said regarding the reason for dislike—that no one has a right over Allah—is debatable, because sincere servants have a right over Him, a grace and generosity from Him, and He made it obligatory upon Himself, and they have an intrinsic entitlement. The full discussion is in Ibn Amir Haj.
Source pages p. 398

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof for the prayer of need (salat al-haja). The matn states that this prayer is recommended (mandub), consisting of two rak'ahs. The proof is the hadith from Abdullah ibn Abi Awfa where the Prophet prescribes this practice. The commentary expands on the number of rak'ahs, mentioning that some say four or even twelve, and clarifies the wording of the supplication. The commentator explains that 'to Allah' means without human intermediary, while 'to a human' refers to needs that are fulfilled through people, though ultimately all needs come from Allah. The supplication emphasizes seeking the causes of mercy and determinants of forgiveness, and includes a famous phrase 'O Most Merciful of the merciful.' The commentary also addresses the issue of asking by the Prophet, noting that it is not disliked because of precedents like Umar's istisqa through al-Abbas, and that sincere believers have a right upon Allah by His grace. The ritual includes performing ablution well, praying two rak'ahs, praising Allah, sending blessings on the Prophet, and reciting the specified supplication.

Key Terms
صلاة الحاجة (ṣalāt al-ḥājah): A supererogatory prayer performed to ask Allah for the fulfillment of a specific need.
موجبات رحمتك (mūjibāt raḥmatika): The causes or things that necessitate mercy, i.e., actions or qualities that draw Allah's mercy.
التوسل (al-tawassul): Seeking closeness to Allah through an intermediary, such as a prophet or righteous person.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the hadith in the lesson, what is the first step recommended for someone with a need?
A) Praying two rak'ahs immediately
B) Reciting the supplication without prayer
C) Performing ablution and doing it well
D) Giving charity

Key Takeaway
The prayer of need (salat al-haja) is a recommended practice combining ablution, two rak'ahs, praise, blessings, and a comprehensive supplication, rooted in prophetic instruction and affirmed by Hanafi scholars.

Reviving Specific Nights: Recommendations and the Dispute on Laylat al-Qadr
Explains recommended revival of specific nights and key intra-Hanafi dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the nights whose revival is recommended in the Hanafi school, identify the proof for reviving the last ten nights of Ramadan, and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute on the timing of Laylat al-Qadr and its practical consequence.

Core Idea
The Hanafi fatwa on Laylat al-Qadr is flexible, allowing it to move within Ramadan to encourage maximum devotion.

This passage from Hashiya al-Tahtawi explains the sunnah acts of reviving specific nights—the last ten of Ramadan, the two Eids, the ten of Dhul Hijjah, and others—and highlights a critical intra-Hanafi debate over when Laylat al-Qadr falls. The mufta bihi position is Abu Hanifa's view that it is not fixed, ensuring believers seek it throughout the month.

Guided Path
1
Identify the recommended nights
List all the nights whose revival is recommended in this passage: the last ten nights of Ramadan, the nights of Eid al-Fitr and Eid al-Adha, the nights of the ten days of Dhul Hijjah, and the night of mid-Sha'ban (though the text breaks off). Note the recommended acts: prayer, dhikr, supplication, and seeking forgiveness.
Revival (ihya') means staying awake in worship; it is mustahabb, not wajib.
2
Analyze the primary dalil for the last ten nights
Examine the hadith of Aisha (RA) cited: the Prophet would revive the night, wake his family, and tighten his garment during the last ten days. In Hanafi usul, the Prophet's fi'l indicates istihbab (recommendation) because it lacks an explicit command. The purpose is to seek Laylat al-Qadr.
The hadith is sahih (qat'i al-thubut) but its implication zanni.
3
Understand the virtue of Laylat al-Qadr and wisdom of concealment
The passage explains that worship in Laylat al-Qadr is better than a thousand months. The wisdom of its concealment is to motivate believers to exert themselves in many nights, increasing worship.
Al-Nawawi's quote confirms the school's view on its existence and concealment.
4
Examine the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on timing
Abu Hanifa holds that Laylat al-Qadr is not fixed to a specific night; it can be early or late within Ramadan, and may even fall outside Ramadan. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad hold it is within the last ten nights, especially odd nights. The text notes that the fatwa is on Abu Hanifa's view.
The evidence for Abu Hanifa includes Ibn Mas'ud's statement and the absence of precise specification by the Prophet.
5
Apply the disagreement to a concrete case
If a master says to his slave 'You are free on Laylat al-Qadr' after some days of Ramadan have passed, according to the Sahibayn the slave is freed after that portion of the current Ramadan. According to Abu Hanifa, he is not freed until the entire next Ramadan passes, because it is possible Laylat al-Qadr falls in the coming year.
The fatwa follows Abu Hanifa's view, making the ruling more cautious and encouraging lifelong devotion.

Book of Prayer. 399. And no worry except You relieve it, and no need in which there is Your pleasure except You fulfill it, O Most Merciful of the merciful. And from his supplication: O Allah, I ask You and I turn to You by Your Prophet Muhammad, the Prophet of mercy. O Muhammad, I turn by you to your Lord concerning this need of mine so that You may fulfill it. O Allah, accept his intercession for me. And it is recommended to revive the last ten nights of Ramadan based on what is reported from Aisha (may Allah be pleased with her) that the Prophet (peace be upon him) when the last ten days of Ramadan entered, he would revive the night, wake his family, and tighten his garment. The purpose of that is to revive Laylat al-Qadr, for action in it is better than action in a thousand months devoid of it. Ahmad narrated: Whoever stands in prayer on Laylat al-Qadr with faith and seeking reward, his previous sins are forgiven. :. 'Your forgiveness' means the things that necessitate forgiveness of sins completely as if they guarantee that. His saying: 'and the spoils of every righteousness' means every good, i.e., I ask You to make my spoils and gift every good. His saying: 'O Most Merciful of the merciful' then he asks regarding worldly and afterlife matters whatever he wishes, for it will be decreed for him. Thus in Ibn Amir Haj. His saying: 'And from his supplication' i.e., the supplication for fulfilling a need after prayer, or from his supplication which he taught to a blind man who came to him, saying: O Messenger of Allah, pray to Allah to cure me. He said: If you wish, I will delay that, as it is greater for your reward; and if you wish, I will pray. He said: Pray to Allah. So he ordered him to perform ablution properly, pray two rak'ahs, and make this supplication. End. It has many chains. Al-Tabarani said after mentioning its chains: The hadith is authentic. His saying: 'I turn by you' etc. is problematic regarding what they said: It is disliked for a man to say: O Allah, I ask You by Your prophets. The answer is that hearing is specific to this, and the truth is that there is no specificity because of what is reported in the istisqa' of Umar by al-Abbas. What is said regarding the reason for dislike, that no one has a right over Allah, is debatable because the sincere servants have a right over Him, as a favor and generosity He has made obligatory upon Himself, and they have an intrinsic entitlement. Its completion is in Ibn Amir Haj. His saying: 'tighten his garment' means he exerted himself in worship. His saying: 'for action in it etc.' It is narrated that a man from the Children of Israel was mentioned who wore armor in the path of Allah for a thousand months, and the Muslims were amazed. So Allah revealed Surah al-Qadr, i.e., Laylat al-Qadr is better than the thousand months in which that man wore armor in the path of Allah. It is also narrated that four from the Children of Israel were mentioned: they worshiped Allah for eighty years without disobeying Him for the blink of an eye. He mentioned Ayyub, Zakariyya, Hizqil, and Yusha' ibn Nun (peace be upon them). The Companions were amazed at that, so Jibril descended and said: O Muhammad, your nation marvels at the worship of these few for eighty years without disobeying Allah for the blink of an eye. Indeed, Allah has sent down to you something better than that. He recited the surah. So this is better than what you and your nation marveled at. The Prophet (peace be upon him) and the people with him rejoiced. A thousand months is eighty-three years and four months. Al-Nawawi said: Allah has distinguished this nation with it; it was not for those before them according to the correct and well-known opinion. Those whose opinion is considered have agreed upon its existence and its continuity until the end of time due to well-known hadiths, and that it is seen truly by whom Allah wills in every Ramadan as the hadiths indicate. It is recommended to conceal it for those who see it, following him (peace be upon him). The wisdom in its concealment is that those who seek it will exert themselves in reviving many nights striving to coincide with it, thus increasing their worship of Allah. End. His saying: 'seek reward' means seeking to store up its reward with Allah. 400 Book of Prayer. His previous and future sins are forgiven. And he said: Seek Laylat al-Qadr in the last ten nights of Ramadan. Agreed upon. Ibn Mas'ud (may Allah be pleased with him) said: It is throughout the entire year. The Great Imam (Abu Hanifa) according to the well-known view from him held that it rotates throughout the year; it may occur in Ramadan or other than it. Qadi Khan said this. In al-Mabsut, the madhhab according to Abu Hanifa is that it occurs in Ramadan but may be early or late, while according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) it is neither early nor late. And it is recommended to revive the two nights of the two Eids (al-Fitr and al-Adha) based on the hadith: Whoever revives the night of Eid, Allah will revive his heart on the day when hearts die. And it is recommended to increase seeking forgiveness at dawn, and the master of seeking forgiveness is: O Allah, You are my Lord; there is no god but You; You created me and I am Your servant; I am upon Your covenant and promise as best I can; I seek refuge in You from the evil of what I have done; I acknowledge Your favor upon me and I acknowledge my sin; so forgive me, for none forgives sins but You. And supplication in them is answered. And it is recommended to revive the nights of the ten days of Dhul Hijjah based on His saying: There are no days more beloved to Allah than these ten days of Dhul Hijjah; fasting each day equals fasting a year, and standing each night equals standing on Laylat al-Qadr. And he said: Fasting the day of Arafah expiates two years: one past and one future; and fasting Ashura expiates one past year. And it is recommended to revive the night of the half (of Sha'ban). His saying: 'in the last ten' - most imams said it is specifically in the odd nights, and the even nights are equal, and some said the odd nights are more emphatic. The majority held that it is the 27th night, which is the saying of Ibn Abbas and a group of Companions. Al-Ayni in his commentary on al-Bukhari attributed this to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). His saying: 'but it advances and delays' - the practical implication appears in the case of someone who says to his slave: You are free on Laylat al-Qadr, and some of Ramadan has passed. According to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), he is not freed until that part of the current Ramadan passes; according to him (Abu Hanifa), he is not freed until the entire next Ramadan passes, and the fatwa is on this because it is possible that it occurs at the end of the coming year. His saying: 'it is recommended to increase seeking forgiveness at dawn' - for Allah praised those who seek forgiveness at dawn, saying: And at dawn they seek forgiveness. His saying: 'the master of seeking forgiveness: O Allah etc.' is a subject and predicate, i.e., it is more worthy than others. The consequence of it being the master is that it fulfills an oath if one swears to seek forgiveness by the master of seeking forgiveness. His saying: 'I am upon Your covenant' i.e., what You have covenanted me with regarding obedience. His saying: 'and Your promise' i.e., Your promise of reward for compliance. In Sharh al-Masabih: i.e., I am steadfast in fulfilling the covenant You made with me in pre-eternity of Your lordship, and I am certain of Your promise of resurrection, spreading, conditions of the Hereafter, reward and punishment. End. His saying: 'I acknowledge' (Abu'u) is on the pattern of 'aqulu', with a hamza at the end, meaning I admit and confess. His saying: 'and supplication in them is answered' - the antecedent is likely the two (Eid nights), or possibly refers to the genus of the nights mentioned in the hadith. His saying: 'equals' (yu'dalu) is passive voice. His saying: 'Fasting the day of Arafah etc.' - so it is recommended to fast it except for the pilgrim, because he might become weak by fasting for what is required of him that day. They said: The wisdom in adding the expiation of fasting Arafah over fasting Ashura is that it is from the Sharia of our master Muhammad (peace be upon him), while fasting Ashura is from the Sharia of Kalim (Moses, peace be upon him), and the law of Muhammad is superior. His saying: 'and because it is decreed in it' (incomplete).
Source pages p. 399

Commentary
This passage from Hashiya al-Tahtawi is a critical refinement (hashiya) on Maraqi al-Falah, explaining the recommended (mustahabb) acts of reviving specific nights. It opens with the famous supplication taught to a blind man by the Prophet (peace be upon him), which is a strong sunnah. Then it dives into the main topic: reviving the last ten nights of Ramadan, especially Laylat al-Qadr. The author presents the hadith of Aisha (may Allah be pleased with her) describing the Prophet's practice and explains that the virtue of Laylat al-Qadr is immense, better than a thousand months. He then details an intra-Hanafi dispute: Imam Abu Hanifa (the Great Imam) held that Laylat al-Qadr is not fixed to a specific night but rotates throughout the year, sometimes in Ramadan and sometimes elsewhere, or within Ramadan it can be early or late. The two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) held it is specifically in the last ten nights of Ramadan. The text mentions that the fatwa is on Abu Hanifa's view, as it affects rulings like manumission tied to Laylat al-Qadr. The passage then moves to other recommended nights: the two Eid nights, the nights of the ten days of Dhul Hijjah, the day of Arafah (fasting), Ashura, and the night of mid-Sha'ban (though the last is cut off). The author also recommends the 'master of supplications' (Sayyid al-Istighfar) at dawn and notes its virtue in fulfilling oaths. Throughout, the style is that of a hashiya: it explains obscure points, resolves apparent contradictions, and provides the later relied-upon position. The overall lesson: the Hanafi school encourages seeking these blessed times through worship, with Laylat al-Qadr being the greatest but not exclusively in the last ten nights according to the official fatwa.

Key Terms
إحياء ليالي (ihya' al-layali): The act of staying awake in worship during the night, including prayer, recitation, dhikr, and supplication.
ليلة القدر (Laylat al-Qadr): The Night of Decree, considered the most blessed night of the year; worship in it surpasses a thousand months.
سيد الاستغفار (Sayyid al-Istighfar): The 'master of seeking forgiveness' — a specific supplication that the Prophet taught as the best form of istighfar.
الوتر (al-witr): Odd numbers; here refers to the odd nights of the last ten days of Ramadan (21st, 23rd, 25th, 27th, 29th).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position (mufta bihi) stated in this passage, when does Laylat al-Qadr occur?
A) It is fixed on the 27th night of Ramadan.
B) It is only in the odd nights of the last ten days of Ramadan.
C) It can be any night throughout the entire year.
D) It occurs in Ramadan but may be early or late, and could even fall in the next Ramadan.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school recommends reviving specific nights, especially the last ten of Ramadan, and the mufta bihi position on Laylat al-Qadr is that it can vary each year to encourage extended devotion.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
6 min
The Timing of Laylat al-Qadr: Abu Hanifa vs. the Sahibayn
Explains the ruling on seeking Laylat al-Qadr and the disagreement between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute on Laylat al-Qadr timing and apply the mufta bihi position to a conditional vow scenario.

Core Idea
Laylat al-Qadr is not fixed; it rotates yearly, affecting vows contingent on it.

This passage addresses the deeply debated question of Laylat al-Qadr's exact timing. While the hadith instructs us to seek it in the last ten nights, the Hanafi school, particularly Imam Abu Hanifa, held a unique view that it rotates throughout the year. The practical consequence emerges in a vow to free a slave on Laylat al-Qadr, showing how even a seemingly theoretical ikhtilaf has real-world application.

Guided Path
1
Identify the hadith and its scope
The hadith 'Search for Laylat al-Qadr in the last ten nights' commands a search but does not specify the exact night. This ambiguity opens the door for ikhtilaf.
Note: The command is to search, implying recommendation, not obligation.
2
Contrast the positions
Abu Hanifa (in the well-known narration) holds that Laylat al-Qadr revolves throughout the year, sometimes in Ramadan, sometimes outside. The Sahibayn hold it is fixed, likely the 27th night.
The text also mentions a narration from al-Mabsut that restricts it to Ramadan but allows variation within Ramadan.
3
Locate the tarjih
The fatwa is upon Abu Hanifa's view because of the possibility that Laylat al-Qadr may occur at the end of the next Ramadan.
Tarjih is based on the likelihood that the night is not confined to a fixed date.
4
Apply to the vow scenario
If a man says to his slave 'You are free on Laylat al-Qadr' and part of Ramadan has passed, according to the Sahibayn the slave is freed after that part of the current Ramadan, according to Abu Hanifa the slave is not freed until after the next entire Ramadan.
The difference arises because Abu Hanifa allows the possibility that Laylat al-Qadr may fall at the end of the next year.
5
Summarize the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position for fatwa is that Laylat al-Qadr is in Ramadan but varies from year to year. Vows should be framed with this in mind.
This view encourages consistent devotion throughout the year.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقال : تحروا ليلة القدر في العشر الأواخر من رمضان متفق عليه وقال ابن مسعود رضي الله عنه : هي في كل السنة وبه قال الإمام الأعظم في المشهور عنه : أنها تدور في السنة وقد تكون في رمضان وقد تكون في غيره قاله قاضي خان، وفي المبسوط أن المذهب عند أبي حنيفة أنها تكون في رمضان لكن تتقدم وتتأخر وعندهما لا تتقدم ولا تتأخر قوله: (في العشر الأواخر ) قال معظم الأئمة أنها مختصة بها الوتر، والشفع في ذلك للسواء، وقال بعضهم : ليالي الوتر آكد، وذهب الأكثر إلى أنها ليلة سبع وعشرين وهو قول ابن عباس وجماعة من الصحابة ونسبه العيني في شرح البخاري إلى الصاحبين قوله: (لكن تتقدم، وتتأخر) والثمرة تظهر فيمن قال لعبده أنت حر ليلة القدر، وقد مضى بعض من رمضان فعندهما لا يعتق حتى يمضي ذلك البعض من رمضان العاجل وعنده حتى يمضي رمضان القابل كله، وعليه الفتوى لإحتمال أنها تكون في آخره في العام القابل.
And he said: 'Search for Laylat al-Qadr in the last ten nights of Ramadan' (agreed upon). And Ibn Mas'ud (may Allah be pleased with him) said: 'It is throughout the whole year,' and the Greatest Imam followed this in the well-known narration: that it revolves throughout the year, sometimes in Ramadan and sometimes outside it, as stated by Qadi Khan. In al-Mabsut, the madhhab according to Abu Hanifa is that it is in Ramadan but may be earlier or later, while according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) it does not advance or delay. His statement: '(in the last ten nights)': most of the imams said that it is specific to the odd nights, and the even are equal in that. Some said the odd nights are more emphatic. The majority held that it is the 27th night, which is the saying of Ibn 'Abbas and a group of Companions, and al-'Aini in his commentary on al-Bukhari attributed it to the two. His statement: '(but it advances and delays)': the practical consequence appears concerning someone who says to his slave, 'You are free on Laylat al-Qadr,' and part of Ramadan has passed. According to the two, he is not freed until that part of the current Ramadan passes; according to him (Abu Hanifa), until the whole next Ramadan passes. And the fatwa is upon his view, due to the possibility that it may be at the end of the next year.
Source pages p. 400

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the timing of Laylat al-Qadr. The author first cites the hadith commanding to seek it in the last ten nights of Ramadan. He then presents the view of Ibn Mas'ud and Abu Hanifa that Laylat al-Qadr is not fixed to a specific night; it rotates throughout the year and may occur in Ramadan or outside it. However, the more reliable narration from al-Mabsut states that Abu Hanifa holds it to be in Ramadan but varying from year to year—sometimes earlier, sometimes later. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that it is fixed on the 27th night. The commentary clarifies the majority view that it is the 27th, but the fatwa is given on Abu Hanifa's view because of the possibility it could be at the end of the upcoming year. A concrete legal application is given: if someone makes a vow to free his slave on Laylat al-Qadr, the timing of the freeing depends on this ikhtilaf.

Key Terms
ليلة القدر (Laylat al-Qadr): The Night of Decree, a night of great virtue in which the Quran was revealed; worship on this night is better than a thousand months.
تدور في السنة (tadūru fī al-sannah): Literally 'revolves in the year,' meaning Laylat al-Qadr is not confined to a fixed date but moves across the calendar year.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position in this passage, what happens if a man says to his slave 'You are free on Laylat al-Qadr' and part of Ramadan has passed?
A) The slave is freed immediately after the statement.
B) The slave is not freed until that part of the current Ramadan passes (according to the Sahibayn).
C) The slave is freed until the whole next Ramadan passes (according to Abu Hanifa).
D) The man must specify which Ramadan he means, otherwise the vow is invalid.

Key Takeaway
The relied-upon Hanafi position is that Laylat al-Qadr rotates yearly, so vows contingent on it may extend to the next year.

Recommended Vigil on the Two Eids and Sayyid al-Istighfar
Ruling on the recommendation to stay awake on Eid nights, with the virtue of seeking forgiveness and the best supplication

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on reviving the nights of the two Eids and recite the Sayyid al-Istighfar supplication with its legal basis.

Core Idea
Reviving Eid nights is a recommended sunnah; the best istighfar is Sayyid al-Istighfar.

This passage from Hashiya al-Tahtawi highlights two recommended acts: staying awake on the nights of Eid al-Fitr and Eid al-Adha, and the virtue of Sayyid al-Istighfar. The ruling is based on a hadith promising divine reward. Let us examine the proof and the wording of this special supplication.

Guided Path
1
Identify the acts and their rulings
The passage begins by stating the recommendation (nudub) to revive the nights of the two Eids. Then it recommends increasing istighfar at dawn and presents Sayyid al-Istighfar as the best form. Note the legal category: sunnah muakkadah.
The term 'nudiba' indicates a recommended act, not obligatory.
2
Locate the dalil for the first ruling
The proof is a hadith: 'Whoever revives the night of Eid, Allah will revive his heart on the day when hearts die.' This is a non-mutawatir hadith, providing zanni evidence.
The hadith is cited as evidence for the virtue; its chain is not elaborated.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The promise of reviving the heart on a difficult day indicates great merit, which motivates the recommended act. The ruling of nudub is derived from the encouragement implied in the promise.
The hadith does not command; it motivates, hence recommendation.
4
Understand the second part: Sayyid al-Istighfar
The passage then states the recommendation to increase istighfar and provides the exact wording of Sayyid al-Istighfar. This is a well-known supplication from Sahih al-Bukhari.
The phrase 'sayyid al-istighfar' indicates its superior status among istighfar forms.
5
Note the thamarah (fruit) of the ruling
Engaging in ihyā' on Eid nights and reciting Sayyid al-Istighfar brings reward and forgiveness. The passage also notes that supplication during these nights is answered.
This encourages diligence in worship on these blessed occasions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
و) ندب (إحياء ليلتي العيدين الفطر والأضحى لحديث من أحيا ليلة العيد أحيا الله قلبه يوم تموت القلوب ويستحب الإكثار من الاستغفار بالأسحار، وسيد الاستغفار اللهم أنت ربي لا إله إلا أنت خلقتني وأنا عبدك وأنا على عهدك ووعدك ما استطعت أعوذ بك من شر ما صنعت أبوء لك بنعمتك علي وأبوء بذنبي فاغفر لي فإنه لا يغفر الذنوب إلا أنت والدعاء فيها مستجاب
(And) it is recommended to revive the nights of the two Eids, Fitr and Adha, due to the hadith: 'Whoever revives the night of Eid, Allah will revive his heart on the day when hearts die.' And it is recommended to increase seeking forgiveness at dawns. The master of seeking forgiveness is: 'O Allah, You are my Lord, there is no god but You, You created me and I am Your servant, and I am upon Your covenant and promise as much as I am able. I seek refuge in You from the evil of what I have done. I acknowledge Your favor upon me and I acknowledge my sin, so forgive me, for none forgives sins but You.' And supplication during them (these nights) is answered.
Source pages p. 400

Commentary
This passage states a ruling of recommendation (nudub) to stay awake and engage in worship on the nights of the two Eids (Eid al-Fitr and Eid al-Adha). The proof is a hadith promising that Allah will revive the heart of one who does so on the Day when hearts die. The commentary adds that increasing istighfar (seeking forgiveness) at dawn is recommended, and it presents Sayyid al-Istighfar (the master supplication for forgiveness) as the most virtuous form. The text also notes that supplication during these nights is answered. This is part of the broader category of recommended night vigils (ihya') in the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
إحياء (iḥyā'): Literally 'giving life'; here it means staying awake at night engaged in worship such as prayer, dhikr, and supplication.
سيد الاستغفار (Sayyid al-Istighfār): The 'master of seeking forgiveness,' a particular supplication (dua) considered the best form of istighfar.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Reviving the nights of the two Eids is a recommended sunnah; Sayyid al-Istighfar is the most virtuous form of seeking forgiveness.

Recommended Worship on the Ten Days of Dhul Hijjah
Ruling on the recommendation to worship during the ten days of Dhul Hijjah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the recommended acts during the first ten days of Dhul Hijjah and explain their virtue based on the hadith proof.

Core Idea
Worship in the first ten days of Dhul Hijjah is recommended with immense reward: fasting each day equals a year, and each night equals Laylat al-Qadr.

This lesson presents the Hanafi ruling on the recommendation (nudub) to revive the nights of the first ten days of Dhul Hijjah. The source text from Maraqi al-Falah, accompanied by a hadith, outlines the unparalleled virtue of these days and specifies the reward for fasting and prayer. Understanding this ruling enables you to apply the correct intention and maximize benefit during this blessed period.

Guided Path
1
Identify the recommended act and its ruling
The passage states 'it is recommended to revive the nights of the ten days of Dhul Hijjah.' The word 'nudiba' indicates a ruling of sunnah/mandub, not obligation.
The act includes both fasting during the days and staying awake in worship at night.
2
Locate the dalil
The hadith is cited: 'There are no days in which worship is more beloved to Allah than these ten days...' This is a hadith ahad (single-chain narration), zanni al-thubut.
The hadith is reported by Ahmad and others.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The phrase 'more beloved' (ahabba) and 'equals' (ya'dilu) indicate great merit but not obligation. The Hanafi principle is that such expressions establish recommendation (nadb) rather than compulsion.
The absence of a direct command (amr) supports the non-obligatory nature.
4
Acknowledge cross-madhhab agreement
All schools agree on the virtue of these days, but the Hanafi school emphasizes the recommendation of fasting and qiyam. The hadith is accepted by all.
The reward for Arafah and Ashura is also mentioned; they are recommended but not exclusive to Hanafi.
5
Apply to practice
For a non-pilgrim, fasting all ten days is recommended. For a pilgrim, fasting on Arafah is not recommended if it weakens them. The night vigil can be performed individually or in congregation.
The ruling is practical and context-sensitive.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
و) ندب إحياء (ليالي عشر ذي الحجة) لقوله : «ما من أيام أحب إلى الله تعالى أن يتعبد فيها من عشر ذي الحجة يعدل صيام كل يوم منها بصيام سنة وقيام كل ليلة منها بقيام ليلة القدر وقال : «صوم يوم عرفة يكفر سنتين ماضية ومستقبلة وصوم عاشوراء يكفر سنة ماضية
(And) it is recommended to revive the nights of the ten days of Dhul Hijjah, due to his saying: 'There are no days in which worship is more beloved to Allah the Exalted than the ten days of Dhul Hijjah. And he said: 'Fasting the day of Arafah expiates two years: the past and the future, and fasting Ashura expiates one year past.'
Source pages p. 400

Commentary
This passage presents the recommendation (nudub) to revive the nights of the first ten days of Dhul Hijjah, which includes staying awake in worship and fasting during the days. The proof is a hadith stating that these are the most beloved days for worship, with immense rewards: fasting each day equals a year of fasting, and worshipping at night equals the reward of Laylat al-Qadr. Additionally, fasting on the day of Arafah (9th Dhul Hijjah) expiates sins of two years, and fasting Ashura (10th Muharram) expiates one year. The commentary from the hashia notes that these virtues are special for the Hanafi school, and the reward for Arafah is greater because it is from the Shariah of Prophet Muhammad (SAW) compared to Ashura from Musa (AS).

Key Terms
عشر ذي الحجة (ʿashr dhī al-ḥijjah): The first ten days of the Islamic month of Dhul Hijjah, a period of special virtue for worship.
صوم عرفة (ṣawm ʿarafah): Fasting on the 9th of Dhul Hijjah, recommended especially for non-pilgrims.
