Fasting and night worship during the first ten days of Dhul Hijjah carry immense reward and are recommended (sunnah muakkadah) in the Hanafi school.

Recommended Vigil on Mid-Sha'ban and Other Virtuous Nights
Ruling on recommending revival of certain nights

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on reviving the night of mid-Sha'ban, explain the hadith proofs, and clarify the theological interpretation of Allah's descent.

Core Idea
Reviving the night of mid-Sha'ban is a strong sunna, promised Paradise, with Allah's descent understood figuratively.

The Hanafi school strongly recommends staying awake on the night of mid-Sha'ban and other blessed nights, citing multiple hadith that promise great rewards. However, the proof texts require careful understanding, especially regarding the description of Allah's descent. This lesson unpacks the ruling, the evidence, and the correct theological stance.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruled Act and Its Ruling
Determine what exactly is being recommended (the act of qiyam on specific nights) and the legal level (sunnah muakkadah).
The text uses 'nudiba' which indicates recommendation, not obligation.
2
Locate the Dalil (Proof)
Identify the hadith cited: 'When it is the night of mid-Sha'ban, stand its night and fast its day...' and others. Note that these are ahad hadith.
The thubut is zanni, which affects the wajh al-dalalah.
3
Trace the Wajh al-Dalalah (How the Proof Yields the Ruling)
The imperative 'faqoomu' indicates recommendation due to the weakness of the hadith; otherwise, a command would indicate obligation in Hanafi usul. The promise of Paradise in other hadith elevates the act to sunnah muakkadah.
The hadith about five nights ensures Paradise, reinforcing the recommendation.
4
Note the Ikhtilaf (Scholarly Disagreement)
While Hanafis consider it sunnah muakkadah, some Malikis and others are cautious about the specific hadith and do not emphasize it as much. The passage acknowledges this with the mention of 'some other schools'.
The difference is about authenticity of the hadith, not the principle of reviving a night.
5
Evaluate the Theological Clarification
The hashia clarifies that Allah's 'descent' is either descent of His command/angels or an attribute not like creation, following the path of tanzih (transcendence). Ensure not to take it literally.
This is important to avoid anthropomorphism.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
و) ندب إحياء ليلة النصف من شعبان لأنها تكفر ذنوب السنة، وليلة الجمعة تكفر ذنوب الأسبوع، وليلة القدر تكفر ذنوب العمر، ولأنها يقدر فيها الأرزاق والآجال والإغناء والأفقار والأعزاز والإذلال والإحياء والإماتة وعدد الحاج وفيها يسح الله تعالى الخير سحاً، وخمس ليال لا يرد فيهن الدعاء ليلة الجمعة وأول ليلة من رجب وليلة النصف من شعبان وليلتا العيدين، وقال : إذا كان ليلة النصف من شعبان فقوموا ليلها وصوموا نهارها فإن الله تعالى ينزل فيها الغروب الشمس إلى السماء فيقول ألا مستغفر فاغفر له الا مسترزق فأرزقه حتى يطلع الفجر» وقال : من أحيا الليال الخمس وجبت له الجنة ليلة التروية وليلة عرفة، وليلة النحر وليلة الفطر وليلة النصف من شعبان وقال : من قام ليلة النصف من شعبان وليلتي العيدين لم يمت قلبه يوم تموت القلوب ومعنى القيام أن يكون مشتغلاً معظم الليل بطاعة وقيل بساعة منه يقرأ، أو القرآن أو الحديث أو يسمع يسبح أو يصلي على النبي ، وعن ابن عباس بصلاة العشاء جماعة والعزم على صلاة الصبح جماعة كما في إحياء ليلتي الأرزاق) قال تعالى: (فيها يفرق كل أمر حكيم [الدخان ٤٤] . قوله: (وفيها يسح ) الله تعالى الخير سحاً) قال في القاموس السح الصب، والسيلان من فوق كالسح بالضم اهـ فشبه الخير بماء يصب من محل عال والمراد كثرة الخير . قوله : ( ينزل فيها أي ينزل أمره، أو ملائكته، أو النزول صفة له تعالى لا كصفة الحوادث على ما ذكروه من الطريقين. قوله: (ألا مستغفر الخ) ألا أداة استفتاح وأغفر له بالرفع لا بالجزم (۱) لأنه في جواب العرض مثلاً، وألا هنا ليست له لأنها تدخل على الأفعال قوله : (ليلة : التروية) هي ليلة الثامن من ذي الحجة. قوله: (لم يمت قلبه يوم تموت القلوب أي بمحبسة الدنيا حتى تصده عن الآخرة كما جاء لا تجالسوا الموتى يعني أهل الدنيا وقال بعضهم : لم يمت قلبه أي لا يتحير قلبه عند النزع، ولا في القبر، ولا في القيامة كذا في الشرح قوله : ( يقرأ، أو يسمع أو يدعو، وأحسن ما يدعو به اللهم إنك عفو كريم تحب العفو فاعف عنا .
(And) it is recommended to revive the night of mid-Sha'ban because it expiates the sins of the year; and Friday night expiates the sins of the week; and Laylat al-Qadr expiates the sins of a lifetime. And because therein provisions, lifespans, enrichment, impoverishment, honor, humiliation, life, and death are decreed, and the number of pilgrims. And in it Allah pours down goodness abundantly. And there are five nights in which supplication is not rejected: Friday night, the first night of Rajab, the night of mid-Sha'ban, and the nights of the two Eids. And he said: 'When it is the night of mid-Sha'ban, stand its night and fast its day, for indeed Allah descends at sunset to the lowest heaven and says: Is there anyone seeking forgiveness that I may forgive him? Is there anyone seeking sustenance that I may provide for him? until dawn breaks.' And he said: 'Whoever revives the five nights, Paradise becomes obligatory for him: the night of Tarwiyah, the night of Arafah, the night of Nahr, the night of Fitr, and the night of mid-Sha'ban.' And he said: 'Whoever stands (in prayer) the night of mid-Sha'ban and the nights of the two Eids, his heart will not die on the day when hearts die.' The meaning of 'standing' (qiyam) is that one occupies most of the night in obedience; it is said that even one hour of it (suffices), reciting, or listening, or supplicating, or glorifying, or sending blessings upon the Prophet. And from Ibn 'Abbas: by praying Isha in congregation and resolving to pray Fajr in congregation, as in the revival of the two nights... (He said): 'Therein is decreed every matter of wisdom' (Quran 44:4). His statement: 'and in it Allah pours goodness abundantly' – al-sahh means pouring, flow from above; so goodness is likened to water pouring from a high place, meaning abundant goodness. His statement: 'He descends' – meaning His command descends, or His angels, or the descent is an attribute of Him not like the attributes of created beings, according to the two approaches. His statement: 'Is there anyone seeking forgiveness?' – 'ala' is a particle of opening; 'aghfir lahu' is with the nominative, not the jussive, because it is in response to a presentation, and 'ala' here is not conditional. His statement: 'the night of Tarwiyah' is the night of the 8th of Dhul Hijjah. His statement: 'his heart will not die on the day when hearts die' – meaning due to love of this world preventing him from the Hereafter, as it came: 'Do not sit with the dead,' meaning people of this world. Some said: 'his heart will not die' means his heart will not be confounded at the time of death, nor in the grave, nor on the Day of Resurrection, as in the commentary. His statement: 'reciting, or listening, or supplicating' – and the best supplication is: 'O Allah, You are Pardoning, Generous, You love pardon, so pardon us.'
Source pages p. 401

Commentary
This passage expands on the recommendation to revive the night of mid-Sha'ban, along with other specific nights. The rulings are: (1) It is recommended (nudiba) to stay awake on the night of mid-Sha'ban, Friday night, Laylat al-Qadr, etc. (2) Each night has expiatory benefits: mid-Sha'ban for the year, Friday for the week, Laylat al-Qadr for a lifetime. (3) Five nights are particularly emphasized for supplication: Friday, first of Rajab, mid-Sha'ban, and the two Eid nights. (4) A hadith encourages fasting the day and praying the night of mid-Sha'ban with a description of Allah's descent. (5) Another hadith lists five nights whose revival ensures Paradise: Tarwiyah (8th Dhul Hijjah), Arafah (9th), Nahr (10th), Fitr, and mid-Sha'ban. (6) The minimum for 'qiyam' is most of the night, or even one hour. (7) The hashia clarifies linguistic and theological points: the descent of Allah is understood figuratively (tanzih).

Key Terms
النصف من شعبان (al-niṣf min shaʿbān): The 15th night of the Islamic month of Sha'ban, considered a night of great virtue and divine decree.
القيام (al-qiyām): Standing in prayer at night; in this context, engaging in any form of worship for most of the night.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
How many nights are mentioned in the hadith that, if revived, ensure Paradise?
A) Five
B) Three
C) Seven
D) Two

Key Takeaway
Reviving the night of mid-Sha'ban is a confirmed sunna in the Hanafi school, supported by hadith (though not mutawatir) and requiring correct theological understanding of Allah's attributes.

Recommended Prayers: Death, Travel, and Forgiveness
List of three recommended prayers with proof for the third

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the three recommended prayers in the Hanafi school (execution, arrival, and forgiveness), state their ruling level as mustahabb, and explain the specific conditions for each.

Core Idea
Three special two-rak'ah prayers are recommended for life's turning points: execution, travel, and repentance.

The Hanafi fiqh text Maraqi al-Falah concludes its section on recommended acts with three prayers tied to critical moments: facing death, arriving at a destination, and repenting from sin. Although not obligatory, these prayers carry great reward and are rooted in prophetic practice and the teachings of the early Muslims. Understanding them helps a Muslim seize opportunities for devotion and forgiveness in everyday transitions.

Guided Path
1
Identify each prayer and its occasion
From the passage, list the three distinct occasions for which a two-rak'ah prayer is recommended: (1) when a Muslim is about to be executed, (2) when one alights at a place (or intends a journey or returns), and (3) when one has committed a sin and seeks forgiveness.
The first is called ṣalāt al-qatl; the third is ṣalāt al-istighfār.
2
State the ruling level for each
The text uses the verb 'yustahabbu' (it is recommended), indicating the ruling is mustahabb (sunnah ghayr muakkadah). These are not fard, wajib, or sunnah muakkadah, but encouraged acts whose omission is not sinful.
The same ruling applies to all three.
3
Analyze the conditions for the prayer of execution
The prayer of execution is to be performed as the last deed: two rak'ahs followed by seeking forgiveness (istighfar). The condition is that it becomes the final act before death.
This prayer is unique to the Hanafi school.
4
Analyze the conditions for the prayer upon arrival
When one alights at a place, it is recommended to pray two rak'ahs before sitting down. The same applies when starting a journey or returning. The condition is that the prayer precedes any sitting or settling.
Referenced from al-Siyar al-Kabir by Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani.
5
Examine the proof for the prayer of forgiveness
A hadith from Abu Bakr al-Siddiq (through 'Ali) states that anyone who commits a sin, performs wudu properly, prays two rak'ahs, and then seeks forgiveness will be forgiven. The condition is proper wudu followed by prayer and istighfar.
The hadith is a sound (ḥasan) tradition, making the act recommended.

Conclusion: Among the recommended (acts) is the prayer of execution. So if a Muslim is afflicted with it, it is recommended that he pray two rak'ahs, then seek forgiveness for his sins afterwards, so that prayer and seeking forgiveness are his last deeds. And from it is the prayer when one alights at a place; it is recommended that he not sit until he prays two rak'ahs, as in al-Siyar al-Kabir. Similarly, if he intends a journey, or returns. And from it is the prayer of seeking forgiveness for a sin committed by him, because of what is related from 'Ali from Abu Bakr al-Siddiq (may Allah be pleased with them both) that the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'There is no servant who commits a sin, then performs wudu and does it well, then prays two rak'ahs and then seeks forgiveness from Allah, but He will forgive him.' Commentary
This concluding section lists additional recommended prayers (mandubat). The first is 'salat al-qatl' – prayer when one is to be executed (e.g., as a punishment or martyrdom). The recommendation is to pray two rak'ahs and then seek forgiveness, making prayer and istighfar the last actions. The second is a prayer upon reaching a destination: one should not sit down until praying two rak'ahs, derived from the practice of the Prophet in al-Siyar al-Kabir. The same applies when starting a journey or returning. The third is a prayer of repentance after sin: one performs wudu carefully, prays two rak'ahs, and then seeks forgiveness; a hadith promises forgiveness. The hashia adds a grammatical note about the hadith wording.

Key Terms
صلاة القتل (ṣalāt al-qatl): A two-rak'ah prayer performed by one who is about to be executed, seeking forgiveness as a final act.
صلاة الاستغفار (ṣalāt al-istighfār): A two-rak'ah prayer of repentance after committing a sin, followed by seeking forgiveness.
السير الكبير (al-Siyar al-Kabir): A major work by Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani on Islamic international law and travel; source for the ruling on prayer upon alighting.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school recommends two-rak'ah prayers at execution, upon arrival, and after sin—all are mustahabb, not obligatory, and the prayer after sin includes wudu and istighfar.

Ruling on Congregational Revival of Specific Nights
Discusses virtues of nights, five nights of answered dua, and ruling on gathering for prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on gathering in congregation to revive the five nights and explain the basis of the inter-madhhab dispute.

Core Idea
Gathering for 'Ihya' al-Layali' in congregation is makruh because it lacks precedent from the Prophet and Companions.

This passage from Hashiya al-Tahtawi discusses the virtues of specific nights and the ruling on congregational acts of worship on those nights. While individual worship is commendable, the Hanafi school holds that organizing group prayers in mosques on these nights is makruh tanzih. The text presents a dispute among early scholars, with the Hanafi position aligning with the majority of Hijazi scholars and al-Awza'i.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Nights and Their Virtues
The text mentions five nights when supplication is not rejected and other virtues such as expiation of sins. Note the specific nights: Friday, first of Rajab, mid-Sha'ban, and the two Eid nights.
2
State the Hanafi Ruling
The Hanafi ruling is that gathering in congregation to revive any of these nights is makruh tanzih because the Prophet and his Companions did not practice it; it is considered an innovation (bid'ah).
This is the position of the majority of Hijaz scholars including Ata and Ibn Abi Mulaykah.
3
Analyze the Opposing View
Some Tabi'un (Khalid ibn Ma'dan, Luqman ibn Amir) and Ishaq ibn Rahawayh considered such gatherings recommended (mustahabb) based on the general virtues of the nights and the permissibility of collective worship.
This view is attributed to a minority of Syrian scholars.
4
Examine the Dalil
The text cites the hadith 'Whoever prays Isha in congregation...' to encourage regular congregation, but this does not prove a specific sunnah for these nights. The absence of evidence for congregational gatherings on these nights is the key proof for the Hanafi position.
The Hanafi response is that while the nights are virtuous, the specific manner of gathering in congregation was not established.
5
Determine the Mufta Bihi
The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is that such gatherings are makruh, as held by al-Awza'i and the majority of early scholars. Individual worship on these nights is commendable.
This is the operative ruling for fatwa in the Hanafi school.

العيدين، وقال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم : من صلى العشاء في جماعة فكأنما قام نصف الليل ومن صلى الصبح في جماعة فكأنما قام الليل كله رواه مسلم ويكره الاجتماع على إحياء ليلة من هذه الليالي المتقدم ذكرها في المساجد وغيرها لأنه لم يفعله النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم ولا أصحابه فأنكره أكثر العلماء من أهل الحجاز منهم عطاء وابن أبي مليكة وفقهاء أهل المدينة، وأصحاب مالك وغيرهم وقالوا ذلك كله بدعة، ولم ينقل عن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم ولا عن أصحابه إحياء ليلتي العيد جماعة واختلف علماء الشأم في صفة إحياء ليلة النصف من شعبان على قولين أحدهما أنه استحب إحياءها بجماعة في المسجد طائفة من أعيان التابعين كخالد بن معدان، ولقمان بن عامر ووافقهم اسحق بن راهويه والقول الثاني أنه يكره الاجتماع لها في المساجد للصلاة وهذا قول الاوزاعي إمام أهل الشام وفقيههم وعالمهم .
From Sha'ban because it expiates the sins of the year; Friday night expiates the sins of the week; Laylat al-Qadr expiates the sins of a lifetime; and because on it are decreed provisions, lifespans, enrichment, poverty, honor, humiliation, life, death, and the number of pilgrims, and in it Allah Almighty pours blessings like a flood. There are five nights in which supplication is not rejected: Friday night, the first night of Rajab, the middle night of Sha'ban, and the two nights of the two Eids. He said: 'When it is the middle night of Sha'ban, stand in prayer and fast its day, for Allah Almighty descends at sunset to the heaven and says: Is there anyone seeking forgiveness that I may forgive him? Is there anyone seeking provision that I may provide for him? Until dawn breaks.' He said: 'Whoever revives the five nights, Paradise is obligatory for him: the night of Tarwiyah, the night of Arafah, the night of Nahr, the night of Fitr, and the middle night of Sha'ban.' He said: 'Whoever stands the middle night of Sha'ban and the two nights of the two Eids, his heart does not die on the day when hearts die.' The meaning of standing (qiyam) is to occupy most of the night with obedience, and it is said that an hour of it suffices, reading Quran, or hadith, or listening, glorifying, or sending blessings on the Prophet. From Ibn Abbas: performing Isha in congregation and being determined to perform Fajr in congregation, as in reviving the two nights of the Eids... [commentary on verses and words] ... Then he said: 'Whoever prays Isha in congregation is as if he stood half the night, and whoever prays Fajr in congregation is as if he stood the whole night' - narrated by Muslim. It is disliked (makruh) to gather for reviving any of these nights in mosques or elsewhere because the Prophet and his Companions did not do so, and most scholars of the Hijaz including Ata, Ibn Abi Mulaykah, the fuqaha of Madinah, the followers of Malik and others disapproved of it, saying all of that is innovation (bidah). It is not reported from the Prophet or his Companions that they revived the two Eid nights in congregation. The scholars of Sham differed about the nature of reviving the middle night of Sha'ban: one view is that gathering in congregation in the mosque is recommended, held by a group of prominent Tabi'un like Khalid ibn Ma'dan and Luqman ibn Amir, and supported by Ishaq ibn Rahawayh. The second view is that gathering for prayer in mosques is disliked, which is the opinion of al-Awza'i, the imam and scholar of Sham.
Source pages p. 401

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute. The author begins by detailing the virtues of specific nights: the middle of Sha'ban, Friday night, Laylat al-Qadr, and the five nights when dua is not rejected. These virtues are established by hadith. The text then discusses the meaning of 'standing' (qiyam) in prayer and the interpretation of 'ascension' (nuzul) as a divine attribute. It also includes a conclusion (khatimah) listing recommended prayers: two rak'ahs at the time of death, upon alighting at a place, before travel or on return, and for forgiveness of a sin. The central issue is the ruling on gathering in congregations to revive these nights. The text states that such gatherings are disliked (makruh) because the Prophet and his Companions did not do them; it is considered an innovation (bidah) by most scholars. This is the position of the majority of Hijaz scholars. However, a difference of opinion among Syrian scholars is noted: some Tabi'un and Ishaq ibn Rahawayh considered it commendable to gather in congregation, while al-Awza'i maintained it is disliked. The Hanafi position, as implied by the text, aligns with the majority view that congregation for these nights is makruh. The passage emphasizes that while the acts of worship themselves are virtuous, the manner of performing them in congregation on these specific nights is not established from early practice.

Key Terms
إحياء (ihya'): Reviving the night by engaging in prayer, dhikr, or other acts of worship.
بدعة (bid'ah): An innovation in religious matters not practiced by the Prophet or his Companions.
الليالي الخمس (al-layali al-khams): The five nights when supplication is not rejected: Friday, first of Rajab, mid-Sha'ban, and the two Eid nights.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) Mubah (permissible)

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi ruling on congregational 'ihya' of specific nights is makruh tanzih, preserving the practice of the Prophet and preventing innovation.

Voluntary Prayer While Sitting: Permissibility
States the permissibility of voluntary prayer while sitting

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on performing supererogatory prayer while sitting and identify whether an excuse is required.

Core Idea
Voluntary prayer while sitting is permissible even without excuse; standing is more virtuous but not required.

This lesson focuses on the Hanafi ruling regarding voluntary prayer (nafl) performed while sitting. The passage clarifies that it is permissible to pray nafl in a seated position without requiring a health excuse, although standing is more virtuous. Understanding this ruling provides flexibility in worship.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
Determine what act is being ruled upon and what the ruling (hukm) is. The act is performing a supererogatory prayer (nafl) while sitting (qāʿidan). The ruling is 'jāʾiz' (permissible) or 'mubāḥ'.
The term 'nafl' here includes both sunnah muakkadah and other voluntary prayers.
2
Note the scope of 'nafl'
The author intentionally uses 'nafl' to cover both confirmed sunnahs and other supererogatory prayers. This means the ruling applies to all voluntary prayers.
3
Understand the absence of an excuse requirement
The Hanafi school does not require a valid excuse (like illness) for sitting during nafl. This distinguishes nafl from fard, where sitting is only allowed with an excuse.
Cross-madhhab note: Some later scholars required an excuse, but the Hanafi muftā bihi permits it unconditionally.
4
Recognize the virtue of standing
Although sitting is permissible, standing remains more virtuous (afḍal) for nafl when one is able. The ruling permits ease without negating merit.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في صلاة النفل جالساً وفي الصلاة على الدابة وصلاة الماشي (يجوز النفل) إنما عبر به ليشمل السنن المؤكدة وغيرها فتصح إذا صلاها (قاعداً مع قوله: (ومن صلى الصبح في جماعة فكأنما قام الليل كله يحتمل أنه بصلاة الصبح يحصل له ثواب النصف الآخر فالليل كله حصل بمجموع الصلاتين وهو الذي يشير إليه كلام ابن عباس فإنه جعل صلاة العشاء بجماعة والعزم على صلاة الصبح بها يقوم مقام إحياء الليل، ويحتمل أنه أشار به إلى أن صلاة الصبح أفضل من صلاة العشاء لأنه يكون بصلاتها كأنه قام نصف الليل، وبصلاته كأنه قام الليل كله قوله : ( ويكره الإجتماع (الخ) ولا يخرج بنذر الجماعة في الصلوات التي في تلك الليالي، أو غيرها من الرغائب عن الكراهة وإن كان لا يخرج عنها إلا بالجماعة بشرط أن يكون الإمام غير ناذر لها، وإلا لا يصح لعدم صحة اقتداء الناذر بالناذر، ويدخل في ذلك صلاة التسبيح، فإن قيل : يلزم على ما سبق من أن النذر وجد من المقتدي لا من الإمام بناء القوي على الضعيف . قلت بناء القوي على الضعيف إنما يمنع حيث كانت القوة ذاتية، أما إذا لم تكن كما هنا، فلا لأنها عرضت بالنذر ومن هذا قال الحلبي : النذر كالنفل، واعلم أن الصلاة في نفسها مشروعة بصفة ،الإنفراد والإقتداء فيها صحيح مع الكراهة حيث كان على التداعي أفاده السيد والله سبحانه وتعالى أعلم، وأستغفر الله العظيم.
Chapter on voluntary prayer while sitting, and prayer on a riding animal, and walking prayer. (Voluntary prayer is permissible) — he only expressed it this way to include confirmed sunnahs and others, so it is valid if one prays it while sitting. With his saying: (And whoever prays Fajr in congregation, it is as if he spent the whole night in prayer) — it is possible that by praying Fajr he obtains the reward of the other half, so the entire night is obtained by the combination of the two prayers, and this is what Ibn Abbas's words indicate, for he made the performance of Isha in congregation and the determination to pray Fajr in congregation a substitute for the revival of the night. It is also possible that he indicated that Fajr prayer is superior to Isha prayer, because by praying it he becomes like one who stood half the night, and by praying it he becomes like one who stood the whole night. His saying: (And it is disliked to gather) — it does not remove the dislike for congregation by making a vow regarding the prayers in those nights or other desired acts, unless it is that the imam is not the one who made the vow, otherwise it is invalid due to the invalidity of a vow-maker following another vow-maker. This includes the prayer of Tasbih. If it is said: This leads to the previous point that the vow came from the follower, not the imam, by building the strong on the weak. I say: Building the strong on the weak is only prohibited when the strength is intrinsic; if not, as here, it is not prohibited because it is acquired by the vow. From this al-Halabi said: A vow is like a voluntary act. Know that the prayer itself is legislated with the characteristic of individuality, and following (i'tida') is valid with dislike when it is done on a call (tada'i). This is what al-Sayyid transmitted. And Allah Almighty knows best, and I seek forgiveness from Allah the Great.
Source pages p. 402

Commentary
This passage is primarily a ruling statement on voluntary prayer while sitting, though interwoven with a discussion on congregational prayers for special nights and vows. The chapter heading indicates that supererogatory prayer (nafl) is permissible while sitting. The text explains that the term 'nafl' is used broadly to include both confirmed sunnahs and other voluntary prayers. The validity of such prayer is affirmed, even if performed without excuse. The subsequent commentary discusses the hadith on Fajr and Isha congregation virtues, and then returns to the issue of gathering for special nights, linking it to vows (nidhr). It explains that making a vow to pray in congregation does not remove the dislike, unless the imam is not the one who vowed. This discussion is a continuation from the previous section. The core ruling of the chapter is that praying voluntary prayers while sitting is permissible and valid. This is a clear Hanafi position that eases the performance of nafl for those who wish to pray while sitting, without the need for a valid excuse, though standing is still more meritorious.

Key Terms
النفل (al-nafl): Supererogatory prayer, including both sunnah mu'akkadah and nafl prayers.
قاعداً (qa'idan): Sitting, as opposed to standing, during prayer.

Key Takeaway
Voluntary prayer while sitting is permissible in the Hanafi school even without an excuse, though standing is more meritorious.

Voluntary Prayer While Sitting: Ruling and Reward
Commentary on the permissibility and reward of nafl salah while sitting

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on performing nafl prayer while sitting, explain the hadith on half reward, and identify the exception for the excused person.

Core Idea
A healthy person's nafl sitting earns half reward; a sick person's sitting prayer with gestures earns even more than a healthy person's standing prayer.

This passage from al-Tahtawi's commentary clarifies the permissibility of performing voluntary prayers while sitting, even without an excuse, and explains the corresponding reward. It also highlights the exceptional reward for those who pray sitting due to illness, emphasizing that their prayer may surpass that of a healthy person in merit.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its hukm level
Determine what is being ruled upon (nafl prayer while sitting) and its legal classification (permissible but with reduced reward).
The ruling is for a healthy person who is capable of standing.
2
Locate the dalil
Find the primary evidence cited: the hadith 'Whoever prays standing is best...' which equates sitting prayer to half the reward of standing.
This is an ahad hadith, zanni in transmission and meaning.
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
How does the hadith prove the ruling? The explicit comparison indicates permissibility but reduced merit for sitting without excuse.
The hadith does not prohibit sitting; it merely states the reward difference.
4
Note the condition for validity
For a sitting nafl prayer to be valid, one must stand upright before bowing (ruku). Without standing, the bow is neither a standing bow nor a sitting bow, invalidating the prayer.
This condition applies to the capable person; the excused person may gesture.
5
Identify the exception for the sick
Understand that the half-reward rule applies only to the capable. For the excused (sick) person, consensus says their sitting prayer equals the standing prayer in reward, and the commentator argues it is even higher due to effort and intention.
This refinement corrects the misconception that sick people's prayers are inferior.

كتاب الصلاة رضي القدرة على القيام وقد حكي فيه إجماع العلماء، وعلى غير المعتمد يقال : الإسنة الفجر لما قيل بوجوبها وقوة تأكدها، وإلا التراويح على غير الصحيح لأن الأصح جوازها قاعداً من غير عذر فلا يستثنى من جواز النفل جالساً بلا عذر شيء على الصحيح لأنه كان يصلي بعد الوتر قاعداً، وكان يجلس في عامة صلاته بالليل تخفيفاً، وفي رواية عن عائشة الله عنها فلما أراد أن يركع قام فقرأ آيات ثم ركع وسجد وعاد إلى القعود، وقال في معراج الدراية، وهو المستحب في كل تطوع يصليه قاعداً موافقة للسنة، ولو لم يقرأ حين قائماً، وركع وسجد أجزأه، ولو لم يستو قائماً وركع لا تجزيه لأنه لا يكون ركوعاً قائماً، ولا ركوعاً قاعداً كما في التجنيس و لكن له أي للمتنفل جالساً (نصف أجر القائم) لقوله : من صلى قائماً فهو أفضل، ومن صلى قاعداً فله نصف أجر القائم ومن صلى نائماً فله نصف أجر القاعد (إلا) أنهم قالوا هذا في حق القادر أما العاجز (من عذر) فصلاته بالإيماء أفضل من صلاة القائم الراكع الساجد لأنه جهد المقل، والإجماع منعقد على أن صلاة القاعد بعذر مساوية لصلاة القائم في الأجر كذا في الدراية قلت: بل هو أرقى منه لأنه أيضاً جهد المقل ونية المرء خير من عمله
The book of prayer. The ability to stand has been mentioned, and consensus of scholars is reported on it. According to the non-reliable view, it is said concerning the sunnah of Fajr because of the opinion of its obligation and its strong emphasis, but not regarding Tarawih according to the incorrect view, because the correct view is that it is permissible to pray it sitting without excuse, and nothing is excepted from the permissibility of supererogatory prayer sitting without excuse according to the correct view, because he (the Prophet) used to pray sitting after Witr, and he used to sit during most of his night prayer as a lightening. And in a narration from Aisha (may Allah be pleased with her): When he wanted to bow, he would stand, recite some verses, then bow, prostrate, and return to sitting. And he said in Miraj al-Diraya: It is recommended in every supererogatory prayer one prays sitting to follow the Sunnah. Even if he did not recite while standing, and he bowed and prostrated, it suffices. And if he did not stand upright and bowed, it does not suffice because it is neither a standing bow nor a sitting bow, as in al-Tajnis. But for the one praying supererogatory sitting, he has half the reward of the one standing, because of his saying: Whoever prays standing is best, and whoever prays sitting has half the reward of the one standing, and whoever prays lying down has half the reward of the one sitting. Except that they said this applies to the capable one; as for the one incapacitated by an excuse, his prayer with gestures is better than the prayer of the standing, bowing, prostrating person, because it is the effort of the one with no means. And consensus is held that the prayer of the sitting person with an excuse is equal in reward to the prayer of the standing person, as in al-Diraya. I say: Rather it is higher than it, because it too is the effort of the one with no means, and the intention of a person is better than his deeds.
Source pages p. 403

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the ruling of performing voluntary (nafl) prayer while sitting. It opens by addressing the ability to stand in obligatory prayers, noting that there is consensus on the obligation of standing in Fajr sunnah according to some weak views, but the relied-upon position is that one may voluntarily pray sitting without any excuse. The Prophet's practice is cited: he would sometimes sit during night prayer for ease, and in a narration from Aisha, he would stand only for the bowing. The commentator stresses that the reward for a sitting volunteer is half that of a standing volunteer, based on a hadith, but this applies only to the capable person. For the sick person with an excuse, sitting with gestures (ima) is actually better than a healthy person's full prayer, because it represents the utmost effort, and intention raises the reward. The commentator concludes that the sick person's prayer is even higher in rank due to the sincerity of intention.

Key Terms
نفل (nafl): Supererogatory/voluntary prayer beyond the obligatory and sunnah mu'akkadah.
إيماء (ima'): Gesturing with the head or body for bowing and prostration when physically unable.

Key Takeaway
A healthy person's nafl sitting prayer earns half reward; a sick person's sitting prayer earns full or greater reward due to effort and intention.

Posture and Changed Posture in Nafl Prayer: Preferred Sitting and Completing Standing Nafl While Sitting
Explaining the preferred sitting posture and ruling on completing a standing nafl while sitting

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the preferred sitting posture for a volunteer praying nafl sitting and explain the Hanafi dispute on completing a standing nafl while sitting, identifying the mufta bihi.

Core Idea
In nafl, standing is not an integral – you may sit mid-prayer; but the two companions disagree.

This passage addresses two practical aspects of supererogatory (nafl) prayer: how a volunteer should sit when praying sitting (without excuse), and whether a person who starts standing can later sit. The first is about posture, the second about a key intra-Hanafi dispute. You will learn the relied-upon view and why Abu Hanifa’s flexibility prevails.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two rulings
The passage discusses (1) the preferred sitting posture for a volunteer who prays nafl sitting, and (2) the permissibility of a capable person completing a standing nafl while sitting.
Stay aware that these are two separate issues, though both concern nafl.
2
Analyse the first ruling: sitting posture
Determine the preferred posture: like tashahhud (left foot spread, right foot erect) according to al-Mukhtar, but Shaykh al-Islam prefers cross-legged. Note the flexibility: Abu Hanifa allows any sitting, and the sick are unrestricted.
The sick have no restriction – this is a mercy.
3
Examine the second ruling: the dispute
Abu Hanifa permits completing a standing nafl sitting because standing is not a rukn in nafl. The Sahibayn forbid it, likening commencement to a vow. Understand the reasoning of each side.
The key point: Abu Hanifa separates the obligation of prayer from the specific posture.
4
Identify the mufta bihi
The text states that the relied-upon view (al-Mukhtar) for sitting posture is like tashahhud, and for changing posture, the most authentic view (al-ashahh) is that it is permissible without dislike – i.e., Abu Hanifa’s position.
Later Hanafi authorities generally follow Abu Hanifa on this.
5
Note the practical consequence
If a person begins nafl standing and due to fatigue or choice sits, the prayer is valid per Abu Hanifa but invalid per the Sahibayn. The mufta bihi allows it, so no need to repeat.
This relief is especially useful for long nafl prayers.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويقعد) المتنفل جالساً (كالمتشهد) إذا لم يكن به عذر فيفترش رجله اليسرى ويجلس عليها وينصب يمناه (في المختار) وعليه الفتوى ولكن ذكر شيخ الإسلام الأفضل له أن يقعد في موضع القيام محتبياً لأن عامة صلاة رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم في آخر عمره كان محتبياً أي في النفل ولأن المحتبي أكثر توجهاً لأعضائه القبلة لتوجه الساقين كالقيام وعن أبي حنيفة رحمه الله تعالى يقعد كيف شاء لأنه لما جاز له ترك أصل القيام فترك صفة القعود أولى، وأما المريض، فلا تتقيد صفة جلوسه بشيء (وجاز إتمامه) أي إتمام القادر نفله (قاعداً سواء كان في الأولى، أو الثانية (بعد افتتاحه قائماً عند أبي حنيفة رحمه الله لأن القيام ليس ركناً في النفل فجاز تركه، وعندهما لا يجوز لأن الشروع ملزم فأشبه النذر ولأبي حنيفة أن نذره ملزم صلاة مطلقة مع جميع الأركان والشروع لا يلزم إلا صيانة النفل، وهي لا توجب القيام فيتمه جالساً (بلا كراهة على الأصح لأن البقاء أسهل من الابتداء وابتداؤه جالساً لا يكره فالبقاء أولى وكان يفتتح التطوع، ثم يتنقل من القيام إلى القعود ومن القعود إلى القيام، روته عائشة
And the volunteer sitting sits like in the tashahhud, if he has no excuse: he spreads his left foot, sits on it, and erects his right foot. According to al-Mukhtar, and the fatwa is upon it. But Shaykh al-Islam mentioned that it is better for him to sit cross-legged in place of standing, because most of the prayer of the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) in his later life was cross-legged, i.e., in supererogatory prayer, and because the cross-legged posture directs more of his limbs towards the qibla due to the direction of the legs like standing. And from Abu Hanifa (may Allah have mercy on him): he sits however he wishes, because since it is permissible for him to leave the original standing, leaving the description of sitting is even more appropriate. As for the sick person, the manner of his sitting is not restricted to anything. And it is permissible for a capable person to complete his supererogatory prayer sitting, whether in the first or second rak'ah, after initiating it standing according to Abu Hanifa, because standing is not an integral in supererogatory prayer, so it is permissible to leave it. According to the two companions, it is not permissible because commencement makes it binding, so it resembles a vow. And for Abu Hanifa, his vow is binding for an absolute prayer with all integrals, and commencement only binds to safeguard the supererogatory, and that does not necessitate standing, so he completes it sitting. Without dislike according to the most authentic view, because remaining is easier than beginning, and beginning sitting is not disliked, so remaining is even more appropriate. And he (the Prophet) would initiate supererogatory prayer, then transition from standing to sitting and from sitting to standing, as narrated by Aisha.
Source pages p. 404

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on two rulings: (1) the preferred sitting posture for a volunteer praying nafl sitting without an excuse, and (2) the ruling on a capable person who begins nafl standing and then decides to complete it sitting. First, the relied-upon view (al-Mukhtar) is to sit like in tashahhud: left foot spread, sitting on it, right foot erect. However, Shaykh al-Islam prefers sitting cross-legged, citing the Prophet's later practice and the advantage of more limbs facing the qibla. Abu Hanifa gives flexibility: since standing is not obligatory in nafl, any sitting posture suffices. The sick person is unrestricted. Second, a person who starts nafl standing may complete it sitting according to Abu Hanifa, because standing is not an integral (rukn) in nafl; the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) disagree, analogizing it to a vow where commencement imposes an obligation. Abu Hanifa argues that the obligation of commencement only safeguards the prayer's validity, not its specific form. The most authentic view says there is no dislike in this, as remaining in the prayer is easier than beginning anew, and beginning sitting is allowed. The Prophet's own practice of transitioning between standing and sitting is cited in support.

Key Terms
المختار (al-Mukhtar): The relied-upon view among Hanafi scholars, here referring to the preferred sitting posture.
شروع (shuru'): The commencement of prayer, which according to the Sahibayn binds the praying person to complete it as initiated.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, what allows a person who began a supererogatory prayer standing to complete it sitting?
A) Standing is not a pillar in supererogatory prayer
B) The prayer becomes invalid if one continues standing
C) The person’s intention changes
D) It is always recommended to sit

Key Takeaway
In nafl prayer, standing is not an integral – Abu Hanifa's view, which is mufta bihi, allows a person to complete a prayer sitting even if started standing, without dislike.

Ruling on Voluntary Prayer While Riding
Explains permissibility and conditions for nafl prayer on a mount.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on voluntary prayer while riding, identify the conditions for its permissibility, and explain the disagreement with Imam Shafi'i regarding facing the qibla.

Core Idea
The rider need not face qibla for nafl prayer; gestures suffice, per the Prophet's practice.

This lesson explores the flexibility of voluntary prayer (nafl) within the Hanafi school. Unlike obligatory prayers, which require standing, facing qibla, and prostrating on the ground, nafl prayer on a moving mount is permitted with gestures. We will examine the conditions, evidence, and the key difference with Imam Shafi'i.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage states that voluntary prayer while riding outside the city is permissible (jā'iz) and recommended (mandūb). The rider performs gestures (īmā') for bowing and prostration.
The ruling applies to places where a traveler would shorten obligatory prayers.
2
Locate the dalil
The hadith of Jabir from Sahih Ibn Hibban shows the Prophet (peace be upon him) praying voluntary prayers on his mount without facing a fixed direction, making gestures.
The hadith is ahaad (single-narrator) but authentic.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The Prophet's action indicates that facing qibla is not a condition for validity; the prayer is valid regardless of direction. Gesturing for ruku and sujud suffices, with sujud lower than ruku.
The hadith also shows that the opening takbir can be done without stopping the animal.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Imam al-Shafi'i insists that facing the qibla at the start is obligatory for all prayers, including voluntary ones on a mount. Hanafis view it as recommended (mustahabb) but not a condition.
The thamarah (practical consequence): Shafi'i deems such a prayer invalid without initial qibla; Hanafis deem it valid but disliked if done without necessity.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The Hanafi position is mu'tamad (relied upon) due to the specific hadith and the principle that voluntary prayers allow greater ease. The interpreter (Al-Tahtawi) confirms that small actions are excused.
Mufta bihi: permissible outside the city; inside the city, it is valid but makruh tanzihan per the preferred view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(ويتنفل) أي جاز له التنقل بل تدب له راكباً خارج المصر يعني خارج العمران ليشمل خارج القرية والأخبية بمحل إذا دخله مسافر قصر الفرض وسواء كان مسافراً، أو خرج لحاجة في بعض النواحي على الأصح، وقيل إذا خرج قدر ميل وقيل إذا خرج قدر فرسخين جاز له وإلا فلا وعن أبي يوسف جوازها في المصر أيضاً على الدابة (مومياً إلى أي جهة ويفتتح الصلاة حيث توجهت به دابته لمكان الحاجة ولا يشترط عجزه عن إيقافها للتحريمة في ظاهر الرواية لقول جابر: رأيت رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم يصلي النوافل على راحلته في كل وجه يومىء إيماء، ولكنه يخفض السجدتين من الركعتين رواه ابن حبان في صحيحه، وإذا حرك رجله، أو ضرب دابته، فلا بأس به إذا لم يصنع شيئاً كثيراً (وبني : من المنفعة وعند مالك ... وتمامه في الشرح. قوله : (موميا إلى أي جهة الخ) فلو سجد على سرجه، أو على شيء وضع عنده يكون عبثاً لا فائدة فيه فيكره، ولا تفسد لأنه إيماء وزيادة اللهم إلا أن يكون ذلك الشيء نجساً، فتفسد لاتصال النجاسة به كما حققه البرهان الحلبي . قوله : ( ويفتتح الصلاة الخ) إنما زاده لوقوع الخلاف فيه فإن الإمام الشافعي رضي الله عنه يشترط الإستقبال عند الإفتتاح، وفي شرح عمدة الأحكام، وعند أبي حنيفة وأبي ثور: يفتتح أولاً إلى القبلة استحباباً، ثم يصلي كيف شاء، وبه قال أحمد: وهو الأشبه كذا في ابن أمير حاج. قوله : (حيث توجهت به دابته أشار به إلى أنه إذا صلى إلى غير ما توجهت به دابته لا يجوز لعدم الضرورة إلى ذلك كما في السراج، وفي توحيد الضمير في قوله ،مومياً، وقوله به إشارة إلى أنّ الصلاة على الدابة لا تصح بالجماعة فإن فعلوا فصلاة الإمام صحيحة، وصلاة القوم فاسدة، وقيل تجوز إذا كانا على دابة واحدة كما في البحر عن الظهيرية وبه جزم في الدور قوله : ( في ظاهر الرواية) وقال الكاكي: يشترط ذلك وإن تعذر جاز قال في الشرنبلالية وينبغي حمله على صلاة الفرض لأن باب النفل أوسع اهـ. قوله : (وإذا حرك الخ) أشار به إلى أن تسيره لا يضر إذا كان بعمل قليل، وهو المعتمد خلافاً
And he may perform voluntary prayer: it is permissible for him to perform voluntary prayer, rather it is recommended for him, while riding, outside the city, meaning outside the built-up area to include outside the village and tents, in a place where if a traveler enters it he shortens the obligatory prayer. And it is the same whether he is a traveler or went out for some need in some direction according to the most correct view. And it was said: if he goes out the distance of a mile, and it was said: if he goes out the distance of two farsakhs, it is permissible for him, otherwise not. And from Abu Yusuf: its permissibility inside the city as well on an animal, making gestures to any direction. And he begins the prayer wherever his animal turns, due to necessity. And his inability to stop it for the takbir is not a condition in the apparent narration, due to the saying of Jabir: I saw the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, praying voluntary prayers on his mount in every direction, making gestures, and he lowered the two prostrations more than the bowing. Ibn Hibban narrated it in his Sahih. And if he moves his leg or strikes his animal, there is no harm as long as he does not do a lot of action. And he built: from benefit and with Malik ... and its completion is in the commentary. He said: (making gestures to any direction etc.): If he prostrates on his saddle or on something placed beside him, it is useless and disliked, but the prayer is not invalidated because it is gesture and extra, unless that thing is impure, then it is invalidated due to contact with impurity as verified by Burhan al-Halabi. He said: (and he begins the prayer etc.): He only added this because of the difference of opinion about it. For Imam al-Shafi'i, may Allah be pleased with him, requires facing the qibla at the beginning. In Sharh 'Umdat al-Ahkam: According to Abu Hanifa and Abu Thawr, he faces the qibla first as a recommendation, then prays as he wishes. Ahmad said the same, and it is the more appropriate. This is in Ibn Amir Hajj. He said: (wherever his animal turns): He indicated by this that if he prays other than where his animal turns, it is not permissible due to lack of necessity, as in al-Siraj. And in the unification of the pronoun in his saying 'making gestures' and his saying 'by it', there is an indication that prayer on an animal is not valid in congregation. If they do it, the imam's prayer is valid and the people's prayer is invalid. And it was said it is permissible if they are on one animal, as in al-Bahr from al-Zahiriya, and it was affirmed in al-Durr. He said: (in the apparent narration): Al-Kaki said: it is a condition; if it becomes difficult, it is permissible. He said in al-Sharnablaliyya: It should be interpreted as obligatory prayer because the scope of voluntary prayer is wider. End. He said: (and if he moves etc.): He indicated by this that his moving does not harm if it is a small action, and that is the relied-upon view, contrary to...
Source pages p. 405

Commentary
This passage from Hashiya al-Tahtawi addresses the ruling of performing voluntary (nafl) prayers while riding an animal. The author explains that it is not only permissible but recommended (mandūb) to do so outside the built-up area (al-miṣr). The condition is that the rider should be in a place where a traveler would shorten the obligatory prayers. There is disagreement about the minimum distance: some say a mile, others two farsakhs. Abu Yusuf even allows it inside the city. The prayer is performed by gestures (īmā') for bowing and prostration, with prostration lower than bowing. The rider does not need to face the qibla at the start according to the apparent narration (ẓāhir al-riwāya), based on the hadith of Jabir reported by Ibn Hibban. However, it is recommended to face the qibla at the beginning, as argued by Imam Shafi'i, but the Hanafi position is that it is not obligatory. The passage also notes that if the rider prostrates on the saddle or on something placed nearby, it is disliked (makrūh) unless it is impure, which invalidates the prayer. Performing such prayers in congregation is generally invalid, except if two people are on one animal. Any small movements, like moving a leg or tapping the animal, do not harm the prayer as long as they are not excessive. The relied-upon view (mu'tamad) is that small actions are excused.

Key Terms
مومياً (mūmiyan): Making gestures with the head for bowing and prostration instead of actual bending and prostrating on the ground.
نفل (nafl): Voluntary, supererogatory prayer beyond the obligatory ones.
راكباً (rākiban): Riding an animal (e.g., camel, horse, donkey). The ruling applies to modern modes of transport by analogy (qiyās).
ظاهر الرواية (zāhir al-riwāyah): The explicit and well-known narrations from the early Hanafi masters (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad al-Shaybani).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on facing the qibla at the beginning of a voluntary prayer while riding a mount?
A) It is obligatory for the prayer to be valid.
B) It is recommended but not obligatory.
C) It is prohibited to face the qibla.
D) It is only required if the mount is stationary.

Key Takeaway
Voluntary prayer while riding is valid with gestures; facing the qibla is recommended but not required.

Voluntary Prayer While Riding: Ruling and Proof
Explains permissibility, conditions, and rulings for nafl prayer on mount.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on voluntary prayer while riding, identify the proof from the hadith of Jabir, and explain the intra-madhhab and inter-madhhab differences regarding location and facing qibla.

Core Idea
Voluntary prayer on a mount is permissible and recommended, with gestures, without facing qibla at start — a dispensation to maintain devotion.

This passage from Hashiya al-Tahtawi explains the Hanafi position on performing nafl prayers while riding. It is a dispensation to encourage continuous devotion, based on the Prophet's practice. The text covers the location (outside the town), the method (gestures), the qibla issue, and disputes within the Hanafi school and with the Shafi'i school. Understanding this ruling helps appreciate the principle of facilitation in voluntary acts and the role of specific proofs over general commands.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is being ruled upon? Acts: performing voluntary (nafl) prayers while riding a mount. Ruling: permissible (ja'iz) and recommended (mandub).
The ruling is established by the Prophet's frequent practice.
2
Locate the dalil
The primary evidence is the hadith of Jabir: the Prophet prayed voluntary prayers on his mount, gesturing, without facing qibla.
This is a dalil naqli (textual evidence) from the Sunnah.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How does the hadith prove the ruling? The act itself is a permissive dispensation (rukhsa) to avoid hardship of dismounting. The gesture (ima') replaces full bowing and prostration. The fact that the Prophet did not face qibla shows it is not a condition.
Hanafi principle: a voluntary act is more flexible than an obligatory one.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Two disputes: (1) Intra-Hanafi: Abu Hanifa restricts to outside town; Abu Yusuf and Muhammad allow inside town. (2) Inter-madhhab: Shafi'i requires facing qibla at the start even for voluntary prayers.
Practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf): Hanafi can begin without qibla; Shafi'i must face it.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is permissibility outside town; inside town, the view of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad is accepted but with caution. The Shafi'i position is rejected because the specific hadith overrides the general command to face qibla.
The Hanafi school prefers the hadith of Jabir as more specific to voluntary prayers.

رضي الله عنها (ويتنفل) أي جاز له التنقل بل تدب له راكباً خارج المصر) يعني خارج العمران ليشمل خارج القرية والأخبية بمحل إذا دخله مسافر قصر الفرض وسواء كان مسافراً، أو خرج لحاجة في بعض النواحي على الأصح، وقيل إذا خرج قدر ميل وقيل إذا خرج قدر فرسخين جاز له وإلا فلا وعن أبي يوسف جوازها في المصر أيضاً على الدابة (مومياً إلى أي جهة ويفتتح الصلاة حيث توجهت به دابته لمكان الحاجة ولا يشترط عجزه عن إيقافها للتحريمة في ظاهر الرواية لقول جابر: رأيت رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم يصلي النوافل على راحلته في كل وجه يومىء إيماء، ولكنه يخفض السجدتين من الركعتين رواه ابن حبان في صحيحه، وإذا حرك رجله، أو ضرب دابته، فلا بأس به إذا لم يصنع شيئاً كثيراً (وبني : من المنفعة وعند مالك من القيام إلى القعود أي في الركعة الواحدة فقد ذكر في مجمع الروايات أنه كان يفتتح التطوع قائماً، ثم يقعد فإذا بقي من قراءته مقدار عشرين آية أو ثلاثين قام فقرأ، ثم سجد كذا في الشرح قوله : ( أي جاز له التنفل) لأن الصلاة خير موضوع فلو اشترط ما يشق من نحو النزول يلزم الإنقطاع عن الخير قال في المبسوط : لو لم يكن في التنفل على الدابة إلا حفظ اللسان من فضول الكلام لكان كافياً في جوازه. قوله: (بل ندب له) لفعله كثيراً . قوله: (إذا دخله) أي وصل إليه قوله : (على الأصح) هو قول جمهور العلماء، يشترط كونه مسافراً، وذكره في الذخيرة عن محمد، وليس مشهوراً عنه، ولكن عن أبي يوسف جوازها في المصر بلا كراهة وعن محمد كذلك، وفي رواية أجازه مع الكراهة مخافة الغلط بكثرة اللغط واستدلا بما روي عن ابن عمر ! أنه لو ركب الحمار في المدينة يعود سعد بن عبادة، وكان يصلي وهو راكب وأجيب عن الإمام بشذوذ الحديث، وتمامه في الشرح. قوله : (موميا إلى أي جهة الخ) فلو سجد على سرجه، أو على شيء وضع عنده يكون عبثاً لا فائدة فيه فيكره، ولا تفسد لأنه إيماء وزيادة اللهم إلا أن يكون ذلك الشيء نجساً، فتفسد لاتصال النجاسة به كما حققه البرهان الحلبي . قوله : ( ويفتتح الصلاة الخ) إنما زاده لوقوع الخلاف فيه فإن الإمام الشافعي رضي الله عنه يشترط الإستقبال عند الإفتتاح، وفي شرح عمدة الأحكام، وعند أبي حنيفة وأبي ثور: يفتتح أولاً إلى القبلة استحباباً، ثم يصلي كيف شاء، وبه قال أحمد: وهو الأشبه كذا في ابن أمير حاج. قوله : (حيث توجهت به دابته أشار به إلى أنه إذا صلى إلى غير ما توجهت به دابته لا يجوز لعدم الضرورة إلى ذلك كما في السراج، وفي توحيد الضمير في قوله ،مومياً، وقوله به إشارة إلى أنّ الصلاة على الدابة لا تصح بالجماعة فإن فعلوا فصلاة الإمام صحيحة، وصلاة القوم فاسدة، وقيل تجوز إذا كانا على دابة واحدة كما في البحر عن الظهيرية وبه جزم في الدور قوله : ( في ظاهر الرواية) وقال الكاكي: يشترط ذلك وإن تعذر جاز قال في الشرنبلالية وينبغي حمله على صلاة الفرض لأن باب النفل أوسع اهـ. قوله : (وإذا حرك الخ) أشار به إلى أن تسيره لا يضر إذا كان بعمل قليل، وهو المعتمد خلافاً لما في القنية أنه إذا سيرها صاحبها لم يجز الفرض ولا التطوع.
Radiya Allahu anha (and he performs voluntary prayers) i.e., it is permissible for him to perform voluntary prayers, rather it is recommended for him while riding outside the town. Meaning outside the built-up area to include outside the village and tents, in a place where if a traveler enters it, he shortens the obligatory prayer. Whether he is a traveler or went out for a need in some direction, according to the most correct view. And it is said: if he went out the distance of a mile, and it is said: if he went out the distance of two farsakhs, it is permissible; otherwise not. And from Abu Yusuf: its permissibility in the town as well, on the mount. (Making gestures toward any direction, and he begins the prayer wherever his mount directs him due to need. It is not a condition that he be unable to stop it for the opening takbir according to the apparent narration, because of the saying of Jabir: I saw the Messenger of Allah ﷺ praying voluntary prayers on his mount in every direction, gesturing with his head, and he lowered the two prostrations more than the two rak'ahs. Reported by Ibn Hibban in his Sahih. And if he moves his leg or strikes his mount, there is no harm if he does not do a lot of it. (And he builds) from the benefit, and according to Malik from standing to sitting, i.e., in a single rak'ah. For it is mentioned in Majma' al-Riwayat that he used to begin voluntary prayer standing, then sit, and when a measure of twenty or thirty verses remained of his recitation, he would stand and recite, then prostrate. Thus in al-Sharh. His saying (i.e., it is permissible for him to perform voluntary prayers) because prayer is a good thing; if one were to require what is burdensome like dismounting, it would entail abandoning good. Al-Mabsut says: If there were nothing in performing voluntary prayers on a mount except protecting the tongue from useless speech, that would be sufficient for its permissibility. His saying: (rather it is recommended for him) because he did it often. His saying: (when he enters it) i.e., arrives at it. His saying: (according to the most correct) is the saying of the majority of scholars, that it is a condition that he be a traveler. And it is mentioned in al-Dhakhira from Muhammad, but it is not well-known from him. But from Abu Yusuf: its permissibility in the town without dislike, and from Muhammad likewise. And in one narration: he permitted it with dislike, fearing error from much noise. And they argued with what is narrated from Ibn Umar: that he rode a donkey in Madinah visiting Sa'd ibn 'Ubadah, and he was praying while riding. And it was answered that the hadith is irregular, and its completion is in al-Sharh. His saying: (gesturing toward any direction etc.) So if he prostrates on his saddle, or on something placed near him, it is useless with no benefit, so it is disliked, but does not invalidate because it is gesture and an addition. Unless that thing is impure, then it invalidates due to contact with impurity, as verified by Burhan al-Halabi. His saying: (and he begins the prayer etc.) He added this because there is a difference of opinion about it. Imam al-Shafi'i (RA) requires facing the qibla at the beginning. In Sharh 'Umdat al-Ahkam, and according to Abu Hanifah and Abu Thawr: he begins first toward the qibla as a recommendation, then prays as he wishes. Ahmad said likewise, and it is more suitable, thus in Ibn Amir Haj. His saying: (wherever his mount directs him) indicates that if he prays to a direction other than where his mount directs him, it is not permissible due to lack of necessity, as in al-Siraj. And in the union of the pronoun in his saying 'mumiyan' and his saying 'bihi' indicates that prayer on the mount is not valid in congregation. If they do so, the Imam's prayer is valid and the people's prayer is invalid. It is said: it is permissible if they are on one mount, as in al-Bahr from al-Zahiriyya, and it is confirmed in al-Durr. His saying: (in the apparent narration) said al-Kaki: that is a condition, and if it is impossible, it is permissible. He said in al-Sharnublaliyya: it should be carried on the obligatory prayer, because the scope of voluntary prayer is broader. End. His saying: (and if he moves etc.) He indicated that his moving does not harm if it is a small action, and that is the relied-upon view, contrary to what is in al-Qunya: if its owner moves it, neither obligatory nor voluntary prayer is permissible.
Source pages p. 405

Commentary
This passage is from a Hanafi commentary on the rules of voluntary prayer while riding. It begins by stating that it is permissible and even recommended to perform nafl prayers on a mount outside the built-up area, such as during travel. The Hanafi school emphasizes that this is a dispensation to encourage continuous devotion. The text notes that the recommended nature is established by the Prophet's frequent practice. There is a dispute regarding the distance required outside the town: the most correct view is that it applies to a traveler, but some say a mile or two farsakhs. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad allow it even inside the town, either without dislike or with dislike to avoid confusion. The proof is a hadith of Jabir describing the Prophet's practice of gesturing (ima') on his mount. The passage then discusses the ruling on facing the qibla: the Hanafi position is that it is recommended to face the qibla at the start, but not obligatory, contrary to the Shafi'i view. It also covers details like prostrating on the saddle (disliked but not invalidating), and the invalidity of congregational prayer on a mount. Finally, it addresses slight movements such as moving the leg or striking the mount: these are permissible if minimal, and this is the relied-upon view, though some sources (like al-Qunya) consider them invalidating, but that is not the accepted position.

Key Terms
ويتنفل (yata-naffal): He performs voluntary (nafl) prayers; used here for the permissibility and recommendation of such prayers.
إيماء (ima'): Gesturing with the head for bowing and prostration instead of full movements, used while riding.
تحريمة (tahreema): The opening takbir that begins the prayer; here it is discussed whether the rider must stop the mount for it.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on facing the qibla at the beginning of a voluntary prayer while riding?
A) It is obligatory.
B) It is recommended but not obligatory.
C) It is not allowed.
D) It is forbidden.

Key Takeaway
Voluntary prayer while riding is a recommended dispensation with gestures, not requiring facing qibla, based on the hadith of Jabir.

Building Prayer When Dismounting from a Mount: Scope of Iḥrām
Intra-Hanafi dispute on building prayer when dismounting.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on building prayer when a rider dismounts, distinguish it from the reverse case and from the sick person's case, and evaluate Zufar's opposing view.

Core Idea
The rider's iḥrām covers both gesture and full movements; the ground-starter's does not.

The Hanafi school carefully defines the scope of iḥrām (the state of consecration upon entering prayer). This lesson examines a subtle ruling: when a person begins prayer on a mount with gestures, he may dismount and continue with full bowing and prostration, building the later part upon the earlier. However, if he starts on the ground, he cannot later ride and use gestures. This distinction hinges on whether the iḥrām was contracted to include both modes. The passage also contrasts this with the sick person's situation and notes an intra-Hanafi disagreement (Zufar).

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
Scenario 1: Prayer begins on a mount (with gesture) then the rider dismounts and continues with full movements. Scenario 2: Prayer begins on the ground then the person rides and gestures. The ruling differs.
Building (bina') means connecting parts performed differently under one iḥrām.
2
Understand the key term 'taḥrīmah'
Taḥrīmah is the opening takbir that defines the scope of the prayer. Building is only valid if a single taḥrīmah encompasses both parts.
This is the core legal criterion.
3
Analyse the distinction between rider and ground-starter
The rider's iḥrām is contracted with the intention of both gesture (while riding) and full movements (if dismounted), so both are under one taḥrīmah. The ground-starter's iḥrām only includes full movements, so gesture on a mount is outside its scope.
Thus building is allowed only in the first scenario.
4
Contrast with the sick person's case
A sick person who prays with gesture due to inability cannot later build full movements if he recovers, because his iḥrām never included the actual pillars.
The rider's gesture is not a substitute (khalaf); it is a form of the original act, since he could have dismounted.
5
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Zufar holds that building is permissible in both directions, considering the iḥrām flexible. The relied-upon majority view is that building is only allowed when starting on the mount.
This dispute does not affect obligatory prayers, which cannot begin on a mount without excuse.

Source Text

بنزوله) على ما مضى إذا لم يحصل منه عمل كثير كما إذا ثنى رجله فانحدر لأن إحرامه انعقد مجوزاً للركوع والسجود عزيمة بنزوله بعده فكان له الإيماء بهما راكباً، رخصة، وبهذا يفرق بين جواز بنائه، وعدم بناء المريض بالركوع والسجود، وكان مومياً لأن إحرام المريض لم يتناولهما لعدم قدرته عليهما فلذا ( لا ) يجوز له البناء بعد (ركوبه) على ما مضى من صلاته نازلاً في ظاهر الرواية عنهم لأن افتتاحه على الأرض استلزم جميع الشروط وفي الركوب يفوت شرط الاستقبال واتحاد المكان وطهارته وحقيقة الركوع والسجود (و) جاز الإيماء على الدابة ولو كان بالنوافل (الراتبة المؤكدة، وغيرها حتى سنة الفجر وروي عن لما في القنية أنه إذا سيرها صاحبها لم يجز الفرض ولا التطوع. قوله: (لأن إحرامه انعقد مجوزاً للركوع والسجود إيضاحه أن يقال أن بناء بعض الصلاة على بعض عند الاختلاف إنما يجوز إذا تناولتهما تحريمة واحدة وأما إذا لم يكونا كذلك فلا يجوز إذا ظهر هذا فتحريمة الراكب انعقدت مجوزة للإيماء راكباً، وللركوع والسجود بتقدير النزول فكان ما صلي بالإيماء وهو راكب، وما يصلي بعد النزول بركوع وسجود داخلين تحت تحريمة واحدة فجاز بناء أحدهما على الآخر وإحرام النازل انقعد موجباً للركوع والسجود فقط فلم يتناول الإيماء راكباً بناؤه عليه كذا في العناية فإن قيل : ما ذكر فيه بناء القوي على الضعيف، وذلك لا يجوز كما في المريض إذا صح أجيب بأن إحرام المريض لم يتناول الأركان أي الأصلية بدون إيماء لعدم قدرته عليها فلا يجوز بناء ما لم يتناوله إحرامه على ما تناوله، وأجيب أيضاً بأن فلا يصح خلفاً، فلا إيماء الراكب كركوعه وسجوده في القوة، وليس خلفاً عنهما، ولذا جاز ابتداؤه بالإيماء قدرته على النزول إذ الخلف ما لا يصار إليه إلا عند تعذر الأصل، ولا يصبح الجمع بينهما بخلاف المريض فإنّ إيماء خلف لا يجوز له ابتداء مع القدرة أي فلا يصح الجمع بينه، وبين الأصل فلا . يصح له البناء قال في النهاية وعلى هذا الفرق يجب أن لا يبني في المكتوبة فيما إذا افتتحها راكباً ،لعذر ثم نزل لأنه ليس له أن يفتتحها على الدابة عند القدرة فكان الإيماء فيها البناء للزوم الجمع بين الأصل والخلف، ولهذا قيد المسئلة في الهداية يصح بالمتطوع اهـ. قوله (عزيمة) أي أمراً محتماً عليه، وهو مفعول مطلق لمحذوف أي عزم عليه عزيمة، وقوله بنزوله متعلق به :قوله فكان له الإيماء) الأولى أن يقول، وللإيماء بهما عطف على قوله : للركوع . قوله: (رخصة) أي جاء على خلاف الحكم الأصلي تسهيلاً قوله : (وبهذا) الإشارة ترجع إلى التعليل قوله : (فلذا) أي للتعليل بعدم التناول قال في الشرح، وعدم بناء المريض إذا قدر على الركوع والسجود، وكان مومياً لأن إحرام المريض لم يتناولهما لعدم قدرته عليها، فصار كإحرام النازل الذي افتتح الصلاة على الأرض فلا يجوز بناء ما لم يتناوله إحرامه على ما تناوله فلذا لا تجوز الخ. قوله : (في ظاهر الرواية) وقال زفر يجوز له البناء كما أوضحه في الفتح. قوله : (حتى سنة الفجر) بالجر عطفاً على النوافل الراتبة. قوله :
(His descending) as previously mentioned if he does not perform a lot of action, such as when he folds his leg and descends, because his iḥrām was contracted permitting bowing and prostration as a determined obligation after his descending, so he may gesture with them while riding, as a concession. And by this the difference is made between the permissibility of his building and the non-building of the sick person with bowing and prostration while he was gesturing, because the iḥrām of the sick person did not include them due to his inability. Therefore, it is not permissible for him to build after (his riding) upon what preceded of his prayer while descending, according to the apparent narration from them, because his opening on the ground entailed all conditions, and in riding, the condition of facing the qibla, unity of place and its purity, and the reality of bowing and prostration are lost. (And) gesturing on the mount is permissible even for (the emphasized regular voluntary prayers) and others, including the sunnah of Fajr, and it is narrated from ... because in al-Qunya: if its owner moves it, neither obligatory nor voluntary prayer is permissible. His saying: (because his iḥrām was contracted permitting bowing and prostration) its clarification is that building part of a prayer upon another in case of difference is only permissible if a single tḥrīmah encompasses both; otherwise not. When this is clear: the tḥrīmah of the rider is contracted permitting gesturing while riding and for bowing and prostration in the event of descending. So what was prayed with gesture while riding and what is prayed after descending with bowing and prostration are both under one tḥrīmah, so building one upon the other is permissible. The iḥrām of the one who starts on the ground is contracted requiring only bowing and prostration, so it does not include gesturing while riding, so building on it is not permissible. Thus in al-ʿInāyah. If it is said: what is mentioned therein is building the strong upon the weak, and that is not permissible, as with the sick person when he recovers, it is answered: The iḥrām of the sick person did not include the essential pillars without gesture due to his inability, so it is not permissible to build what was not included in his iḥrām upon what was included. It is also answered that it is not valid as a substitute. So the gesture of the rider is like his bowing and prostration in strength, and it is not a substitute for them. Therefore, it is permissible for him to begin with gesture despite his ability to descend, because a substitute is only resorted to when the original is impossible, and combining them is not sound. Unlike the sick person, whose gesture is a substitute, so it is not permissible for him to begin with it while able, i.e., combining it and the original is not sound, so building is not sound for him. He said in al-Nihāyah: Based on this distinction, one should not build in an obligatory prayer if he began it while riding due to an excuse and then descended, because he is not allowed to begin it on the mount when able, so the gesture in it would be building, because of the necessity of combining the original and the substitute. For this reason, the issue was restricted in al-Hidāyah to voluntary prayer. End. His saying (determined obligation) i.e., an imperative matter incumbent upon him, and it is an absolute object of an omitted verb, i.e., he resolved upon it as a determination. His saying (his descending) is attached to it. His saying (so he may gesture) would be better as 'and to gesture with them' as an addition to his saying 'for bowing'. His saying (concession) i.e., it came contrary to the original ruling as a facilitation. His saying (and by this) the reference goes back to the reasoning. His saying (therefore) i.e., due to the reasoning of non-inclusion. He said in al-Sharḥ: And the non-building of the sick person when he becomes able to bow and prostrate while he was gesturing, because the iḥrām of the sick person did not include them due to his inability, so he becomes like the iḥrām of the one descending who started the prayer on the ground, so it is not permissible to build what was not included in his iḥrām upon what was included. Therefore, it is not permissible etc. His saying (in the apparent narration) and Zufar said: it is permissible for him to build, as clarified in al-Fatḥ. His saying (including the sunnah of Fajr) with genitive case, joined to the regular voluntary prayers.
Source pages p. 406

Commentary
This passage delves into a nuanced Hanafi legal issue: Can a person who begins praying on a mount (with gestures) dismount and continue the prayer with full bowing and prostration? And vice versa? The core ruling is that if one starts on the mount, his iḥrām (state of consecration) is contracted in a way that permits both gesture (while riding) and actual bowing/prostration (when dismounted) under the same intention. Therefore, he may build the later part upon the earlier. However, if one starts on the ground, his iḥrām requires all conditions and full movements, so if he later rides, he cannot build because the conditions (qibla direction, purity of place, etc.) are lost. The passage distinguishes this from a sick person who prays with gesture due to inability: his iḥrām does not include the actual movements, so when he recovers, he cannot build. The rider's gesture is not a 'substitute' (khalaf) but rather a form of the original (since he could have dismounted to perform full movements), whereas the sick person's gesture is a true substitute. This distinction explains the different rulings. The text also mentions an intra-Hanafi dispute: Zufar holds that building is permissible even when starting on the ground, but the relied-upon view is otherwise. The rule is restricted to voluntary prayers; for obligatory prayers, building is not allowed because one should not begin on a mount without an excuse.

Key Terms
بناء (bina'): Building or continuing the prayer upon a previous part, used here in the context of joining two parts performed with different postures.
إحرام (iḥrām): The state of consecration upon entering prayer, including the intention and takbir.
تحريمة (taḥrīma): The opening takbir that renders the prayer valid; here, the concept of a single taḥrīma covering multiple parts.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi view, if a person begins a voluntary prayer on the ground and then mounts a ride, can he continue the prayer with gestures?
A) Yes, because gesture is permissible in voluntary prayers.
B) No, because his iḥrām did not include gesture.
C) Yes, but only if he stops the mount.
D) No, because voluntary prayers cannot be performed while riding.

Key Takeaway
Building prayer after changing posture is only valid if a single taḥrīmah encompasses both parts, which occurs when starting on a mount but not when starting on the ground.

Building Prayer When Descending: The Role of Ihram
Ruling with proof on building prayer when descending

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on building prayer when descending from a mount and explain the distinction based on how the prayer began.

Core Idea
Building prayer upon descent depends on whether the ihram encompassed the actual pillars or not.

This passage from Hashiya al-Tahtawi explains a key ruling on building (binā') prayer when a person who began praying on foot later mounts an animal and then descends. The central issue is whether the initial intention (ihram) covers both actual bowing/prostration and gesturing, and whether the two can be combined in a single prayer. We will unpack the Hanafi position, its proof, and how it differs from the case of the sick person.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
Determine whether the prayer began on foot (nāzilan) or on a mount (rākiban). This is the decisive factor.
The passage contrasts two scenarios: starting on foot then riding, vs. starting on a mount then descending.
2
Understand the role of ihram
The ihram (intention) at the start of prayer determines what acts of prayer are permitted. If the ihram is concluded for actual pillars (rukūʿ and sujūd), it cannot later include a mere gesture (īmāʾ) because that would be combining a strong act with a weak substitute.
Ihram is like a contract that specifies the obligations.
3
Analyze the loss of conditions when riding
When riding, conditions like facing the qibla, purity of place, and stability are lost. The gesture is a concession, but the original ihram did not anticipate this concession.
The text lists: shart al-istiqbāl, ittiḥād al-makān, ṭahāratuhu, and ḥaqīqat al-rukūʿ wa al-sujūd.
4
Compare with the sick person
A sick person's ihram never encompassed actual pillars due to inability, so his gesture is a substitute (khalaf). Building is not allowed when he recovers because the gesture is weak and cannot be built upon.
The rider's gesture is strong (ʿazīmah) because he could have descended to perform actual pillars.
5
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Imam Zufar allowed building in both scenarios, but the relied-upon view (Zahir al-Riwayah) is that building is not allowed when starting on foot.
The tarjīḥ is based on the strength of the transmitted evidence.
