(upon his descending) on what has passed if he did not perform much action, like when he bends his leg and descends, because his ihram was concluded as permitting bowing and prostration as an obligation upon his descending, so he could gesture with them while riding as a concession. And by this is distinguished between the permissibility of building and the non-building of the sick with bowing and prostration, and he was gesturing because the sick person's ihram did not encompass them due to his inability upon them. Therefore, (not) permissible for him to build after (his riding) on what has passed of his prayer while descending in the apparent transmission from them, because his opening on the ground necessitated all conditions, and in riding the condition of facing the qibla, unity of place, its purity, and the reality of bowing and prostration are lost. ... (then the commentary continues explaining the difference and the ruling).
Source pages p. 406

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the Hanafi school regarding building one's prayer when descending from a mount. The key ruling: if a person begins prayer on the ground (as a pedestrian) and then mounts an animal, he cannot build the remaining prayer upon descending; rather he must start anew. The reason given is that the initial ihram (intention) concluded with the obligation of actual bowing and prostration, which require specific conditions (facing qibla, purity, stationary place). When riding, these conditions are lost, and only gesturing (ima') is permissible as a concession. In contrast, a sick person who cannot bow and prostrate may gesture from the start; but his ihram never encompassed actual pillars, so he cannot build when able. The commentary elaborates that the difference lies in the strength of the gesture: a healthy rider's gesture is strong and not a substitute (khalaf), so building is allowed when he descends, whereas a sick person's gesture is a weak substitute, precluding building. The relied-upon position (Zahir al-Riwayah) is that building is not allowed when starting on foot; Imam Zufar held a different opinion, allowing it.

Key Terms
إحرام (ihram): The intention (niyyah) to enter prayer, which determines the obligations and concessions.
إيماء (ima'): Gesturing with the head for bowing and prostration when unable to perform them actually.
خلف (khalaf): A substitute that stands in for the original when it is impossible; here contrasted with a strong gesture.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school (Zahir al-Riwayah), if a person begins his obligatory prayer on the ground and then mounts a riding animal without a valid excuse, can he build the remaining prayer after descending?
A) Yes, he can build because his ihram includes the gesture.
B) No, he must restart the prayer.
C) Yes, but only for supererogatory prayers.
D) No, but he can continue by gesturing while riding.

Key Takeaway
Building prayer when descending is only permissible if the initial ihram encompassed the gesture as a concession, which occurs when starting on the mount, not on the ground.

Obligatory Prayer on a Mount: General Ruling and Necessity
Ruling on obligatory prayers on mounts and exceptions for necessity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that obligatory and wajib prayers on a mount are invalid except for necessity, and list the valid necessity scenarios with their proof from the Quran.

Core Idea
Obligatory prayer on a mount is invalid without necessity; the Quran permits it in fear.

This lesson covers the fundamental Hanafi principle that obligatory and wajib prayers cannot be performed on a riding animal unless a genuine necessity exists. The ruling is derived from the Quranic verse permitting prayer while riding in fear. We will explore the scope of necessity and its conditions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general ruling
Note the explicit statement: obligatory and wajib prayers (like witr, vowed prayers, Eid, qada of invalidated nafl, funeral prayer, and prostration of recitation) are not valid on a mount.
This is the default position; validity requires the act to be performed on the ground.
2
Recognize the exception for necessity
The text states 'except for necessity' and provides examples: fear of a thief, predator, rain and mud, etc. Understand that necessity overrides the general prohibition.
Necessity is defined by genuine hardship or danger.
3
Locate the Quranic proof
The author cites Surah al-Nisa' verse 101: 'If you fear, then pray on foot or riding.' This is the primary textual evidence for the exception.
The verse is a direct permission for prayer in a state of fear, which extends to other necessities.
4
Understand the mode of prayer during necessity
When praying on a mount out of necessity, one performs gestures (ima') for ruku and sujud, facing the qibla if possible, and if not, any direction.
The prayer is valid with gestures and does not require repetition after the necessity ends.

Chapter on the obligatory and wajib prayer on a mount. And the litter: The obligatory prayers and wajib prayers like witr and vowed prayers, and the two Eid prayers, and the makeup of what one started as nafl and then invalidated, and the funeral prayer, and the prostration of recitation whose verse was recited on the ground are not valid on a mount except due to necessity, as established in the Quran: 'If you fear, then [pray] on foot or riding.' And the wajib is annexed to it, like fear of a thief for himself, his mount, or his clothes if he dismounts, and his group does not stop for him; and fear of a predator for himself or his mount; and existence of rain and mud in the place... etc.
Source pages p. 407

Commentary
This passage from Hashiyat al-Tahtawi expands on the rulings of prayer on a mount. It begins by stating the general principle that obligatory and wajib prayers (like witr, nadhr, Eid, and qada of invalidated nafl) are not valid on a mount. However, exceptions exist for genuine necessity, such as fear of harm from thieves or predators, or extreme rain and mud that would soil one's clothing. The proof is the Qur'anic verse allowing prayer while riding when in fear. The commentary explains that necessity includes various scenarios and clarifies that the prayer is performed with gestures (ima') while facing the qibla if possible. A key point is the dispute on whether a person is considered 'capable through another's ability' (qadir bi-qudrat al-ghayr). Imam Abu Hanifa holds that if one can dismount with the help of another (e.g., a woman helped by her husband or mahram), then they must dismount and pray on the ground; the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) consider such a person still incapable and allow prayer on the mount. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that of the Sahibayn, as the commentator says 'tarjih qawlihima' (their view is preferred). The passage also discusses the ruling of praying in a litter (mahmil): if it is placed on the ground with supports, it takes the ruling of the ground, and one can perform the obligatory prayer standing with full ruku' and sujud.

Key Terms
دابة (dābba): Any riding animal (horse, camel, donkey, etc.) used for transport.
محمل (maḥmil): A litter or carriage placed on a mount; when placed on the ground with supports, it takes the ruling of the earth.
إيماء (īmā’): Gesturing with the head for ruku' and sujud when unable to perform them fully prayed on a mount or when sick.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, when is it permissible to perform an obligatory prayer on a mount?
A) In all circumstances, as long as one faces the qibla.
B) Only when there is a genuine necessity like fear of a thief, predator, or extreme mud.
C) Only during travel, regardless of danger.
D) It is never permissible for obligatory prayers.

Key Takeaway
Obligatory and wajib prayers on a mount are invalid without a genuine necessity, which is supported by the Quranic verse permitting prayer during fear.

Intra-Hanafi Dispute: Capability Through Others and the Litter Ruling
Intra-Hanafi dispute on capability through others and ruling on the litter.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the difference between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding whether a person who can dismount with help is considered capable, and apply the mufta bihi position. Also, state the ruling of the litter (mahmil) when it is supported on the ground.

Core Idea
Abu Hanifa says one is capable through another's ability; Sahibayn say true incapacity permits prayer on the mount.

This lesson examines an important intra-Hanafi difference on the concept of 'capability through another' (al-qadir bi-qudrat al-ghayr). It also clarifies when a litter (mahmil) on a mount takes the ruling of the ground, allowing a full standing prayer. Understanding this dispute is crucial for issuing correct fatwas in contemporary scenarios involving assisted mobility.

Guided Path
1
Identify the disputed case
The case is a woman who cannot dismount from her mount without the help of her husband or mahram. The question: Is she considered able (qadir) to dismount because she has help, or is she still unable?
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn.
2
State Abu Hanifa's position
Abu Hanifa holds that she is capable through the capability of others (qadir bi-qudrat al-ghayr). Since her mahram can help her dismount, she must do so and pray on the ground.
His view relies on the legal maxim that capability can be transferred.
3
State the Sahibayn's position
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani say she is genuinely incapable because the ability of others does not transfer to her. Therefore, she may pray on the mount with gestures.
The Sahibayn prioritize personal inability over external help.
4
Apply the tarjih (preference)
The commentator (al-Tahtawi) indicates that the Sahibayn's view is preferred (takhrij qawlihima), so the mufta bihi is that she may pray on the mount.
This tarjih is based on later Hanafi authorities like al-Bahr.
5
Understand the litter (mahmil) ruling
The passage then explains that if a litter is placed on a mount and then supported by a board or similar so that its base rests on the ground, it is considered like the ground. Thus, one can pray the obligatory prayer standing in it with full ruku and sujud.
This is an exception to the general rule: the litter becomes stationary like a room.

Source Text

( يعني أنّ الأولى الخ) أي فيجاب عنه بجوابين قوله : (كره في الأظهر) أي تنزيها بدليل التعليل. قوله : (بخلاف القعود فإنه لا كراهة فيه على الأصح قوله: (للضرورة) ولأنه لما سقط اعتبار الأركان الأصلية فلأن يسقط شرط طهارة المكان أولى قوله: (ولا تصح صلاة الماشي) ولا السابح، وهو يسبح : كما في المضمرات سواء كان بعذر أم لا فرضاً كانت الصلاة أم لا . قوله : (لاختلاف) (المكان ولأن كلا من المشي، والسباحة مناف للصلاة، وأداء الأركان مع المنافي لا يصح والله سبحانه وتعالى أعلم، وأستغفر الله العظيم.
فصل في صلاة الفرض، والواجب على الدابة

فهي
مسئلة
يغيب فيه الوجه أو يلطخه ويتلف ما يبسط عليه أما مجرد ندوة فلا يبيح ذلك والذي لا دابة له يصلي قائماً في الطين بالإيماء (وجموح الدابة، وعدم وجدان من يركبه) دابته، ولو كانت غير جموح العجزه) بالاتفاق، ولا تلزمه الإعادة بزوال العذر والمريض الذي يحصل له بالنزول والركوب زيادة مرض أو بطء يجوز له الإيماء بالفرض على الدابة واقفة مستقبل القبلة إن أمكن وإلا ،فلا وكذا الطين المكان وإن وجد العاجز عن الركوب معيناً . القادر بقدرة الغير عاجز عنده خلافاً لهما كالمرأة إذا لم تقدر على النزول إلا زوج ومعادل زوجته أو محرمه إذا لم يقم ولده محله كالمرأة (والصلاة في المحمل) وهو (على الدابة كالصلاة (عليها في الحكم الذي علمته سواء كانت سائرة أو واقفة ولو) أوقفها و (جعل تحت المحمل خشبة) أو نحوها حتى بقي قراره أي المحمل إلى الأرض) بواسطة ما جعل تحته (كان) أي صار المحمل (بمنزلة الأرض فتصح الفريضة فيه قائماً) لا قاعداً بالركوع والسجود.
فيجوز له حينئذ الصلاة عليها قوله : (واقفة مستقبل القبلة لا يخص المريض، بل هو حكم صلاة الفرض، وما ألحق به على الدابة مطلقاً . قوله : (خلافاً لهما ) تقدم ترجيح قولهما . قوله : (كالمرأة) أي فإنها قادرة بقدرة الغير قوله : ( ومعادل زوجته) مبتدأ وخبره قوله كالمرأة، والظاهر أن الزوجة والمحرم ليسا بقيد قوله : (إذا لم يقم ولده محله) أي لأجل تعادل الحمل. قوله : (كالمرأة) أي المعادلة فيجوز له الصلاة على الدابة كذا بحثه صاحب البحر، وأقره عليه من بعده.
قوله : فتصح الفريضة فيه قائماً فإن لم يمكنه القيام ولا النزول صلى قاعداً كما هو كلامهم أفاده بعض الأفاضل بحثاً، وقال السيد بعد عبارة المصنف : هذه، وهذا وإن أطلقه المصنف يحمل على ما إذا أمكنه القيام والله سبحانه وتعالى أعلم وأستغفر الله العظيم.
Chapter on the obligatory and wajib prayer on a mount. And the litter: The obligatory prayers and wajib prayers like witr and vowed prayers, and the two Eid prayers, and the makeup of what one started as nafl and then invalidated, and the funeral prayer, and the prostration of recitation whose verse was recited on the ground are not valid on a mount except due to necessity, as established in the Quran: 'If you fear, then [pray] on foot or riding.' And the wajib is annexed to it, like fear of a thief for himself, his mount, or his clothes if he dismounts, and his group does not stop for him; and fear of a predator for himself or his mount; and existence of rain and mud in the place... etc.
Source pages p. 407

Commentary
This passage from Hashiyat al-Tahtawi expands on the rulings of prayer on a mount. It begins by stating the general principle that obligatory and wajib prayers (like witr, nadhr, Eid, and qada of invalidated nafl) are not valid on a mount. However, exceptions exist for genuine necessity, such as fear of harm from thieves or predators, or extreme rain and mud that would soil one's clothing. The proof is the Qur'anic verse allowing prayer while riding when in fear. The commentary explains that necessity includes various scenarios and clarifies that the prayer is performed with gestures (ima') while facing the qibla if possible. A key point is the dispute on whether a person is considered 'capable through another's ability' (qadir bi-qudrat al-ghayr). Imam Abu Hanifa holds that if one can dismount with the help of another (e.g., a woman helped by her husband or mahram), then they must dismount and pray on the ground; the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) consider such a person still incapable and allow prayer on the mount. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that of the Sahibayn, as the commentator says 'tarjih qawlihima' (their view is preferred). The passage also discusses the ruling of praying in a litter (mahmil): if it is placed on the ground with supports, it takes the ruling of the ground, and one can perform the obligatory prayer standing with full ruku' and sujud.

Key Terms
قادر بقدرة الغير (qādir bi-qudrat al-ghayr): Capable through another's capability; a legal status where one is deemed able because assistance is available.
محمل (maḥmil): A litter or carriage placed on a mount; when supported on the ground, it becomes like earth.
تخريج قولهما (takhrij qawlihimā): Preferring the view of the two (Sahibayn); a tarjih mechanism giving weight to their opinion.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi position in this lesson, what is the ruling for a woman who cannot dismount without her husband's help?
A) She must dismount with his help and pray on the ground.
B) She may pray on her mount with gestures.
C) She must wait until she can dismount and then make up the prayer.
D) She must pray in the litter only if it is on the ground.

Key Takeaway
The relied-upon Hanafi position is that a person who cannot dismount independently may pray on the mount with gestures, and a litter supported on the ground is treated like the earth for obligatory prayers.

Prayer in a Moving Ship: Abu Hanifa's Ruling
Ruling with proof: validity of prayer in a moving ship.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state Imam Abu Hanifa's ruling on obligatory prayer in a moving ship and distinguish it from the position of the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
In a moving ship, sit and pray with full ruku' and sujud—standing is not required.

This passage addresses a classic Hanafi dispute: how to perform obligatory prayers on a moving ship. Imam Abu Hanifa holds that sitting is sufficient with full ruku' and sujud, even if one could exit and pray on land. His two foremost students, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, disagreed. Let's examine the reasoning behind Abu Hanifa's view and understand the conditions for valid prayer aboard a vessel.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage deals with obligatory and wajib prayers performed in a moving ship. According to Imam Abu Hanifa, the prayer is valid (sahih) when performed while sitting.
The ruling applies to both farḍ and wājib prayers; nafl is included by priority (awlā).
2
Locate the key condition
The prayer is performed sitting, but with full ruku' and sujud (not gestures). The condition of standing is dropped due to the ship's movement.
The text explicitly states 'bil rukū‘ wa al-sujūd' – not imā’.
3
Understand the basis of the rule
The ship is compared to a mount (dābba) for dropping standing, and to land (arḍ) for requiring ruku' and sujud and facing the qibla. The ship's stability (qarār) ensures full prostration is possible.
This is a qiyas (analogical reasoning) combining two analogies.
4
Note the intra-madhhab disagreement
The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) disagree; they likely require standing or deem the prayer invalid if one can exit. Abu Hanifa's view is presented as the sahīh (sound) position.
The text says 'khilāfan lahumā' – contrary to them both. The dispute is legitimate ikhtilāf.

Source Text

Chapter on prayer in the ship: The obligatory and wajib prayer in it, while it is moving, while he is sitting without excuse and he is able to exit from it, is valid according to the Great Imam Abu Hanifa, may Allah have mercy on him, but with ruku' and sujud, not... So it is permissible for him then to pray on it. He said: 'Standing facing the qibla is not specific to the sick, but rather it is the ruling of obligatory prayer and what is annexed to it on the mount absolutely.' He said: 'Contrary to them both, the preference of their view has preceded.' He said: 'Like the woman' meaning she is capable through the capability of another... etc.
Source pages p. 408

Commentary
This passage begins a new chapter on prayer in a ship. The commentator first relates the ship to the mount (dābba) and to the earth: the ship is like a mount on sea, so standing is waived; but like the earth, one sits on it with stability (qarār), so ruku', sujud, and facing the qibla are required. The key ruling states that obligatory and wajib prayers in a moving ship are valid according to Imam Abu Hanifa, performed while sitting, with full ruku' and sujud (not just gestures), even if the person is able to exit the ship but chooses to pray inside. The condition is that standing is not required; the prayer is valid sitting. The commentary then returns to a previous discussion about the woman or mahram (possibly from the animal section), indicating that the text is somewhat jumbled. The commentator notes that the preferred view is that of the Sahibayn on the earlier issue. The ship ruling is clear: Abu Hanifa validates the prayer with ruku' and sujud in a moving ship while sitting, provided the person is capable of exiting but does not do so (or is unable to stand). The reasoning is qiyas on the mount (where standing is dropped) but distinction due to the ship's stability. The text ends abruptly, referring back to the mahmil or ground ruling.

Key Terms
سفينة (safīnah): A ship; considered a hybrid between land (for stability) and mount (for movement on water).
جارية (jāriyah): Moving or sailing (of the ship).

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) It is invalid unless the ship is stationary.

Key Takeaway
In a moving ship, obligatory prayers are valid when performed sitting with full ruku' and sujud, according to Imam Abu Hanifa.

Prayer on a Mount: Conditions and the Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Incapacity
Rulings for prayer on an animal and in a litter with conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for valid prayer on a mount and explain the intra-Hanafi disagreement regarding whether a person who can be assisted to mount is considered incapable.

Core Idea
Prayer on a mount is a concession for genuine incapacity; the disagreement lies in whether assistance from another removes that incapacity.

This passage from Hashiya al-Tahtawi clarifies the rulings for performing salah on a riding animal or in a litter. It specifies when gestures (ima') are permissible and highlights a critical disagreement within the Hanafi school: does a person who can be assisted to mount count as incapable? Understanding this distinction is essential for applying the ruling correctly.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the excuse
The ruling concerns obligatory prayer when one cannot stand on the ground due to mud, a refractory mount, or illness. The core permission is based on genuine inability.
Mere dampness (nadwa) does not justify the concession.
2
Note the condition for gestures (ima')
Gestures replace bowing and prostration only if the face would be smeared or the ground spoiled. The text explicitly states that mere dampness is insufficient.
This is a refinement of the general principle.
3
Compare the two scenarios of inability
First: a refractory mount or no rider available – agreed upon concession. Second: a person who cannot mount alone but has assistance – this is the point of ikhtilaf.
The second scenario is the core of the intra-Hanafi dispute.
4
Analyze the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Imam Abu Hanifa considers the assisted person as incapable (like a woman needing her husband), so prayer on the mount is valid. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) disagree, holding that such a person must pray on the ground.
The text does not give tarjih here, but later sources may prefer one view.
5
Apply to the litter (mahmil)
Prayer in a litter follows the same rules as on a mount. However, if the litter is grounded (e.g., by placing wood under it), it is treated as earth, and obligatory prayer must be performed standing with full actions.
This clarifies the physical attachment to the mount.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فهي مسئلة يغيب فيه الوجه أو يلطخه ويتلف ما يبسط عليه أما مجرد ندوة فلا يبيح ذلك والذي لا دابة له يصلي قائماً في الطين بالإيماء (وجموح الدابة، وعدم وجدان من يركبه) دابته، ولو كانت غير جموح العجزه) بالاتفاق، ولا تلزمه الإعادة بزوال العذر والمريض الذي يحصل له بالنزول والركوب زيادة مرض أو بطء يجوز له الإيماء بالفرض على الدابة واقفة مستقبل القبلة إن أمكن وإلا فلا وكذا الطين المكان وإن وجد العاجز عن الركوب معيناً . القادر بقدرة الغير عاجز عنده خلافاً لهما كالمرأة إذا لم تقدر على النزول إلا زوج ومعادل زوجته أو محرمه إذا لم يقم ولده محله كالمرأة (والصلاة في المحمل) وهو (على الدابة كالصلاة (عليها في الحكم الذي علمته سواء كانت سائرة أو واقفة ولو) أوقفها و (جعل تحت المحمل خشبة) أو نحوها حتى بقي قراره أي المحمل إلى الأرض) بواسطة ما جعل تحته (كان) أي صار المحمل (بمنزلة الأرض فتصح الفريضة فيه قائماً) لا قاعداً بالركوع والسجود. أو بمحرم، والواجب فيها وهي جارية) حالة كونه قاعداً) بلا عذر به وهو يقدر على الخروج منها (صحيحة عند الإمام الأعظم (أبي حنيفة رحمه الله تعالى لكن (بالركوع والسجود) لا بالإيماء لأن الغالب في القيام دوران الرأس، والغالب كالمتحقق لكن القيام فيها والخروج أفضل إن أمكنه لأنه أبعد عن شبهة الخلاف وأسكن لقلبه
This is an issue: if the face is covered or smeared, or what is laid out is spoiled, but mere dampness does not permit that. One who has no mount performs standing prayer in mud with gestures. (And the mount being refractory, and not finding someone to ride it) his mount, even if it is not refractory but he is unable, by agreement, and he is not required to repeat when the excuse ceases. The sick person who gets increased illness or slowness from dismounting and mounting: he may perform obligatory prayer with gestures on the mount while facing the qibla if possible, otherwise not. Likewise for a muddy place. And the person unable to ride but finds someone to assist: the one capable by another's capability is considered incapable in his (Abu Hanifa's) view, contrary to the two companions, like a woman who cannot dismount except with her husband, and the equivalent of his wife or her mahram, if his son does not take his place, like a woman. (And prayer in a litter) which is (on the mount) is like prayer (on it) in the ruling you have learned, whether it is moving or stationary, even if he stops it and (places under the litter a piece of wood) or the like so that the base of the litter rests on the ground by means of what he placed under it, (the litter becomes like the ground, so obligatory prayer in it is valid standing) not sitting, with bowing and prostrations. Or with a mahram, and the obligatory prayer in it while it is moving, while he is sitting without excuse and he is able to exit from it, is valid according to Imam al-A'zam Abu Hanifa, may Allah have mercy on him, but with bowing and prostration, not with gestures because the head usually turns when standing, and the usual is like the actual. But standing in it and exiting is better if possible, because it is farther from the shadow of disagreement and more calming for his heart.
Source pages p. 408

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement on prayer when one cannot stand on the ground due to mud or lack of a mount, and on prayer on a mount (dabba) or in a litter (mahmil). The author first clarifies that mere dampness (nadwa) does not permit prayer in mud without standing; it requires the face to be covered or the ground spoiled. One who has no mount prays standing in mud using gestures (ima'). For a refractory mount or inability to find a rider, the ruling is agreed upon: one may pray on the mount. If the excuse later ceases, no repetition is required. A sick person who fears harm from mounting/dismounting may gesture for obligatory prayers on a mount facing qibla if possible. The text then addresses a person who is physically unable to ride but has someone to help him mount: according to Imam Abu Hanifa, such a person is considered incapable (like a woman who cannot dismount without her husband or mahram), but Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (Sahibayn) disagree. Finally, praying in a litter (mahmil) on a mount follows the same rules as praying on the mount. If the litter is supported by wood so that its base rests on the ground, it is like praying on the earth, so obligatory prayer is valid standing with bowing and prostration.

Key Terms
الدابة (al-dābba): Any riding animal used for travel
المحمل (al-maḥmil): A litter or howdah placed on a mount for carrying passengers
الإيماء (al-īmā’): Gestural indication replacing bowing and prostration for those unable to perform them

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, when is a person permitted to use gestures (ima') for obligatory prayer on a mount?
A) Whenever the ground is damp
B) Only when the face would be smeared or the ground spoiled, and dismounting would cause harm or is impossible
C) Anytime the mount is moving
D) Only for supererogatory prayers

Key Takeaway
Prayer on a mount is a conditional concession requiring genuine incapacity, and the Hanafi school has a legitimate internal disagreement on whether assistance from another removes that incapacity.

Prayer in a Ship: Dispute of Imam Abu Hanifa and the Companions
Intra-Hanafi dispute on prayer in a moving ship

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi intra-madhab difference between Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding sitting prayer in a moving ship, identify the evidence for each, and state the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
Sitting in a moving ship without excuse: Abu Hanifa allows it, Sahibayn require standing – the mufta bihi is to stand unless excused.

This passage from Hashiya al-Tahtawi presents an intra-Hanafi dispute on the validity of sitting prayer in a moving ship when one is able to stand and exit. Imam Abu Hanifa holds it valid with bowing and prostration, while his two leading students Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani require standing unless there is a genuine excuse. The text weighs the evidence and declares the Sahibayn's view as the apparent (adhhār) position, but notes the strength of the Imam's proof.

Guided Path
1
State the dispute
What are the two positions? Identify the ruling of Imam Abu Hanifa and that of the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad).
The dispute is about sitting prayer without excuse in a moving ship.
2
Identify the evidence for each
What dalil does each side cite? The Sahibayn rely on the hadith of Ibn 'Umar and Ja'far; Imam relies on the practice of Companions Anas and Junada.
Both sides use ahadith and practice.
3
Analyse the Imam's proof
Why does the commentator say the Imam's proof is stronger? Because it is supported by two Companions and two Successors, and the hadith of Ibn 'Umar is interpreted as recommendation (nadb) rather than obligation.
The text says 'دليل الإمام أقوى' – the Imam's proof is stronger.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
What is the practical difference? According to Imam, sitting is valid; according to Sahibayn, it is invalid unless there is an excuse.
The thamarah is whether the prayer must be repeated if sat without excuse.
5
Identify the mufta bihi
Which view is relied upon for fatwa? The Sahibayn's view is declared 'al-adhhar' (the apparent) and thus the operative position.
Despite the Imam's stronger proof, the school adopts the Sahibayn's view for practice.

فصل في الصلاة في السفينة صلاة الفرض والواجب فيها وهي جارية) حالة كونه قاعداً) بلا عذر به وهو يقدر على الخروج منها (صحيحة عند الإمام الأعظم (أبي حنيفة رحمه الله تعالى لكن (بالركوع والسجود) لا بالإيماء لأن الغالب في القيام دوران الرأس، والغالب كالمتحقق لكن القيام فيها والخروج أفضل إن أمكنه لأنه أبعد عن شبهة الخلاف وأسكن لقلبه (وقالا) أي أبو يوسف ومحمد رحمهما الله تعالى (لا تصح) جالساً (إلا) من عذر وهو الأظهر) لحديث ابن عمر النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم سئل عن الصلاة في السفينة فقال : صل فيها قائماً إلا أن تخاف الغرق، وقال: مثله الجعفر ولأن القيام ركن فلا يترك إلا بعذر محقق لا موهوم ودليل الإمام أقوى فيتبع لأن ابن سيرين قال صلينا مع أنس في السفينة قعوداً، ولو شئنا لخرجنا إلى الجد وقال مجاهد : صلينا مع جنادة رضي الله عنه في السفينة قعوداً، ولو شئنا لقمنا، وقال الزاهدي، وحديث ابن ع ور جعفر محمول على الندب فظهر قوة دليله لموافقة تابعيين ابن سيرين ومجاهد وصحابيين أنس وجنادة فيتبع قول الإمام رحمه الله تعالى: (والعذر كدوران الرأس وعدم القدرة على الخروج ولا تجوز أي لا تصح الصلاة فيها بالإيماء) لمن يقدر على الركوع والسجود (اتفاقاً) لفقد المبيح حقيقة، وحكماً والمربوطة في لجة البحر) بالمراسي والحبال (و) مع ذلك (تحركها الريح) تحريكًا شديدًا) هي (كالسائرة) في الحكم الذي قد علمته والخلاف فيه ( وإلا) أي إن لم تحركها شديداً (فكالواقفة) بالشط على الأصح و) الواقفة ذكرها مع حكمها بقوله إن كانت مربوطة بالشط لا تجوز صلاته فيها (قاعداً . قدرته على القيام لانتفاء المقتضى للصحة (بالإجماع) على الصحيح وهو احتراز عن قول بعضهم أنها أيضاً على الخلاف فإن صلى) في المربوطة بالشط (قائماً وكان شيء من السفينة على قرار الأرض صحت الصلاة بمنزلة الصلاة على السرير (وإلا) أي وإن لم يستقر منها شيء على الأرض فلا تصح الصلاة فيها ( على المختار) كما في المحيط والبدائع لأنها حينئذ كالدابة وظاهر الهداية والنهاية جواز الصلاة في المربوطة بالشط قائماً مطلقاً أي سواء استقرت أولا (إلا) إذا لم يمكنه الخروج بلا ضرر فيصلي فيها للخروج
Chapter on prayer in a ship. Obligatory and required prayer in it while it is moving, while he is sitting without excuse and he is able to exit from it, is valid according to Imam al-A'zam Abu Hanifa, may Allah have mercy on him, but with bowing and prostration, not with gestures because the head usually turns when standing, and the usual is like the actual. But standing in it and exiting is better if possible, because it is farther from the shadow of disagreement and more calming for his heart. (And the two said) i.e. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, may Allah have mercy on them, (it is not valid) while sitting (except with an excuse, and that is the apparent view) due to the hadith of Ibn 'Umar: The Prophet, peace be upon him, was asked about prayer in a ship, and he said: 'Pray in it standing unless you fear drowning.' And it was said similar by Ja'far. And because standing is a pillar, so it is not abandoned except for a verified excuse, not a delusion. And the proof of the Imam is stronger and is followed because Ibn Sirin said: We prayed with Anas in the ship sitting, and if we wished we could have gone out to the shore. And Mujahid said: We prayed with Junada, may Allah be pleased with him, in the ship sitting, and if we wished we could have stood. And al-Zahidi said: The hadith of Ibn 'Umar and Ja'far is interpreted as recommendation. So the strength of his proof is clear due to the agreement of the two successors Ibn Sirin and Mujahid and the two Companions Anas and Junada, so the saying of the Imam is followed, may Allah have mercy on him. (And the excuse is like dizziness and inability to exit. And prayer in it with gestures is not valid) for one who is able to bow and prostrate (by consensus) due to the absence of the permitter actually and legally. (And the ship tied in the deep sea) with anchors and ropes (and despite that the wind moves it strongly) it is (like the moving ship) in the ruling that you have learned, and the difference of opinion applies. (Otherwise) i.e. if it is not moved strongly (then it is like the stationary ship) at the shore on the correct view. (And) the stationary ship, its ruling is mentioned: if it is tied at the shore, his prayer in it while sitting is not valid due to his ability to stand, because the condition for validity is absent, by consensus according to the correct view, which is a reservation against the saying of some that it also is subject to difference. If he prays in the ship tied at the shore while standing, and part of the ship rests on the ground, the prayer is valid like prayer on a bed. Otherwise, i.e. if nothing of it rests on the ground, the prayer in it is not valid according to the chosen view, as in al-Muhit and al-Bada'i', because then it is like a mount. And the apparent meaning of al-Hidaya and al-Nihaya is the permissibility of prayer in a ship tied at the shore while standing absolutely, i.e. whether it rests or not. Except when he cannot exit without harm, then he prays in it for exit.
Source pages p. 408

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding prayer in a moving ship. The ruling: obligatory prayer in a moving ship while sitting without excuse is valid according to Imam Abu Hanifa, but with bowing and prostration (not gestures). He argues that the usual dizziness from standing is like certainty. The two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold it invalid unless there is an excuse (like fear of drowning or dizziness). They rely on the hadith of Ibn 'Umar and the practice of Ja'far ibn Abi Talib, and the principle that a pillar (standing) cannot be abandoned for a delusory reason. The commentator then weighs the evidence: the Imam's proof is stronger because it is supported by the practice of Companions (Anas, Junada) and Successors (Ibn Sirin, Mujahid). The relied-upon view (al-adhhar) is that of the two companions, but the text notes that the Imam's evidence is strong. The passage also clarifies that prayer with gestures is unanimously invalid if one can bow and prostrate. For a ship tied in deep sea that is strongly moved by wind, it has the same ruling as a moving ship. If tied at the shore and not strongly moved, it is like stationary land, so sitting prayer is invalid without excuse. If part of the ship rests on the ground, standing prayer is valid; otherwise, according to the chosen view, it is like a mount and prayer while standing is valid only if unable to exit without harm.

Key Terms
السفينة (al-safīna): A ship or boat used for water travel
القيام (al-qiyām): Standing posture in prayer, a pillar (rukn) for obligatory prayers for those able
الإيماء (al-īmā’): Gestural indication replacing bowing and prostration

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon view (al-adhhar) in this passage, what is required for valid prayer in a moving ship?
A) One must pray sitting with gestures
B) One must pray standing unless there is an excuse like dizziness
C) One may pray sitting with bowing and prostration
D) One must exit the ship before praying

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, the relied-upon view (mufta bihi) requires standing in a moving ship unless there is a genuine excuse, even though Imam Abu Hanifa allowed sitting as valid.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
12 min
Ruling on Prayer in a Ship: Standing vs Sitting
Resolving the Hanafi dispute on prayer posture on ships

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions on prayer posture on a ship, explain the evidence for Imam Abu Hanifa's view, and apply the ruling to different ship scenarios.

Core Idea
Prayer on a ship: Standing is best, but Imam Abu Hanifa allows sitting even without excuse; Sahibayn need a genuine excuse.

This passage from Hashiyat al-Tahtawi addresses a key internal Hanafi dispute: can one pray sitting on a ship without a genuine excuse? Imam Abu Hanifa permits it, while the two disciples (Sahibayn) require an excuse. The author favors the Imam's view, citing the practice of Companions and Successors. Understanding this dispute requires analysing the evidence and scenarios such as anchored vs moving ships.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal issue
Determine the core question: is sitting in prayer on a ship valid without an excuse? Note that standing is a pillar (rukn) of prayer.
The dispute revolves around necessity and the interpretation of hadith.
2
State both Hanafi positions
State the view of Imam Abu Hanifa (valid without excuse) and the view of the Sahibayn (invalid without excuse). The author calls the Sahibayn's view 'al-azhar' but then supports the Imam.
The 'al-azhar' here is the Sahibayn's view, but the author later favours the Imam.
3
Examine the evidence for each position
For the Sahibayn: hadith of Ibn 'Umar commanding standing unless fear of drowning; analogy that standing is a pillar. For Imam: practice of Companions and Successors praying sitting while able to stand.
The evidence is dalil naqli (textual).
4
Analyse the Hanafi response and tarjih
The author interprets the command as recommendation (nadb) to harmonise with the Companions' practice. The Imam's proof is favoured because of multiple reliable reports.
Tarjih is based on number and reliability of narrations.
5
Apply to different ship scenarios
Examine the rules for a ship tied to the shore but rocking, and for a stationary ship. Understand when standing is valid or when the ship is treated like an animal.
The state of the ship affects the ruling: moving vs stationary, stability on ground.

By nodding because most of the time when standing, the head turns, and what is common is like what is certain, but standing in it and exiting are better if possible because it is further from the semblance of disagreement and more calming to his heart. (And they both said) i.e. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, may Allah have mercy on them, (it is not valid) sitting (except) with an excuse, and this is the more apparent view, due to the hadith of Ibn 'Umar: The Prophet ﷺ was asked about prayer on a ship, so he said: Pray in it standing unless you fear drowning. And the proof of the Imam is stronger, so it is followed, because Ibn Sirin said: We prayed with Anas on a ship sitting, and if we wished we would have come out to the shore. And Mujahid said: We prayed with Junada, may Allah be pleased with him, on a ship sitting, and if we wished we would have stood. And al-Zahidi said: The hadith of Ibn 'Umar and Ja'far are taken as recommendation, so the strength of his proof became apparent due to the agreement of the two Successors Ibn Sirin and Mujahid and the two Companions Anas and Junada, so the statement of the Imam, may Allah be exalted, is followed. (And the ship tied in the deep sea) with anchors and ropes (and) despite that (the wind moves it) severely (it is like the moving ship) in the ruling already known and the disagreement about it (and if not) i.e. if it does not move it severely (then it is like the stationary ship) by the shore according to the most correct view. (If he prays) in the ship tied to the shore (standing and part of the ship is on the ground, the prayer is valid, like prayer on a bed. (And if not) i.e. if none of it is stable on the ground, then the prayer in it is not valid (according to the chosen view) as in al-Muhit and al-Bada'i' because then it is like an animal. After his statement: (And exiting is better) i.e. than praying standing in it, meaning if he can do so without harm to himself or his property. His statement: (Because it is further) is on the way of lath and nashr (intertwined and ordered). His statement: (And he said similarly for Ja'far) i.e. Ibn Abi Talib when he sent him to Abyssinia. His statement: (We would have come out to the shore – الجِدّ) with a kasra on the jim and shadda on the dal, meaning the shore. This is evidence for the permissibility of praying in it while being able to exit from it, and what follows is evidence for the permissibility of praying sitting while being able to pray standing. His statement: (Taken as recommendation) i.e. the command in it, which is 'Pray in it standing', is taken as recommendation to harmonize the evidences. His statement: (The permissibility truly is like the sick person, and effectively is like an animal). His statement: (As in al-Muhit and al-Bada'i') etc. Know that the apparent meaning of al-Hidaya, al-Nihaya, and al-Ikhtiyar is the permissibility of praying standing in the ship tied to the shore. When it is moving, (the worshipper faces the qibla in it) because he is able to fulfill the obligation of facing the qibla (at the start of the prayer and whenever the ship turns away from it) i.e. the qibla, (the worshipper turns with its turning towards it) i.e. the qibla (during the prayer). And if he is incapable, he refrains from prayer (until) he is able (to complete it facing the qibla). And if he abandons facing the qibla, it does not suffice him according to all of their statements.
Source pages p. 409

Commentary
This passage from Hashiyat al-Tahtawi resolves a key intra-Hanafi dispute regarding prayer in a ship. The author first presents the ruling: standing in prayer on a ship is the norm, and nodding (imā') is only for genuine excuses like dizziness or inability to exit. The dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) is about whether sitting without an excuse is permissible. The Sahibayn hold that it is not valid except with an excuse, basing their view on the hadith of Ibn 'Umar and Ja'far. Imam Abu Hanifa, however, permits sitting even without an excuse, relying on the practice of Companions and Successors like Anas, Junada, Ibn Sirin, and Mujahid, who prayed sitting on ships despite being able to stand. The author favors Imam Abu Hanifa's view, calling it 'more apparent' (al-azhar), and explains that the hadith commanding standing is taken as recommending (nadb), not obligation, to reconcile the evidences. The passage then discusses different scenarios: a ship tied to the shore but rocking severely is treated like a moving ship; if not severely rocking, it is like a stationary ship. For stationary ships tied to the shore, prayer sitting is invalid by consensus if one can stand, unless part of the ship is stable on the ground, then standing is valid. The chosen view (al-mukhtār) is that if the ship is stably grounded, standing prayer is valid; otherwise, it is like an animal and prayer while standing is not valid. However, some sources like al-Hidaya allow standing unconditionally. The author also addresses facing the qibla on a moving ship: one must face the qibla at the start and turn with the ship if it changes direction; if unable, one must wait until able to complete the prayer facing the qibla. Abandoning qibla entirely invalidates the prayer by consensus.

Key Terms
الإيماء (al-imā'): Nodding or gesturing with the head in place of bowing and prostrating, used when one is unable to perform full movements.
المبيح (al-mubīḥ): That which permits a concession (rukhsa); here it refers to the cause that allows sitting or imā' instead of standing.
كالسائرة (ka-al-sā'ira): Like a moving ship (in legal ruling). A ship anchored but severely rocking is treated as moving.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), which of the following excuses would permit sitting in prayer on a ship?
A) The ship is moving fast.
B) The ship is tied to the shore.
C) The worshipper feels dizzy and may fall.
D) The worshipper prefers to sit for comfort.

Key Takeaway
Prayer posture on a ship involves a legitimate intra-Hanafi dispute: Imam Abu Hanifa permits sitting without excuse, while the Sahibayn require one; the later preferred view is the Imam's, though standing remains better.
